## Assistant (2026-04-25 16:10:12)

I’ll treat this as a coordination/triage pass: first verify the handover against the latest draft, then identify which branches are mathematically live, which are stale, and what the next agent prompts should force.

_Thought for 1m 26s_

## Coordinator verdict

The handover is directionally correct, but I would sharpen it further: **the next wave should be a local falsification sprint**, not a broad seven-agent continuation.

The governing question is now binary:

\[
\boxed{\text{Does the concrete odd-}\eta\eta\text{ top row physically cancel?}}
\]

If the answer is **no**, the current local Bottleneck-C package fails before finite-core, interaction, or global transfer arguments matter. The attached handover and the current draft both identify the same live obstruction:

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0},
\qquad
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7},
\]

with the homogeneous test giving

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}\neq0
\]

on a good patch. 

## What should be treated as closed

Do **not** spend more agent cycles on these unless a convention is challenged:

1. **Gate A**: aggregate-closed under the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention.
2. **\(M_A,M_C\) connection table**: closed under source-grade reflection and corrected mixed-block swap.
3. **Mixed four-point branch**: dependency-closed; it sees \(ev_5-u_5f\), not the independent hidden-state \(f/c\).
4. **Finite odd-germ determinacy**: qualitatively closed, but it does **not** supply calibrated lower bounds.

The handover is right that finite determinacy is not enough; the remaining finite-core issue is sampled vector non-concentration, not another Noetherian/determinacy proof. 

## Main correction to the agent strategy

I would **not** run all agents at equal weight. Use this hierarchy:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Local row sprint first; everything else conditional or low-cadence.}
}
\]

Recommended active allocation now:

\[
\boxed{
3\text{ local/physical agents}
+
2\text{ interaction agents}
+
1\text{ finite-core monitor}
+
0\text{ or }1\text{ theta escape agent}
}
\]

The previous \(2+1+2+2\) allocation is acceptable, but too generous to finite-core work before the local package survives. The finite-core agents can keep working only if their task is narrowly scoped and does not consume coordination bandwidth.

## Immediate local sprint

### Local Agent A — row-cancellation audit

Task:

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\quad\text{versus all other frozen Bottleneck-C rows.}
\]

They must produce a row-signature table with, for each candidate row:

\[
(a,\chi,g,r,b),
\quad
Q\text{-homogeneity},
\quad
\text{source-jet profile},
\quad
\text{matrix support},
\quad
S\text{-coefficient},
\quad
\Phi_K\text{-visibility}.
\]

The key question is not “is the total table complicated?” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{\text{same signature top }\eta\eta} f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}=0?
}
\]

If no row has the same source-jet/Q/signature profile, this agent should state a **row-level no-go**:

\[
f_{A,Y}\neq0
\]

in the good-patch model.

### Local Agent B — actual-source admissibility audit

Task:

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0?
\]

This is the most important independent route. They must determine whether the homogeneous test

\[
r(u)=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0
\]

is actually admissible under the real zeta source model. If it is admissible, then universal cancellation via

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0
\]

is dead.

They must not assume arbitrary scalar jets are allowed. They need to locate the actual definitions of

\[
r_i(u),\quad \eta_i(s),\quad q_0,\quad q_0''
\]

and determine whether affine removal, phase-gap normalization, or corrected source geometry imposes a relation among

\[
q_0,\ q_0'',\ \rho_{i,2},\ \rho_{i,4}.
\]

The formula to test is:

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

### Local Agent C — physical correction/no-go

This is not another \(\Theta_\pm\) coordinate agent. The task is narrower:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is there a physical finite-}s\text{ term already present that cancels the row?}
}
\]

They should inspect whether omitted diagonal, off-diagonal, whitening-bundle, or source-curvature terms can cancel the top row **at the physical \(T\)-readout level**, not merely in a formal normal coordinate.

The \(\Theta_\pm\) route should be presumed no-go unless this agent finds a genuinely physical correction. The handover already records that formal \(\Theta_\pm\) coordinates can hide the residual, but the physical hidden coordinate carries it back as

\[
T^{\phys}=T^\star+\frac{\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}}{c},
\qquad
\partial_\kappa(\beta_{\loc}^{\Theta}/c)\neq0.
\]

So do **not** assign more agents to re-audit \(\Theta_\pm\) as a coordinate package. 

## Decision tree

Use this as the coordinator’s kill/continue logic.

### Case 1 — Local A finds structural cancellation

Then the local package survives provisionally. Next step is to verify both:

\[
Q_{A,Y}=e_{A,Y}v_5-u_5f_{A,Y}=0
\]

and the stronger transform-safe condition

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

Quotient closure alone is insufficient. If

\[
Q_{A,Y}=0,\qquad f_{A,Y}\neq0,
\]

then the quotient closes but the hidden-state \(T\)-coordinate leaks. The handover explicitly identifies this distinction. 

### Case 2 — Local B proves \(\nu_{21,7}=0\)

Then the top row is neutralized by actual-source geometry. The next step is the full finite Bottleneck-C table, but now with source constraints inserted before any symbolic cancellation claim.

### Case 3 — Local A finds no cancellation and Local B finds homogeneous test admissible

Then the current local proof strategy fails.

The conclusion should be stated cleanly:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\text{ is a physical } \Phi_K\text{-visible Bottleneck-C survivor.}
}
\]

At that point, do **not** keep proving downstream finite-core statements as if the local package is intact. Switch to redesign: either find a new physical package mechanism or abandon the current Bottleneck-C route.

### Case 4 — homogeneous test inadmissible, but no identity yet

Then the attack narrows to the exact admissibility constraint. Local B must give the replacement constraint explicitly, and Local A must rerun the row-cancellation table under that constraint.

## Interaction agents: keep, but focus

Interaction work is worth continuing because it may affect finite-core alignment and could reveal structural rigidity useful elsewhere. But it should not distract from the local row.

### Interaction Agent A

Attack feature balance:

\[
\sum_i a_i v_i=0
\]

under

\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]

Ordinary amplitude balance does not imply feature balance. The handover notes that feature balance for every balanced amplitude vector would force

\[
v_1=\cdots=v_k,
\]

so the agent must either prove actual-source constancy/incidence or produce a good-patch countermodel. 

### Interaction Agent B

Attack spectral positivity for

\[
K_{dd}(t;m)
=
t^2\left\langle v(m+t/2),v(m-t/2)\right\rangle.
\]

They must compute or constrain

\[
\kappa_2,\quad \kappa_4,\quad \kappa_6,
\]

especially

\[
\kappa_4
=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right).
\]

If the sign is not forced by actual source geometry, the spectral route is not a proof route.

## Finite-core: reduce to one monitor for now

The finite-core branch should not be abandoned, but it should be lower priority until the local row survives.

Keep one finite-core monitor on the sharp formulation:

\[
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q)
\]

outside

\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

The older distance-to-\(\mathcal Z_k\) formulation is only a geometric proxy. The live branch is the interaction-aligned small-vector branch

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
\]

The finite-core agent should not re-prove finite determinacy or projective detection. Their only useful deliverable is either a pointwise non-concentration theorem or a precise counter-branch showing

\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
\]

far from \(\mathcal Z_k\). 

## Stale items to suppress during attack

Do not let agents spend time on:

1. The old \(a\in\{1,5\}\) shorthand. The active finite Fréchet index includes \(a=2\).
2. Broad “60-row table” rhetoric without isolating the top-row signature.
3. \(\Theta_\pm\) as formal normal coordinates.
4. Mixed four-point routes that do not read \(T=v_7/c\) or \(\Phi_K(A_7)\).
5. Finite determinacy as if it implied calibrated transfer.
6. Pure quotient closure without checking \(f_{A,Y}=0\).

## Bottom line

Set the next attack objective as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove physical cancellation of }
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\text{, or certify it as a good-patch survivor.}
}
\]

That is the gate. Everything else is downstream.

## Coordinator readout

The initial agent wave is strongly negative. Taken at face value, the current Bottleneck-C/local package is no longer merely “open”; it is **failing in a concrete good-patch model** unless one of two premises in the local agents’ reports is false.

The live obstruction remains:

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0},
\qquad
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

Local Agent A reports no structural row cancellation in the frozen Bottleneck-C table and gives a good-patch survivor with

\[
f_{A,Y}
=
\frac{u q_0^3}{5184\pi q^3Q^{14}}
\neq0.
\]

Local Agent B reports that the current source model does not force

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]

and that the homogeneous post-affine source test

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0
\]

is not excluded by the currently stated constraints.  

## The important distinction

Do **not** yet write “proof strategy dead” as a final mathematical conclusion. The right conclusion is sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The local package fails unless the homogeneous good-patch model is inadmissible or the frozen row table is incomplete.}
}
\]

Those are now the only two serious escape routes.

Everything else looks secondary:

1. **No aggregate row cancellation found.**
2. **No source-jet identity found.**
3. **No \(\Theta_\pm\) / counterterm physical repair found.**
4. **Finite-core remains dependent on a pointwise small-value avoidance theorem.**
5. **Interaction remains dependent on a feature-balance/spectral-rigidity theorem.**

The \(\Theta\) result is especially constraining: any correction that cancels a physical \(S\)-component is itself \(\Phi_K\)-visible, because the physical readout is

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]

So formal normal-form counterterms just move the obstruction into \(T^{\mathrm{phys}}\); they do not close Bottleneck C. 

## What I would do next

Stop broad agent work. Run a **two-premise audit** before assigning more attacks.

### Audit 1 — actual-source admissibility

Question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }r(u)=u^2,\ q_0''=0\text{ genuinely admissible in the actual zeta source class?}
}
\]

Local Agent B says yes under the currently stated constraints, but this must be verified directly from the latest draft’s definitions, not inferred from absence of an exclusion. If the actual source class secretly imposes a differential relation among

\[
q_0,\quad q_0'',\quad \rho_{i,2},\quad \rho_{i,4},
\]

then the homogeneous model may be a false countermodel.

But the required locking law is extremely specific:

\[
\frac{\rho_{i,4}}{\rho_{i,2}}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

Unless the paper already derives something of this form from the zeta source geometry, the source-identity route is effectively dead. 

### Audit 2 — frozen table completeness

Question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is }\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}\text{ truly isolated at }(a,r,g,b)=(2,0,7,0)?
}
\]

Local Agent A’s no-go depends on the assertion that the only relevant zeroth source primitive is

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}\propto E_{22},
\]

and that no other active row with the same \(\eta_i\eta_j\), \(Q\)-homogeneity, matrix support, and \(S\)-readout exists. 

This needs one direct verification against the actual primitive coefficient table in the draft.

If both audits confirm the agents’ assumptions, then the local package should be marked failed.

## Direction for agents now

### Keep active: 2 local auditors only

Assign two agents, not seven.

#### Local Audit Agent 1 — admissibility

Prompt:

```text
Work only from the latest draft.

Audit whether the homogeneous post-affine source model
\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,\qquad q_0\neq0
\]
is admissible under the actual zeta source definitions.

Do not infer admissibility from absence of a prohibition. Locate the definitions of the actual source variables and determine whether they impose any relation among
\[
q_0,\ q_0'',\ \rho_{i,2},\ \rho_{i,4}.
\]

Deliverable:
Either prove the homogeneous good-patch model is admissible, or identify the exact draft-defined constraint excluding it.
```

#### Local Audit Agent 2 — row-table completeness

Prompt:

```text
Work only from the latest draft.

Audit whether the frozen Bottleneck-C row table is complete at the signature
\[
\eta_i\eta_j,\quad [z^7],\quad (a,r,g,b)=(2,0,7,0).
\]

Verify whether any other physical frozen row has the same source-jet profile, same \(Q\)-homogeneity, compatible matrix support, and opposite \(S\)-coefficient.

Do not count formal counterterms, \(\Theta_\pm\) coordinate rewrites, or later source-motion \([z^7\delta^1]\) layers.

Deliverable:
Either confirm row isolation, or give the missing row and exact cancellation identity.
```

### Pause theta

Theta should be paused. The escape hatch returned a structural no-go: no genuinely physical finite-\(s\) correction was visible, and counterterms are not \(\Phi_K\)-invisible. 

### Put finite-core on standby

Finite-Core A and B are useful, but downstream. Their reports agree on the real dependency:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Finite-Core A correctly says this is a pointwise analytic small-value avoidance theorem, not a consequence of finite determinacy, spacing, compactness, or sublevel-volume estimates. Finite-Core B correctly reframes alignment as the mechanism by which samples enter a near-\(\mathcal Z_k\) tube, not as a separate far-from-zero branch.  

This matters later, but it cannot rescue the local Bottleneck-C failure.

### Keep one interaction agent only

The interaction reports are also negative. Feature balance for all balanced amplitudes is equivalent to

\[
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k),
\]

which is far stronger than amplitude balance. The spectral route also has independent Taylor obstructions: even under unit normalization, the \(t^6\) coefficient requires a higher-jet sign condition

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\le0
\]

in the negative-type convention.  

Keep at most one interaction agent to derive the actual transported feature \(v(u)\) from the draft and test this sign condition. But this is not the critical path until the local audits resolve.

## My current best assessment

If the two local audits confirm the agents’ assumptions, then the current proof architecture has a **hard local obstruction**:

\[
\boxed{
f_{A,Y}\neq0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\partial_\kappa T\neq0.
}
\]

That means Bottleneck C does not close physically. The paper should then stop treating the local package as provisionally successful and instead record the obstruction as a no-go theorem.

The next mathematical move is therefore not “more coefficient hunting.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Certify or invalidate the homogeneous good-patch countermodel.}
}
\]

That is the decisive fork.

Below are six audit prompts, scoped so each agent returns a falsifiable result rather than more broad exploration.

## 1. Local Agent A — actual-source admissibility audit

```text
You are Local Agent A. Work only from the latest draft and the current handover.

Audit whether the homogeneous post-affine source model
\[
r_i(u)=r_j(u)=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,\qquad q_0\neq0
\]
is genuinely admissible in the actual zeta source class.

Context:
The current local obstruction is
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0},
\qquad
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]
The claimed countermodel uses
\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}\neq0.
\]

Tasks:
1. Locate the draft definitions of the actual source variables:
\[
r_i(u),\quad \eta_i(s),\quad q_0,\quad q_0'',\quad \rho_{i,2},\quad \rho_{i,4}.
\]
2. Determine whether affine removal, endpoint normalization, same-scale normalization, phase-gap geometry, or source-grade parity imposes any relation among
\[
q_0,\ q_0'',\ \rho_{i,2},\ \rho_{i,4}.
\]
3. Specifically test whether the draft forces the locking law
\[
\frac{\rho_{i,4}}{\rho_{i,2}}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]
4. Decide whether
\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\quad q_0''=0
\]
is admissible or excluded.
5. If excluded, identify the exact draft-defined constraint excluding it.
6. If admissible, state the local consequence:
\[
\nu_{21,7}\neq0
\]
on a good phase patch.

Deliverable:
A definitive admissibility verdict: either the homogeneous good-patch model is admissible and kills the universal \(\nu_{21,7}=0\) route, or it is inadmissible and the exact excluding condition is stated.
```

---

## 2. Local Agent B — frozen Bottleneck-C row-table completeness audit

```text
You are Local Agent B. Work only from the latest draft and the current handover.

Audit whether the frozen Bottleneck-C table is complete around the row
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]

Context:
The alleged survivor has source signature
\[
\eta_i\eta_j,\qquad [z^7],\qquad (a,r,g,b)=(2,0,7,0),
\]
and coefficient
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Reconstruct the active frozen Bottleneck-C coefficient:
\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_g
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]
2. List every row with the same ordinary order and potential \(S\)-visibility as
\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
\]
3. For each candidate row, record:
\[
(a,\chi,g,r,b),
\quad
\text{source monomial},
\quad
Q\text{-homogeneity},
\quad
\text{left primitive},
\quad
\text{right whitening slot},
\quad
S\text{-coefficient}.
\]
4. Check whether any row has the same \(\eta_i\eta_j\) source profile and an opposite forced \(S\)-coefficient.
5. Do not count:
   - formal \(\Theta_\pm\) counterterms;
   - quotient-line cancellations with \(f\neq0\);
   - later source-motion \([z^7\delta^1]\) terms;
   - accidental parameter cancellations.
6. If a cancellation exists, give the exact row identity.
7. If none exists, state the row-isolation theorem.

Deliverable:
Either a concrete missing frozen row with exact cancellation identity, or a verified row-level no-go:
\[
f_{A,Y}\neq0
\]
in the good-patch model.
```

## 3. Finite-Core Agent A — pointwise small-value avoidance audit

```text
You are Finite-Core Agent A. Work only from the latest draft and the current handover.

Audit the exact missing finite-core theorem:
\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Context:
Finite determinacy is already accepted qualitatively. Do not re-prove it. The live issue is pointwise sampled non-concentration for actual zeta finite-core samples.

Tasks:
1. Reconstruct the definitions of
\[
C_{\rm fd},\quad P_{\rm fd},\quad J_{\rm fd},\quad F_N(\theta,Q),\quad \Lambda(m,Q).
\]
2. Identify exactly which currently proved draft results imply:
   - compactness;
   - finite determinacy;
   - projective detection;
   - zero-spacing or endpoint-gap control;
   - Łojasiewicz/sublevel estimates.
3. For each such result, decide whether it proves pointwise exclusion of
\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]
4. Do not accept density-zero, small-volume, or genericity arguments unless they imply an actual zero-count exclusion at the calibrated scale.
5. Try to construct a formal good-patch model with
\[
J_{\rm fd}\approx -P_{\rm fd}
\]
while avoiding
\[
\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
6. If such a model is allowed by current controls, state the exact missing arithmetic/source-geometry theorem.
7. If impossible, prove the actual pointwise anti-alignment theorem.

Deliverable:
Either a proof of sampled vector non-concentration, or a theorem-ready statement of the unresolved bad branch
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
\]
```

---

## 4. Finite-Core Agent B — geometric tube calibration and alignment-containment audit

```text
You are Finite-Core Agent B. Work only from the latest draft and the current handover.

Audit the relationship between the coefficient-small branch
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}
\]
and the geometric near-zero branch
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm geom}.
\]

Context:
The current claim is that small
\[
\|P_{\rm fd}+J_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
=
\|C_{\rm fd}\|_\infty
\]
forces proximity to
\[
\mathcal Z_k
\]
by Łojasiewicz, but does not force controlled incidence.

Tasks:
1. Reconstruct the exact definition of
\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta:H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0\}
\]
and verify whether the finite coefficient vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}
=
(c_{\core,1},c_{\core,3},\ldots,c_{\core,2R_{\Theta_k}+1})
\]
cuts it out on the relevant compact nonsingular stratum.
2. Establish the precise Łojasiewicz estimate:
\[
\|C_{\rm fd}(\theta)\|_\infty
\ge
C_{\Theta_k}
\operatorname{dist}(\theta,\mathcal Z_k)^{\mu_{\Theta_k}}.
\]
3. Compute the induced geometric radius
\[
D_{\Theta_k}^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left(
\frac{\Lambda(m,Q)}{C_{\Theta_k}}
\right)^{1/\mu_{\Theta_k}}.
\]
4. Determine whether the draft’s existing definition of
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm geom}
\]
uses a radius at least this large.
5. Decide whether
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}
\subseteq
\mathcal N_k^{\rm geom}
\]
is actually proved with the draft’s constants and exponents.
6. Then audit whether proximity to \(\mathcal Z_k\) implies membership in
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
7. If not, identify the remaining theorem needed to prove
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}=\varnothing.
\]

Deliverable:
A precise containment/calibration theorem, or a corrected statement showing where the geometric tube formulation is too weak.
```

---

## 5. Interaction Agent A — actual feature-balance audit

```text
You are Interaction Agent A. Work only from the latest draft and the current handover.

Audit whether the actual \(dd\)-interaction feature satisfies feature balance.

Context:
The live \(dd\)-interaction kernel is
\[
K_{ij}^{dd}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2\langle v_i,v_j\rangle,
\qquad
v_i=v(u_i).
\]
Feature balance would require
\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\]
for every balanced amplitude vector
\[
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]

Tasks:
1. Locate the draft definition of the transported transverse \(dd\)-feature
\[
v(u).
\]
2. Verify the algebraic equivalence:
\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\text{ for all }a\in\mathbf 1^\perp
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k).
\]
3. Determine whether actual same-scale source geometry forces
\[
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k)
\]
on every admissible finite core.
4. If not, test whether failure of feature balance is contained in the controlled incidence set:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]
5. Specifically check whether nonconstant \(v(u)\), or finite differences such as
\[
v(-1)-2v(0)+v(1),
\]
force one of:
\[
M=0,\ W=0,\ K_v=0,\ T_v=0,
\]
collision, endpoint-gap failure, patch-boundary, amplitude drop, whitening singularity, \(c=0\), \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}=0\), or hidden-rank jump.
6. If no containment holds, construct a draft-compatible good-patch model with balanced amplitudes but failed feature balance.

Deliverable:
Feature-balance theorem, incidence-containment theorem, or an independent \(dd\)-feature obstruction.
```


## Coordinator verdict

The six-agent audit converged. The current architecture now has a **formal local-source countermodel** and no compensating cancellation in the frozen Bottleneck-C table.

The strongest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current Bottleneck-C local package fails in the stated formal source category.}
}
\]

The slightly weaker but more precise version is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{It is not yet a certified literal zeta-source counterexample, because actual zeta-source realization was not proved.}
}
\]

That distinction matters. The formal package is broken as written; the only remaining rescue is an **actual zeta-source restriction** not currently in the draft.

---

## 1. Local branch: decisive negative result

Local Agent A found that

\[
r_i(u)=r_j(u)=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,\qquad q_0\neq0
\]

is admissible under the draft’s **formal corrected-source category after affine removal**. Affine removal only imposes

\[
r_\rho(m)=0,\qquad r_\rho'(m)=0,
\]

and does not impose any relation between the second and fourth source jets. Under this model,

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}\neq0,
\]

hence

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
\frac{u q_0^3}{5184\pi q^3Q^{14}}\neq0.
\]

The caveat is that the agent did **not** prove this germ is literally realized by an exterior zeta zero pair; it only proves the current formal source axioms do not exclude it. 

Local Agent B then found that the row

\[
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\]

is isolated in the frozen table. Since \(g=7\), the relation

\[
r+b=7-g
\]

forces

\[
r=b=0,
\]

so there are no convolutional \(\Lambda^-_{a,r}\) or \(W_{+,b}\) partner rows at the same top order. No physical frozen row with the same \(\eta_i\eta_j\) profile, same \(Q\)-homogeneity, and opposite forced \(S\)-coefficient was found. 

So the local result is:

\[
\boxed{
f_{A,Y}\neq0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f_{A,Y}/c\neq0.
}
\]

This is not a quotient-only issue. It is a physical \(T\)-horizontal failure.

---

## 2. What can still rescue the local branch?

Only one serious route remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove an actual zeta-source realization constraint excluding }r=u^2.
}
\]

The needed theorem is not mild. It must imply something like

\[
\frac{\rho_{i,4}}{\rho_{i,2}}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0},
\]

or an equivalent pairwise identity forcing

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0.
\]

Without such a theorem, the local package should be marked **failed**, not merely incomplete.

I would now stop asking agents to search for row cancellations or \(\Theta_\pm\) repairs. Those routes are exhausted at the current level.

---

## 3. Finite-core branch: still unresolved, but downstream

Finite-Core Agent A confirmed that the required theorem is still missing:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Compactness, finite determinacy, projective detection, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap control, and Łojasiewicz/Remez estimates do not give pointwise exclusion of the bad tube. The live branch remains

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q).
\]

Finite-Core Agent B clarified the geometry: the aligned branch is contained in the geometric near-zero branch if the tube radius is calibrated as

\[
D_{\Theta_k}^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left(\frac{\Lambda(m,Q)}{C_{\Theta_k}}\right)^{1/\mu_{\Theta_k}}.
\]

But this only says alignment brings the sample near \(\mathcal Z_k\). It does **not** prove controlled incidence or eliminate the branch. The missing statement remains

\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]

Finite-core is therefore a genuine later dependency, but it cannot rescue the local failure.

---

## 4. Interaction branch: also negative

Interaction Agent A confirmed that feature balance is not available. For every balanced amplitude vector,

\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\]

is equivalent to

\[
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k).
\]

The current same-scale and incidence hypotheses do not force this. The countermodel

\[
v(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w,\qquad u=(-1,0,1),\qquad a=(1,-2,1)
\]

has balanced amplitudes but

\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

So the \(dd\)-feature branch remains live. 

Interaction Agent B confirmed that spectral positivity is not proved. Unit normalization gives the correct \(\kappa_4\) sign, but leaves

\[
\kappa_6
=
-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

The required negative-type sign is

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\le0,
\]

and the draft does not prove it. A unit feature curve

\[
v(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

can violate the required \(t^6\)-sign when

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}.
\]

So interaction remains a separate obstruction, but again: it is downstream of the local failure.

---

I would not run another broad six-agent round. The next attack should be concentrated on one question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual zeta source class satisfy a hidden jet-locking law?}
}
\]

Specifically, we need to derive \(r_\rho\) from the actual exterior zero-pair phase contribution \(f_\rho\), expand it at the midpoint, and compute whether \(\rho_4/\rho_2\) is free or locked.

The next agent wave should be only **three agents**:

Derive \(f_\rho(t)\), subtract the midpoint affine jet, compute

=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}
\]

can ever be forced.

### Agent Z2 — realization/freedom theorem

\[

\]

has enough local freedom to approximate the \(r=u^2,\ q_0''=0\) model. If yes, the obstruction is not merely formal; it is source-realization compatible.

### Agent Z3 — package redesign/no-go

Assume the local obstruction survives. Determine whether any new physical package can make Bottleneck C close without requiring

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

If not, formalize the local no-go theorem and stop treating the current route as viable.

# Zeta-agent shared background

We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft and recent multi-agent audits. The project is currently in **attack mode**, not paper-polish mode. Do not propose cosmetic LaTeX edits. Produce derivations, countermodels, explicit source formulas, or theorem-ready no-go statements.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual zeta source class impose a hidden jet-locking law excluding the formal countermodel?}
}
\]

If no, then the current local Bottleneck-C strategy fails.

---

# 1. Current global status

## 1.1 Gate A is closed

Do not reopen Gate A. It is accepted as aggregate-closed under the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention.

The earlier leading homogeneous cubic non-\((1,1)\) sector is no longer a live obstruction. Prior apparent terms such as

\[
L_2N_0R_1+L_1N_0R_2
\]

and

\[

\]

are treated as aggregate fixed-sector cancellations, not termwise vanishing.

## 1.2 \(M_A,M_C\) connection table is closed

The connection-table branch is conditionally closed under source-grade reflection and the corrected mixed-block swap identity. Do not spend time there unless attacking the convention itself.

## 1.3 Mixed four-point branch is closed as a dependency

The mixed four-point scalar exit sees

\[
ev_5-u_5f,
\]

whereas the physical hidden-state/\(\Phi_K\)-visible effect is

\[
\frac{f}{c}.
\]

Thus a quotient-line cancellation does not imply physical \(T\)-horizontal closure. Do not use mixed four-point invisibility to excuse a nonzero \(S\)-coefficient.

## 1.4 Finite-core and interaction branches remain open but downstream

Finite-core still needs pointwise sampled non-concentration:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))+J_{\rm fd}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda(m,Q).
\]

Current audits found no such theorem in the draft. Compactness, finite determinacy, projective detection, zero-spacing, endpoint-gap control, and Łojasiewicz/Remez estimates do not imply pointwise exclusion of the aligned small-value tube. 

The coefficient-small finite-core branch lies inside a geometric near-zero tube if the radius is calibrated by

\[
D_{\Theta_k}^{\rm align}(m,Q)
=
\left(
\frac{\Lambda(m,Q)}{C_{\Theta_k}}
\right)^{1/\mu_{\Theta_k}},
\]

but this does not prove controlled incidence or eliminate the branch. 

The \(dd\)-interaction branch also remains open. Feature balance would force

\[
v(u_1)=\cdots=v(u_k),
\]

which is not implied by the current source geometry.  Spectral positivity is also unproved: unit normalization controls the \(\kappa_4\)-sign but leaves the \(t^6\) condition

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\le0
\]

unproved. 

These branches matter later, but they do not rescue the current local failure.

---

# 2. The current decisive local obstruction

The active local Bottleneck-C row is

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}.
}
\]

It is a frozen Bottleneck-C row, not a later source-motion row.

The relevant coefficient is

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
\tau_{h\to m}\pi_{\mathfrak f_h}
\operatorname{Sym}
\sum_{\chi\in\{dd,d\eta+\eta d,\eta\eta\}}
\sum_g
\sum_{r+b=7-g}
H^A_{r,0}Y^\chi_{g,0}W_{+,b}.
\]

At the target row,

\[
\chi=\eta\eta,\qquad g=7,\qquad r=0,\qquad b=0,\qquad a=2.
\]

Because

\[
r+b=7-g,
\]

at \(g=7\) we necessarily have

\[
r=b=0.
\]

So this is a genuine top row. There are no convolutional partition partners from \(r>0\) or \(b>0\).

The finite Fréchet primitive is

\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22}.
\]

The row is driven by the odd scalar \(\eta\eta\) term

\[
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
J\eta_i\eta_j
\right]_7.
\]

Define

\[
\nu_{21,7}
:=
[z^7]
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right].
\]

On a diagonal leading right-whitening patch

\[
W_{+,0}=\operatorname{diag}(u,v),
\]

the \(S\)-coefficient is

\[
\boxed{
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}.
}
\]

Thus the physical hidden-state variation is

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}}{c}.
\]

So \(f\neq0\) is a physical Bottleneck-C failure.

---

# 3. What the local audits established

## 3.1 The row is isolated in the frozen table

Local Agent B audited the frozen Bottleneck-C table and found no missing physical frozen row with the same source profile, \(Q\)-homogeneity, and opposite forced \(S\)-coefficient. At \(g=7\), \(r=b=0\), so the row has no partition partner; \(dd\) and \(d\eta+\eta d\) rows have different source monomials; \(\Theta_\pm\) counterterms and later \([z^7\delta^1]\) source-motion layers do not count. 

The resulting row-isolation theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\text{ has no structural frozen-row cancellation partner.}
}
\]

Therefore the only ways to kill the row are:

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0
\]

by actual source geometry, or a genuinely new physical correction not presently in the frozen table.

## 3.2 The homogeneous formal source model is admissible under current package axioms

Local Agent A audited the source definitions. The draft defines a one-pair perturbation by taking a one-pair phase-derivative contribution \(f_\rho(t)\) and subtracting its midpoint affine jet:

\[
r_\rho(t)=f_\rho(t)-f_\rho(m)-f_\rho'(m)(t-m).
\]

It then defines

\[
d_\pm(z)=r_\rho(t_\pm),
\qquad
e_\pm(z)=r_\rho'(t_\pm),
\qquad
g_\pm(z)=r_\rho''(t_\pm),
\]

and the phase-gap source variable

\[
\eta(z)=\int_{t_+}^{t_-}r_\rho(u)\,du.
\]

The resulting kernels have the parity/scale structure

\[
d_\pm(z)=\frac{z^2}{Q^4}U_\pm(z),
\quad
e_\pm(z)=\frac{z}{Q^2}E_\pm(z),
\quad
g_\pm(z)=G_\pm(z),
\quad
\eta(z)=\frac{z^3}{Q^6}V(z).
\]

This means affine removal imposes only

\[
r_\rho(m)=0,
\qquad
r_\rho'(m)=0,
\]

and does not impose a relation between \(r_\rho^{(2)}(m)\) and \(r_\rho^{(4)}(m)\). 

Thus the formal homogeneous source

\[
r(u)=u^2
\]

respects the stated source constraints:

\[
r(0)=0,\qquad r'(0)=0.
\]

Its phase-gap integral is

\[
\eta(s)=\int_{-s/2}^{s/2}u^2\,du=\frac{s^3}{12}.
\]

In the notation

\[
r(u)=\rho_2u^2+\rho_4u^4+\cdots,
\]

this gives

\[
\rho_2=1,
\qquad
\rho_4=0.
\]

The audit concluded:

\[
\boxed{
r_i=r_j=u^2,\quad q_0''=0,\quad q_0\neq0
\text{ is admissible under the draft’s formal local source constraints.}
}
\]

But it is **not yet proved** to be literally realized by an actual exterior zeta zero pair. This distinction is now the entire point of the Zeta agents. 

---

# 4. The formal countermodel

In the favorable phase-gap integral model, the coefficient is

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right].
\]

For

\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

we have

\[
\rho_{i,2}=\rho_{j,2}=1,
\qquad
\rho_{i,4}=\rho_{j,4}=0,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}
=
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}.
}
\]

On a good phase patch,

\[
q_0\neq0,
\]

hence

\[
\nu_{21,7}\neq0.
\]

Therefore

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}
=
\frac{u q_0^3}{5184\pi q^3Q^{14}}.
\]

On a good patch with

\[
u q_0 q\neq0,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}\neq0.
}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}}{c}
\neq0.
}
\]

On a generic \(u_5\neq0\) quotient patch, the quotient determinant also fails:

\[
Q_{A,Y}
=
-u_5f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm top}
\neq0.
\]

But the primary failure is \(T\)-horizontal, not merely quotient-level.

---

# 5. The exact locking law needed to rescue the local branch

The only known source-identity route would require

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0.
\]

Assuming

\[
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}\neq0,
\]

set

\[
\lambda_i=\frac{\rho_{i,4}}{\rho_{i,2}},
\qquad
\lambda_j=\frac{\rho_{j,4}}{\rho_{j,2}}.
\]

Then \(\nu_{21,7}=0\) requires

\[
\frac{q_0}{480}(\lambda_i+\lambda_j)
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
=0.
\]

For this to hold uniformly for all active source directions, one needs a jet-locking law of the form

\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_{i,4}}{\rho_{i,2}}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
}
\]

The formal homogeneous model has

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}=0,
\qquad
q_0''=0.
\]

The locking law would then demand

\[
0=\frac{10q_0^2}{9},
\]

which contradicts the good-patch condition \(q_0\neq0\).

So the Zeta agents must decide whether the actual zeta source class really satisfies such a constraint, or whether the local formal countermodel reflects genuine source freedom.

---

# 6. What not to do

Do not:

1. Reopen Gate A.
2. Search for more \(dd\), \(d\eta\), or \(\eta\eta\) frozen-row cancellations unless you find an explicitly missing row from the actual draft.
3. Use \(\Theta_\pm\) formal normal coordinates as a rescue. That path only hides the \(S\)-visible residual and reintroduces it through \(T^{\rm phys}\).
4. Use quotient cancellation \(ev_5-u_5f=0\) as a substitute for \(f=0\).
5. Treat finite-core lower transfer as relevant until the local Bottleneck-C obstruction is resolved.
6. Prove genericity, density-zero, or small-volume claims. The local question is pointwise.

The target is actual-source realization/rigidity, not package bookkeeping.

---

# 7. Core mission for the Zeta agents

The Zeta agents must determine whether the formal local source countermodel is actually compatible with zeta-side source geometry.

There are two possible outcomes.

## Outcome A — actual zeta source rigidity exists

If actual zeta exterior-pair sources satisfy a hidden relation forcing

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]

or at least excluding

\[
r=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,\qquad q_0\neq0,
\]

then the local package may survive, but the draft needs a new theorem proving that actual-source rigidity.

## Outcome B — actual zeta source freedom exists

If the exterior zero-pair source map can realize or approximate the formal germ

\[
r=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

or if it leaves \(\rho_4/\rho_2\) free enough to violate the locking law, then the current local Bottleneck-C package fails.

In that case the proof should stop treating the package as viable and record a local no-go theorem.

---

# 8. Agent-specific responsibilities

## Zeta Agent 1 — actual exterior-pair source expansion

Your job is to derive the actual source jets.

Work from the draft’s definition of the exterior one-pair phase-derivative contribution \(f_\rho(t)\). Expand at the midpoint \(m\). Then subtract the affine jet:

\[
r_\rho(t)
=
f_\rho(t)-f_\rho(m)-f_\rho'(m)(t-m).
\]

Compute:

\[
r_\rho^{(2)}(m),
\qquad
r_\rho^{(4)}(m).
\]

Translate them into:

\[
\rho_2,
\qquad
\rho_4.
\]

Then determine whether the actual formula imposes

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.

## Zeta Agent 2 — source-realization/freedom theorem

Your job is to decide whether the formal countermodel is source-realization compatible.

Study the map from exterior zero-pair parameters to post-affine jets:

\[
\text{exterior zero-pair parameters}
\longmapsto

\]

## Zeta Agent 3 — local no-go/package redesign fork

Assume the local obstruction survives unless Zeta Agents 1–2 prove actual-source locking.

Your job is to determine whether any physical package redesign can close Bottleneck C without requiring

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

You must respect:

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]

Therefore any physical correction that cancels an \(S\)-visible row must itself be \(S\)-visible. It cannot be \(\Phi_K\)-invisible unless its \(S\)-component is zero.

Deliverable:

\[
\boxed{
\text{new physical mechanism closing Bottleneck C despite the surviving row,}
}
\]

\[

}

# 9. Recommended exact prompt for Zeta Agent 1

```text
You are Zeta Agent 1. Work only from the latest draft and the shared Zeta-agent background.

Your task is to audit actual exterior-pair source jets.

The current local formal countermodel uses
\[
r_i=r_j=u^2,\qquad q_0''=0,\qquad q_0\neq0,
\]
which gives
\[
\nu_{21,7}=-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}}\neq0.
\]
This model is admissible under the formal post-affine source category, but it is not yet proved to be literally realized by an actual exterior zeta zero pair.

Locate the draft definition of the one-pair phase-derivative contribution \(f_\rho(t)\). Define
\[
r_\rho(t)=f_\rho(t)-f_\rho(m)-f_\rho'(m)(t-m).
\]
Compute
\[
r_\rho^{(2)}(m),\qquad r_\rho^{(4)}(m),
\]
and express the corresponding
\[
\rho_2,\qquad \rho_4,\qquad \rho_4/\rho_2.
\]

Then test whether the actual formula forces
\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

Deliverable:

```

# 12. Tactical bottom line

The Zeta agents are not trying to improve the paper prose. They are deciding whether the current proof architecture survives.

The fork is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta source locking}
}
\]

versus

\[
\boxed{
\text{local Bottleneck-C no-go.}
}
\]

The decisive calculation is the actual zeta-side relation, if any, among

\[
q_0,\quad q_0'',\quad \rho_2,\quad \rho_4.
\]

If that relation does not force

\[
\nu_{21,7}=0,
\]

then the current local package is not viable.

_Thought for 8s_

## Coordinator verdict

The Zeta-agent round closes the main local escape route. The current Bottleneck-C package should now be marked **locally failed**, modulo one remaining, much stronger possibility:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a global aggregate identity over the actual zeta zero set.}
}
\]

The weaker rescue—“actual one-pair zeta sources secretly satisfy the needed jet-locking law”—appears dead.

---

## 1. Zeta A: no one-pair jet-locking law

Zeta A derived the actual one-pair phase-derivative contribution:

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

After setting

\[
a=1-\beta,\qquad b=\beta,\qquad x=2m-\gamma,\qquad u=t-m,
\]

and subtracting the midpoint affine jet, the post-affine coefficients are:

\[
\rho_2
=
4a\frac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
4b\frac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3},
\]

\[
\rho_4
=
16a\frac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
16b\frac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}.
\]

Thus

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}=R(\beta,x),
\]

a nonconstant rational function of the exterior-pair parameters. It is not forced to equal

\[
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

So the required Bottleneck-C jet-locking identity is **not intrinsic to a single actual zeta pair**. 

---

## 2. Zeta B: the formal \(r=u^2\) model is source-compatible by approximation

Zeta B pushed further: in the far exterior-pair regime,

\[
|x|\to\infty,
\]

one has

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

Therefore, after normalizing \(\rho_2=1\), actual exterior-pair sources approximate

\[
r(u)=u^2
\]

to finite jet order. This remains true even on the critical-line subfamily \(\beta=1/2\). Hence the obstruction is not merely caused by allowing arbitrary formal post-affine sources. It is compatible with actual one-pair zeta source shapes. 

For a good patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

the obstruction coefficient tends to

\[
\nu_{21,7}
\to
-\frac{q_0^3}{216Q^{14}},
\]

so the local obstruction survives the actual-source approximation. 

---

## 3. Zeta C: no package redesign avoids \(f_{A,Y}=0\)

Zeta C formalized the package no-go.

On the fixed-sector patch,

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}}
=
e_{A,Y}I+f_{A,Y}S,
\]

and

\[
\Phi_K(I)=0,\qquad \Phi_K(S)=2.
\]

Therefore

\[
\Phi_K(E_{A,Y}^{\mathrm{BC}})=2f_{A,Y},
\]

and the physical hidden-state slope is

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
-a_1^2\frac{f_{A,Y}}{c}.
\]

So any transform-faithful Bottleneck-C package that diagonally merges on the exceptional divisor must satisfy

\[
f_{A,Y}=0.
\]

Quotient closure,

\[
e v_5-u_5f=0,
\]

does not suffice. Formal \(\Theta_\pm\) coordinates and septic counterterms merely move the \(S\)-visible residual into \(T^{\rm phys}\). They do not remove the physical obstruction. 

---

## 4. Updated proof-state

The local situation is now:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal E^{2}_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}
\text{ is isolated in the frozen table.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual one-pair zeta sources do not satisfy the needed jet-locking law.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual exterior-pair sources approximate the formal bad germ }r=u^2.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{No transform-faithful package redesign closes Bottleneck C unless }f_{A,Y}=0.
}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current local Bottleneck-C strategy is nonviable unless a global aggregate zero-set identity cancels the obstruction.}
}
\]

This is now a much stronger failure mode than “missing local calculation.”

---

## 5. Remaining possible rescue

The only remaining mathematical rescue is not local. It would have to be a theorem of the form:

\[
\sum_{\rho_i,\rho_j \text{ actual exterior sources}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{480}
(\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,4}+\rho_{i,4}\rho_{j,2})
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}\rho_{j,2}
\right]
=0
\]

or an equivalent full aggregate cancellation of the physical \(S\)-coefficient.

That is a **global zeta-tail identity**, not a package identity, not a one-pair source identity, and not a formal coordinate repair.

---

}
\]

If that aggregate identity is not available, the current RH proof route should be marked failed at the local Bottleneck-C stage.

## 1. Exact aggregate obstruction

Zeta Global A gives the actual aggregate source moments:

\[
A_2=\sum_{\alpha}w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,2},
\qquad
A_4=\sum_{\alpha}w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,4}.
\]

The aggregate coefficient is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
}
\]

Equivalently, in derivative-moment form, if

\[
F_{\rm ext}(t)=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha f_\alpha(t),
\]

then

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}{2},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Thus the required global identity is:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0.
}
\]

If \(A_2\neq0\), this becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
}
\]

Zeta Global A also checked that symmetrization, functional-equation pairing, conjugation, and amplitude normalization do not alter the vanishing condition. 

---

## 2. Aggregate cancellation is not structurally forced

Zeta Global B tested the only plausible remaining rescue. The result is negative.

For far exterior source atoms,

\[
\rho_2>0,
\qquad
\rho_4>0,
\qquad
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

Taking far exterior atoms with positive natural weights gives

\[
A_2>0,
\qquad
\frac{A_4}{A_2}\approx0.
\]

On a good patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,
\qquad
q_0''=0,
\]

the required cancellation would demand

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9},
\]

which is not compatible with the far-tail model. Therefore

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}\neq0
\]

in the adversarial finite-tail model. 

This does not prove that the actual infinite zeta tail never cancels. But it proves a crucial negative:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cancellation is not a consequence of local source geometry, zeta symmetries, or pair-level structure.}
}
\]

The only remaining rescue is a **new pointwise global identity over the full exterior zero set**.

---

## 3. Decision theorem now stands

Zeta No-Go C gives the correct theorem-level statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{physical Bottleneck-C closure}
\iff
f_{A,Y}^{\rm agg}=0
\iff
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
}
\]

Because

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c,
\]

a nonzero aggregate \(S\)-coefficient is a physical \(T\)-horizontal failure. Quotient closure is irrelevant unless it also gives \(f=0\). Formal \(\Theta_\pm\) packages and counterterms merely move the obstruction into the physical hidden coordinate. 

So the clean ledger entry is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.86\linewidth}
Under the current Bottleneck-C architecture, local closure is equivalent to the full aggregate identity
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
\]
The formal source category does not force this, actual one-pair source rigidity does not force this, and local source symmetries do not force this. Therefore the proof requires a new global zeta-tail cancellation theorem. Absent that theorem, the Bottleneck-C route fails.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

```text id="global-identity-attack"
A_2^2
\right],

A_2=\sum_\alpha w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,2},
\qquad

5. No transform-faithful package redesign can replace this identity.
6. Finite-tail adversarial models can violate the identity.
Therefore the only remaining possible rescue is that the **full actual exterior zeta tail**, as a global object, satisfies this identity pointwise on every good patch.

Your task:
Attack this exact global identity.

Do not discuss package redesign, \(\Theta_\pm\), quotient closure, finite-core, or interaction branches. Do not give genericity or density arguments. This is a pointwise identity question.

Steps:

1. Reconstruct the actual global exterior-tail object.
   Identify precisely what \(F_{\rm ext}(t)\), \(q(t)\), \(q_0=q(m)\), and \(q_0''=q''(m)\) are in the draft.
   Determine whether \(F_{\rm ext}\) is:
   - the full omitted-zero phase derivative tail,
   - the same object as \(q(t)\),
   - a complementary part of \(q(t)\),
   - or a cutoff/truncated/windowed tail distinct from \(q(t)\).

2. Express \(A_2,A_4\) in terms of derivatives of the actual global object:
   \[
   A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,\qquad
   A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
   \]
   Verify whether weights, cutoffs, self-pair terms, symmetrization, or normalization introduce correction terms.

3. Rewrite the required identity entirely in derivative notation:
   \[
   q_0 F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)
   +
   20\left(
   \frac{q_0''}{6}
   -
   \frac{2q_0^3}{3}
   \right)
   F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2
   =0
   \]
   up to the exact constant normalization. Check constants carefully.
   If \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), reduce to
   \[
   \frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
   =
   \frac{40q_0^2}{3}
   -
   \frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
   \]

4. Test whether this is a known or derivable differential identity.
   Specifically check whether the draft’s definitions imply an ODE of the form
   \[
   F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}
   =
   \left(
   \frac{40q^2}{3}
   -
   \frac{10q''}{3q}
   \right)
   F_{\rm ext}''
   \]
   at \(t=m\), or whether such an ODE would impose impossible constraints on the zero-tail sum.

5. Compare asymptotics from the actual zero-tail formula.
   Use the one-pair atom
   \[
   f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
   =
   \frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
   +
   \frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
   \]
   Analyze whether summing over all exterior zeros could force
   \[
   F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}/F_{\rm ext}''
   \]
   to equal the expression involving \(q,q''\).
   Pay special attention to whether far exterior zeros contribute positive-sign leading terms to \(F_{\rm ext}''\) and small positive ratio \(F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}/F_{\rm ext}''\), since finite-tail models violate the identity.

6. Look for sign or positivity obstructions.
   If on a good patch \(q_0\neq0\), \(q_0''=0\), and \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), the identity requires
   \[
   F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}/F_{\rm ext}''
   =
   \frac{40q_0^2}{3}.
   \]
   Test whether the actual tail can have \(F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}/F_{\rm ext}''\) near zero, or varying freely, contradicting this.

7. Decide whether the identity is:
   A. proved by the draft or a standard zeta/xi phase identity;
   B. derivable but missing, giving a route to rescue Bottleneck C;
   C. false for admissible global/cutoff tails;
   D. unproved and highly nonstandard, meaning the Bottleneck-C route depends on a new global zeta-tail identity.

8. Deliver one of the following:
   - a proof of the global identity;
   - a counterexample/model showing it cannot follow from the current framework;
   - or a theorem-ready dependency statement:
     \[
     \text{Bottleneck C closes only if the full actual exterior tail satisfies }
     \frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
     =
     \frac{40q_0^2}{3}
     -
     \frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
     \]

Required final format:
1. State the verdict in one sentence.
2. Give the derivative-form identity with constants checked.
3. Explain whether \(F_{\rm ext}\) is identical to, complementary to, or independent from \(q\).
4. Give the decisive calculation or obstruction.
5. State the impact on Bottleneck C:
   \[
   \nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
   \quad\text{proved / refuted / still an unproved global dependency}.
   \]
```

## Coordinator readout

The final global-identity attack came back negative across all agents. The Bottleneck-C route should now be marked **failed at the local stage**, unless we are willing to introduce and prove a new pointwise global zeta-tail cancellation theorem.

The required identity is:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0,
\]

equivalently

\[
q_0F_{\rm ext}''(m)F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)
+
20
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
F_{\rm ext}''(m)^2
=0.
\]

When \(F_{\rm ext}''(m)\neq0\), this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
}
\]

All agents checked the constants and agreed this is the exact derivative-form identity required for aggregate cancellation.   

## Key finding

\(F_{\rm ext}\) is **not** the full \(q(t)\). It is the exterior omitted-zero tail, or cutoff/windowed exterior-tail source component. The identity therefore couples derivatives of one object,

\[
F_{\rm ext}''(m),\quad F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m),
\]

to baseline local phase data,

\[
q_0,\quad q_0''.
\]

The draft does not contain an ODE or conservation law forcing this cross-identity. The agents explicitly found that the draft provides decomposition, tail estimates, affine subtraction, and holomorphic/curvature control, but not a fourth-order exact identity tying the cutoff exterior tail to the baseline jet. 

## Decisive obstruction

For a one-pair exterior atom,

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

the far-tail regime gives

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

In derivative form,

\[
\frac{f^{(4)}(m)}{f''(m)}
=
12\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{80}{x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\to0.
\]

Thus finite far-tail models with positive natural weights can have

\[
F_{\rm ext}''(m)>0,
\qquad
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}\approx0.
\]

But on a good patch with

\[
q_0\neq0,\qquad q_0''=0,
\]

the required identity demands

\[
\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3},
\]

which is nonzero. This shows the identity is not forced by local source geometry, one-pair structure, conjugation symmetry, functional-equation pairing, or cutoff-tail architecture.  

## Stronger structural warning

One agent added a useful meromorphic obstruction: near an exterior-tail pole \(p\),

\[
f(t)\sim \frac{C}{t-p},
\]

so

\[
\frac{f^{(4)}(t)}{f''(t)}
\sim
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}.
\]

That pole signature belongs to the exterior tail. The right-hand side,

\[
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0},
\]

is built from the local baseline, which by construction has removed the omitted exterior pole structure. So the proposed identity cannot be a natural local differential law of the current decomposition unless the baseline secretly reimports the exterior poles, contradicting the local/tail split. 

## Final classification

The identity is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{not proved by the draft;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{not derivable from the current local zeta-source machinery;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{not forced by one-pair rigidity, conjugation, or functional-equation symmetry;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{an unproved, highly nonstandard global zeta-tail dependency.}
}
\]

Therefore the proof route now depends on a theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{For every good patch, the full actual exterior zeta tail satisfies }
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
}
\]

No current agent found such a theorem, and the finite-tail/cutoff models argue strongly against it as a structural consequence.

## Decision

I would now stop the attack on this Bottleneck-C architecture and mark the route failed.

The clean ledger statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
Under the current Bottleneck-C architecture, physical local closure is equivalent to the vanishing of the full aggregate \(S\)-visible coefficient \(\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}\). The required vanishing is not forced formally, not forced by actual one-pair zeta sources, not forced by source symmetries, and not proved as a global zeta-tail identity. Absent a new pointwise global zeta-tail cancellation theorem, Bottleneck C fails.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

Next step: update the proof ledger/paper draft to record this as a no-go, then pivot to a different architecture rather than continuing coefficient repair on this one.

## Coordinator readout

The ODE rescue has now been tested in the right way. The result is negative for the **current Bottleneck-C coefficient**.

The important distinction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{An ODE may exist for some related object, but not for the object that supplies }A_2,A_4\text{ in the current row.}
}
\]

For the existing \(\eta\eta\) top row, the moments are source-tagged zero-tail moments:

\[
A_2=\frac{F_{\rm ext}''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{F_{\rm ext}^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]

with

\[
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far}
\quad\text{or}\quad
T_{\far,R},
\]

depending on cutoff notation. It is **not** \(q\), \(q-q_{\core}\), or \(T_{\far,R}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}\). Therefore an ODE for a renormalized complement would not cancel the current coefficient unless the entire Bottleneck-C row is rederived with new source variables. 

## The ODE itself is also structurally blocked

ODE Agent B found a decisive meromorphic obstruction. If a candidate object \(G\) carries a zero-pair pole,

\[
G(t)\sim \frac{C}{t-p},
\]

then

\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
\sim
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}.
\]

But the proposed right-hand side

\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}-\frac{10q''}{3q}
\]

has leading pole coefficient

\[
\frac{40R^2}{3}-\frac{20}{3}
\]

if \(q(t)\sim R/(t-p)\). Equality would require

\[
R^2=\frac75.
\]

The actual zero-pair residues are purely imaginary, e.g.

\[
R=\pm\frac{i}{4}
\]

or positive-multiplicity variants, so \(R^2<0\). Hence the proposed ODE cannot be a meromorphic identity for \(F_{\rm ext}\), full \(q\), or any renormalized complement that still carries the same zero-pair poles. 

ODE Agent C also checked the standard \(\xi'/\xi\), Riccati/log-derivative, functional-equation, and phase-calculus routes. No such fourth-order closure appears. For the full phase derivative \(G=q\), the ODE is asymptotically false:

\[
\frac{q^{(4)}}{q''}=O(t^{-2}),
\]

whereas

\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}-\frac{10q''}{3q}
\asymp \log^2 t.
\]

So the full-\(q\) version is also dead. 

## Renormalized-complement escape

ODE Agent D’s result is the cleanest operational conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Renormalized-complement ODEs cannot rescue the present coefficient unless the row is rebuilt.}
}
\]

The only source-compatible enlargement that might matter is to define the source object as the entire exterior zero complement,

\[
F_{\zeroext}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\]

rather than only \(T_{\far,R}\). But then the required identity is still the same type of new global zero-tail identity:

\[
\frac{F_{\zeroext}^{(4)}(m)}
{F_{\zeroext}''(m)}
=
\frac{40q_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q_0''}{3q_0}.
\]

The draft does not derive it. Adding background or error terms such as \(B_{\bg}\) or \(E_{\est,R}\) would introduce terms that are not source-tagged \(\eta\)-variables in the current row, and would require recomputing the row from scratch. 

## Updated decision

The ODE attack does **not** rescue Bottleneck C.

The current ledger should now say:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0
\text{ remains an unproved global zero-tail dependency.}
}
\]

More sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No ODE for }F_{\rm ext},q,q-q_{\core},\text{ or a renormalized complement currently cancels the existing }\eta\eta\text{ top row.}
}
\]

## Only meaningful continuation

There is one coherent way to continue without repeating failed attacks:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rebuild the Bottleneck-C source convention.}
}
\]

That means: abandon the current row formula as fixed, choose a new source object such as

\[
F_{\zeroext}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

or even a larger complement, then rederive the promoted mixed-block \(\eta\eta\) coefficient from scratch. The question would be whether the bad top row changes, cancels, or is replaced by a better-structured expression.

That is not a repair of the current coefficient. It is a new architecture.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 16:48:42)

_Thought for 10s_

Attack the new architecture as a **source-convention rebuild**, not as a patch.

The failed architecture used:

\[
F_{\rm ext}=T_{\far,R}
\]

as the source object for \(A_2,A_4\), while \(q_0,q_0''\) remained frozen baseline data. The ODE agents found that an ODE for \(q\), \(q-q_{\core}\), or a renormalized complement does not rescue the existing coefficient because those are not the objects used by the current \(\eta\eta\) row. 

So the only legitimate next attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Choose a new source/baseline split, then rederive Bottleneck C from scratch.}
}
\]

Do **not** replace \(F_{\rm ext}\) by a larger object inside the old formula. That double-counts or changes the row without justification. ODE Agent D was explicit: a renormalized-complement ODE can matter only if \(A_2,A_4\) are actually derivatives of that renormalized object in a newly derived row. 

---

## New architecture target

Define a new split:

\[
q(t)=q_{\base}^{\new}(t)+G^{\new}(t),
\]

where \(G^{\new}\) is the source variable used to build

\[
r_G(t)=G^{\new}(t)-G^{\new}(m)-G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m),
\]

and hence

\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{G^{\new\,\prime\prime}(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{G^{\new\,(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

Then rederive the promoted mixed-block coefficient using \(q_{\base}^{\new}\) as the baseline and \(G^{\new}\) as the source. The question is whether the new \(\eta\eta\) top row becomes:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new}=0,
\]

or at least becomes physically \(S\)-invisible:

\[
f_{A,Y}^{\new}=0.
\]

Anything weaker does not close Bottleneck C because physical closure still requires the \(S\)-coefficient to vanish:

\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]

---

## Candidate source splits to attack

### Candidate 1 — full exterior-zero source

Use:

\[
G^{\new}=F_{\zeroext}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]

This is the most plausible source-compatible rebuild. It treats **all non-core zero atoms** as the source, not only the far omitted tail.

Then:

\[
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

This may remove cutoff instability because moving the cutoff only reallocates terms inside the zero-exterior source, rather than between source and non-source bookkeeping.

### Candidate 2 — full smooth complement source

Use:

\[
G^{\new}=q-q_{\core}
=
q_{\aux,R}+B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

This is more radical. It treats background and estimation terms as part of the source. It risks destroying the tagged-zero source calculus, but it may align the source object with a better ODE/complement identity.

### Candidate 3 — gauge-balanced complement

Choose \(q_{\base}^{\new}\) so that the source complement satisfies a normalization such as:

\[
G^{\new\,\prime\prime}(m)=0
\]

or

\[
\frac{G^{\new\,(4)}(m)}{G^{\new\,\prime\prime}(m)}
=
\frac{40(q_0^{\new})^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})''}{3q_0^{\new}}.
\]

This is dangerous because it may be circular. It only counts if the gauge is forced by a physical/analytic convention, not chosen to kill the obstruction.

---

## Attack sequence

### Phase 1 — source split validity

For each candidate split, ask:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does this source object actually enter the finite-}s\text{ transform?}
}
\]

The old row was quadratic in tagged zero-source variables. If \(B_{\bg}\) or \(E_{\est,R}\) are added to the source, then the row must acquire new terms:

\[
B_{\bg}\times T_{\far,R},
\qquad
B_{\bg}\times B_{\bg},
\qquad
E_{\est,R}\times T_{\far,R},
\qquad
\ldots
\]

Those terms cannot be inserted by hand. They must appear from a rederived source calculus.

### Phase 2 — rederive the \(\eta\eta\) top row

For a new source \(G\), compute the analogue of:

\[
\nu_{21,7}
=
[z^7]
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta_0}{s}
\right)
\eta_i\eta_j
\right].
\]

But now:

\[
q_-,\Delta_0,\eta_i,\eta_j
\]

must all be recomputed relative to

\[
q_{\base}^{\new}+G^{\new}.
\]

Do not reuse the old formula unless the derivation shows the same algebra survives.

### Phase 3 — check lower gates

The old architecture had closed Gate A and conditional Gate B structures. A new split must not reopen them.

Audit:

\[
\text{Gate A aggregate closure}
\]

\[
\text{Gate B through order }7
\]

\[
M_A,M_C\text{ connection tables}
\]

\[
\Phi_K\text{-visible }T\text{-readout}
\]

The key check is whether the new split introduces lower-order source terms that were previously absent.

### Phase 4 — ODE/identity test for the new object

Only after the new row is derived should agents test an ODE. The relevant identity will have the form:

\[
\frac{G^{\new\,(4)}(m)}{G^{\new\,\prime\prime}(m)}
=
\frac{40(q_0^{\new})^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})''}{3q_0^{\new}},
\]

but the constants may change if the row algebra changes.

This is why the new architecture must rederive the coefficient first.

---

```text
\[

1. Identify whether it is built from tagged zero-pair atoms, smooth background terms, error terms, or mixed bookkeeping objects.
```

## Strategic rule

Do not let agents “patch” the old formula.

The attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{new split}
\Rightarrow
\text{new finite-}s\text{ derivation}
\Rightarrow
\text{new top row}
\Rightarrow
\text{new identity test}.
}
\]

If any agent skips directly from a proposed \(G\) to the old identity, reject the result.

The first architecture I would test is:

\[
\boxed{
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}}
\]

with

\[
\boxed{
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}}.
\]

Reason: it is the least artificial enlargement. It keeps the source object as a zero-source object, avoids adding background/error terms as source atoms, and may remove cutoff instability.

## Coordinator readout

The source-convention rebuild was tested correctly. The result is:

\[
\boxed{
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
}
\]

is the only viable new source object to attack first, but it **does not remove** the Bottleneck-C obstruction. It merely upgrades the dependency from “raw far-tail identity” to “full non-core zero-complement identity.”

The rebuilt architecture is cleaner, but still not closed.

---

## 1. Valid split

Agent 1 and Agent 3 agree: the only plausible first rebuild is

\[
\boxed{
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
}
\]

Reason: \(G^{\new}\) is still a zero-source object. It consists of non-core zero-pair atoms, not background or estimation terms. The more radical candidates

\[
q-q_{\core}
\]

or

\[
B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R}
\]

mix tagged zero atoms with background/error bookkeeping and would reopen lower gates unless the whole Gate A/Gate B machinery is rebuilt.  

The rebuild is conditionally safe if:

\[
r_G(t)=G^{\new}(t)-G^{\new}(m)-G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m)
\]

is used, atom labels are preserved, and \(q_{\aux,R}\) atoms obey the same source-grade/reflection rules as \(T_{\far,R}\) atoms. 

---

## 2. New row derivation: obstruction survives

Agent 2 rederived the \(\eta\eta\) top row under the new split. The row algebra survives unchanged in form.

The new aggregate coefficient is:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
}
\]

Here

\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The physical \(S\)-coefficient is still

\[
\boxed{
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
}
\]

So physical Bottleneck-C closure still requires

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
}
\]

The new split does not algebraically kill the row and does not generate background/source cross terms that cancel it. 

---

## 3. New identity required

If

\[
A_2^{\new}\neq0,
\]

then the required cancellation is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{
\frac{A_4^{\new}}{A_2^{\new}}
=
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})^2}{9}
-
\frac{5(q_0^{\new})''}{18q_0^{\new}}.
}
\]

In derivative form:

\[
\boxed{
\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}
{(G^{\new})''(m)}
=
\frac{40(q_0^{\new})^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})''}{3q_0^{\new}}.
}
\]

Agent 4 found no ODE, meromorphic identity, moving-cutoff identity, or standard \(\xi'/\xi\) phase-calculus identity forcing this. The moving-cutoff problem is improved because \(q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\) is the full non-core zero complement, but removing cutoff instability does not produce the needed identity. 

---

## 4. Where this leaves us

The rebuild did something useful: it eliminated the objection that the old source object \(T_{\far,R}\) was an unstable cutoff tail. Now the source is the full non-core zero complement:

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]

But the same structural obstruction survives:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
}
\]

is still an unproved global zero-complement identity.

So the updated ledger is:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
The source-convention rebuild with \(G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\) is coherent and conditionally lower-gate safe. However, the rederived \(\eta\eta\) top row reproduces the same Bottleneck-C obstruction form with new baseline/source moments. Therefore the rebuild does not close Bottleneck C; it shifts the required theorem to a full non-core zero-complement identity.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

---

## 5. Next attack

There are now only two meaningful directions.

### Direction A — attack the full non-core zero-complement identity

This is the direct continuation:

\[
\frac{(q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R})^{(4)}(m)}
{(q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R})''(m)}
=
\frac{40(q_0^{\new})^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})''}{3q_0^{\new}}.
\]

But we should be honest: Agent 4 already found no known mechanism for this identity. So this is likely a last-ditch global identity attack.

### Direction B — abandon \(\eta\eta\)-source splitting as the Bottleneck-C architecture

The rebuild preserved the obstruction form because the same second-\(\Delta\)-Hessian mechanism survives. If we want a genuinely new route, it probably must avoid making Bottleneck C depend on a quadratic phase-gap source row of the form

\[
\eta_i\eta_j.
\]

That means redesigning the local invariant, not just changing which zero-tail is called “source.”

My recommendation: run one final attack on **whether the \(\eta\eta\) top row can be structurally avoided by choosing a different local invariant/readout**, not merely a different source split.

The current Bottleneck-C architecture should now be marked **locally failed**, unless we abandon the finite-\(s\) transform-faithful framework itself.

---

## 1. Local invariant redesign fails

Agent 1 found the core dichotomy:

\[
E=eI+fS.
\]

Any local invariant whose first differential sees \(S\),

\[
D\mathcal J[S]\neq0,
\]

is transform-faithful to the physical hidden \(T\)-direction, but it inherits the obstruction. Any invariant with

\[
D\mathcal J[S]=0
\]

can hide the bad row, but only by losing the physical \(T\)-readout.

So trace, determinant, unordered conjugacy class, symplectic/area invariants, and endpoint-symmetrized projective invariants hide \(f\) only by discarding the oriented hidden-transform direction. Oriented eigenvalue ratios, cross-ratios, and Schwarzian/curvature-like readouts remain sensitive to \(f\), hence inherit the obstruction. 

The theorem-level takeaway is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{transform-faithful} \Rightarrow \text{sees } f
\Rightarrow \text{inherits the }\eta\eta\text{ obstruction.}
}
\]

---

## 2. Quotient/moduli route fails for full Bottleneck C

Agent 2 clarified the distinction we already suspected:

\[
T \text{ is quotient-gauge for mixed four-point scalar exits,}
\]

but

\[
T \text{ is not gauge for the full transform package.}
\]

The quotient condition

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0
\]

only says the residual is invisible to the determinant/mixed-four-point quotient. It does not imply

\[
f=0.
\]

Indeed, if

\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0
\]

but

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5,
\qquad
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

So quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) identifies physically distinct transform states on the \(v_5\neq0\) patch. 

The clean statement:

\[
\boxed{
\ker\omega_h(\cdot,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\not\subset
\ker\Phi_K.
}
\]

Therefore quotient closure cannot replace the physical Bottleneck-C condition

\[
f=0.
\]

---

## 3. Alternative carrier attack fails

Agent 3 tested linear endpoint carriers, ratios, logarithmic carriers, determinant-normalized carriers, first-order carriers, phase-coordinate carriers, and finite-\(s\) exact carriers.

The bad mechanism is elementary and exact:

\[
N_{12}=\frac{\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\]

\[
N_{21}=-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}.
\]

The second \(\Delta\)-derivatives give:

\[
\partial_\Delta^2 N_{12}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
-
\frac{q_+\cos\Delta}{s},
\]

\[
\partial_\Delta^2 N_{21}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]

For a general linear carrier

\[
C_{a,b}=aN_{12}+bN_{21},
\]

the Hessian is

\[
\partial_\Delta^2 C_{a,b}
=
\frac{(b-a)\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{(bq_- - aq_+)\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]

To cancel identically, one needs

\[
a=b,\qquad a(q_- - q_+)=0.
\]

So nontrivial cancellation requires \(q_-=q_+\), which is not true at finite \(s\) generically. 

Log, ratio, determinant, and phase-coordinate carriers either retain the Hessian, reintroduce it when reconstructing the physical kernel, or lose the physical \(S\)-visible transform information.

So there is no transform-faithful alternative carrier inside the finite-\(s\) off-diagonal numerator framework.

---

## 4. Endpoint symmetrization fails

Agent 4 did the exact endpoint-symmetrized finite-\(s\) calculation. The off-diagonal second-Hessian matrix is

\[
H_{\eta\eta}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-B_+\\
B_-&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]

where

\[
B_\pm
=
\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_\pm\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]

This decomposes as

\[
H_{\eta\eta}=AJ+DX,
\]

with

\[
A=
\frac{B_++B_-}{2}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{(q_++q_-)\cos\Delta}{2s},
\]

and

\[
D=
\frac{B_- - B_+}{2}
=
\frac{(q_- - q_+)\cos\Delta}{2s}.
\]

Endpoint symmetrization can trade the common \(\sin\Delta/s^2\) part for endpoint-gradient data, or vice versa, but cannot kill both. Worse, both \(J\) and \(X\) feed the same \(S\)-visible row after the active \(E_{22}\) left whitening slot:

\[
E_{22}J=E_{21},
\qquad
E_{22}X=E_{21}.
\]

After fixed-sector symmetrization,

\[
E_{21}W_{+,0}\mapsto wI+uS.
\]

So both endpoint-skew and endpoint-symmetric pieces remain \(S\)-visible when their coefficients are nonzero. 

Thus the bad row is not an artifact of looking only at \(N_{21}\). It is intrinsic to the endpoint pair after whitening.

---

## 5. Final mathematical ledger

We have now tested:

\[
\text{source split}
\]

\[
\text{global tail identity}
\]

\[
\text{ODE rescue}
\]

\[
\text{renormalized complement}
\]

\[
\text{local invariant replacement}
\]

\[
\text{quotient/moduli interpretation}
\]

\[
\text{alternative finite-}s\text{ carrier}
\]

\[
\text{endpoint symmetrization}
\]

All preserve or rediscover the same issue:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a transform-faithful Bottleneck-C architecture must control the }S\text{-component }f.
}
\]

The concrete \(\eta_i\eta_j\) top row produces such an \(S\)-component. If it does not vanish by an actual global zero identity, physical \(T\)-horizontal closure fails.

The ledger statement should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.88\linewidth}
The Bottleneck-C obstruction is intrinsic to the transform-faithful finite-\(s\) off-diagonal phase-gap Hessian. Changing the source split, local invariant, quotient, carrier, or endpoint symmetrization does not remove the \(S\)-visible \(\eta_i\eta_j\) top row. Therefore Bottleneck C closes only if the physical aggregate \(S\)-coefficient vanishes by a genuine zeta identity. No such identity is presently proved. Absent that identity, the current Bottleneck-C route fails locally.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

## Recommendation

Stop trying to repair Bottleneck C within this finite-\(s\), transform-faithful, off-diagonal-kernel framework.

The next strategic move should be one of:

1. **Record the no-go cleanly** in the paper/ledger and pivot to a different route.
2. **Abandon the Bottleneck-C architecture entirely** and search for a proof strategy that does not require diagonal-merger \(T\)-horizontal closure.
3. **Attack the global zero identity directly** as a separate deep theorem, but no longer treat it as a likely hidden consequence of the current machinery.
