```latex
\subsection{Source-convention rebuild and persistence of the \(\eta\eta\) row}
\label{subsec:source-convention-rebuild-etaeta-row}

The preceding obstruction used the tagged omitted-zero tail as the source
object.  One possible repair is to rebuild the source convention by moving all
non-core zero atoms into the source.  The least artificial split is
\[
q
=
q_{\base}^{\new}
+
G^{\new},
\]
where
\[
G^{\new}
:=
q_{\mathrm{aux},R}+T_{\mathrm{far},R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}
:=
q_{\mathrm{core}}+B_{\mathrm{bg}}+E_{\mathrm{est},R}.
\]
Thus \(G^{\new}\) remains a zero-source object; it contains the auxiliary
non-core zero contribution and the far zero tail, but not the smooth background
or estimation terms.

The affine-subtracted source is
\[
r_G(t)
:=
G^{\new}(t)-G^{\new}(m)-G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m).
\]
Equivalently, the effective baseline in the finite-\(s\) expansion is
\[
q_0^{\new}(t)
:=
q_{\base}^{\new}(t)
+
G^{\new}(m)+G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m),
\]
so that
\[
q(t)=q_0^{\new}(t)+r_G(t),
\]
with
\[
q_0^{\new}(m)=q(m),
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})'(m)=q'(m),
\qquad
(q_0^{\new})''(m)=(q_{\base}^{\new})''(m).
\]
This affine absorption is necessary: otherwise the source would contain value
and linear jets and would reopen lower source-grade gates.

\begin{remark}[Admissibility conditions for the rebuilt split]
\label{rem:rebuilt-source-split-admissibility-conditions}
The split
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\mathrm{aux},R}+T_{\mathrm{far},R}
\]
is conditionally compatible with the already-closed lower gates under the
following hypotheses:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(G^{\new}\) is kept as a tagged zero-source sum through the finite-\(s\)
calculation, not collapsed prematurely into an unlabelled aggregate;
\item \(r_G(m)=r_G'(m)=0\) is imposed after the new split;
\item \(q_{\base}^{\new}\) is used consistently in \(q_\pm,\Delta_0,d_\pm,
e_\pm,g_\pm,\eta\);
\item the \(q_{\mathrm{aux},R}\)-atoms satisfy the same endpoint reflection and
source-grade conventions as the \(T_{\mathrm{far},R}\)-atoms;
\item the \(q_{\mathrm{aux},R}\)-atoms have compatible scalar-grade
normalization, or else the affected coefficient tables must be regraded;
\item no \(B_{\mathrm{bg}}\) or \(E_{\mathrm{est},R}\) term is treated as a
zero-source variable.
\end{enumerate}
Under these hypotheses the rebuild does not introduce value or linear source
jets before the Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) row.  By contrast, the more radical
choices
\[
G=q-q_{\mathrm{core}}
\quad\text{or}\quad
G=B_{\mathrm{bg}}+T_{\mathrm{far},R}+E_{\mathrm{est},R}
\]
mix zero atoms with background or error terms.  Those choices introduce
background--source and error--source products and would require a fresh
Gate~A/Gate~B analysis.
\end{remark}

For a tagged exterior-zero source atom \(\alpha\) in \(G^{\new}\), write
\[
r_\alpha(t)
=
g_\alpha(t)-g_\alpha(m)-g_\alpha'(m)(t-m).
\]
Define
\[
d_{\alpha,\pm}^{\new}=r_\alpha(t_\pm),
\qquad
e_{\alpha,\pm}^{\new}=r_\alpha'(t_\pm),
\qquad
g_{\alpha,\pm}^{\new}=r_\alpha''(t_\pm),
\]
and let \(\eta_\alpha^{\new}\) be the corresponding phase-gap source variable.
For two tagged source atoms \(i,j\), the finite-\(s\) substitutions become
\[
q_\pm
=
q_{0,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_i a_i d_{i,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j d_{j,\pm}^{\new},
\]
\[
q'_\pm
=
(q_0^{\new})'_\pm
+
\tau_i a_i e_{i,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j e_{j,\pm}^{\new},
\]
\[
q''_\pm
=
(q_0^{\new})''_\pm
+
\tau_i a_i g_{i,\pm}^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j g_{j,\pm}^{\new},
\]
and
\[
\Delta
=
\Delta_0^{\new}
+
\tau_i a_i\eta_i^{\new}
+
\tau_j a_j\eta_j^{\new}.
\]

The lower-left off-diagonal channel is still
\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}.
\]
Therefore its pure \(\eta_i\eta_j\) second phase-gap variation is
\[
\partial_\Delta^2N_{21}\big|_{\Delta=\Delta_0^{\new}}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta_0^{\new}}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_{0,-}^{\new}\cos\Delta_0^{\new}}{s}.
\]
Thus the rebuilt top-row scalar is
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,ij}
:=
[z^7]\left[
\left(
\frac{\sin\Delta_0^{\new}}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_{0,-}^{\new}\cos\Delta_0^{\new}}{s}
\right)
\eta_i^{\new}\eta_j^{\new}
\right].
\]

Let \(\rho_{\alpha,2}^{\new}\) and \(\rho_{\alpha,4}^{\new}\) be the midpoint
source coefficients of \(r_\alpha\) in the same normalization as before.  Then
the rederived pair coefficient has the same form as the old obstruction:
\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,ij}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{480}
\left(
\rho_{i,2}^{\new}\rho_{j,4}^{\new}
+
\rho_{i,4}^{\new}\rho_{j,2}^{\new}
\right)
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
\rho_{i,2}^{\new}\rho_{j,2}^{\new}
\right].
}
\]
Hence the source-convention rebuild does not algebraically kill the top row.

Aggregating over the full non-core zero source, define
\[
A_2^{\new}
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}^{\new}}
w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,2}^{\new}
=
\frac{(G^{\new})''(m)}{2},
\]
and
\[
A_4^{\new}
:=
\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal I_{\mathrm{ext}}^{\new}}
w_\alpha\rho_{\alpha,4}^{\new}
=
\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
}
\]

With
\[
W_{+,0}^{\new}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
u^{\new}&w^{\new}\\
w^{\new}&v^{\new}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
the corresponding fixed-sector row is
\[
\mathcal E_{\eta\eta;7,0,0}^{2,\new}
=
-\frac{\nu_{21,7}^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\left(
w^{\new}I+u^{\new}S
\right),
\]
so
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\top}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new}.
\]
Consequently, on a good patch with \(u^{\new}q_{\wh}^{\new}\ne0\), physical
Bottleneck~C closure still requires
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]

\begin{remark}[Outcome of the source-convention rebuild]
\label{rem:outcome-source-convention-rebuild}
The split
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\mathrm{aux},R}+T_{\mathrm{far},R}
\]
is cleaner than the raw far-tail source convention because all non-core zero
atoms are placed on the source side.  Nevertheless, the rederived
\(\eta\eta\) top row has the same obstruction form, with
\[
q_0,\ q_0'',\ A_2,\ A_4
\]
replaced by
\[
q_0^{\new},\ (q_0^{\new})'',\ A_2^{\new},\ A_4^{\new}.
\]
Thus the rebuild merely shifts the needed cancellation theorem to the full
non-core zero complement:
\[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
=
0.
\]
If \(A_2^{\new}\ne0\), this is equivalently
\[
\frac{A_4^{\new}}{A_2^{\new}}
=
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})^2}{9}
-
\frac{5(q_0^{\new})''}{18q_0^{\new}}.
\]
No such global zero-complement identity is presently proved.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 4 — Insert local invariant / quotient no-go subsection

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 3, before the finite-core subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Invariant and quotient no-go for the \(S\)-visible defect}
\label{subsec:invariant-quotient-no-go-s-visible-defect}

The source rebuild still leaves a physical \(S\)-visible defect.  One might
therefore ask whether replacing the local invariant or quotienting the fixed
sector can make this defect irrelevant.  This subsection records the negative
answer.

Let
\[
E=eI+fS
\]
be a Bottleneck-C fixed-sector residual.  The current physical readout has
\[
\Phi_K(I)=0,\qquad \Phi_K(S)=2,
\]
so
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f.
\]
The hidden-state slope is
\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Local invariant no-go]
\label{prop:local-invariant-no-go-bc}
Let \(\mathcal J\) be a smooth local invariant or readout defined near the
exceptional divisor.  Suppose \(\mathcal J\) is transform-faithful in the sense
that its first variation determines the physical \(T\)-direction.  Then
\[
D\mathcal J[S]\ne0.
\]
Consequently, whenever the Bottleneck-C defect has \(f\ne0\), the first
exceptional-divisor slope of \(\mathcal J\) contains a nonzero contribution
from the same \(S\)-component.  Thus replacing \(\Phi_K\) by
\(\mathcal J\) does not remove the \(\eta\eta\) obstruction.

Conversely, if
\[
D\mathcal J[S]=0,
\]
then \(\mathcal J\) may hide the \(\eta\eta\) row at first order, but it cannot
reconstruct or control the physical hidden-state slope
\(\partial_\kappa T\).  Such a readout is not a valid Bottleneck-C replacement
unless an independent theorem proves that \(T\) is pure gauge.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
At the exceptional divisor,
\[
\partial_\kappa\mathcal J
=
D\mathcal J[E]
=
D\mathcal J[eI+fS].
\]
If \(D\mathcal J[S]\ne0\), then the \(fS\)-component contributes to
\(\partial_\kappa\mathcal J\).  After any normalization that removes scalar
\(I\)-data, the \(S\)-term remains visible.  If \(D\mathcal J[S]=0\), then
\(\mathcal J\) cannot distinguish \(eI\) from \(eI+\varepsilon S\) to first
order.  But this is precisely the distinction measured by
\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]
Thus \(D\mathcal J[S]=0\) loses the physical \(T\)-direction, while
\(D\mathcal J[S]\ne0\) inherits the obstruction.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Examples of non-faithful and faithful invariants]
\label{rem:examples-local-invariant-no-go-bc}
Trace, determinant to first order at the scalar merger, unordered conjugacy
class, and symplectic area are blind to \(f\) at first order.  They hide the
bad row only by discarding the oriented \(S\)-direction.  Oriented eigenvalue
ratios, oriented projective cross-ratios, and oriented curvature or
Schwarzian-type readouts are sensitive to \(f\), and therefore inherit the
same obstruction.
\end{remark}

Next consider the quotient line generated by
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S.
\]
The quotient determinant coordinate is
\[
\Delta_7
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]
A residual \(E=eI+fS\) changes this coordinate by
\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f.
\]
Thus the quotient condition is
\[
ev_5-u_5f=0.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Quotient invisibility is not transform invisibility]
\label{prop:quotient-not-transform-invisibility-bc}
Assume \(v_5\ne0\).  The quotient condition
\[
ev_5-u_5f=0
\]
does not imply the transform-safe condition \(f=0\).  In particular,
\[
E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is invisible to the quotient determinant, but
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5
\]
and
\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
Therefore the quotient
\[
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
is a valid moduli object for mixed four-point scalar exits, but not for the
full Bottleneck-C physical transform state.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
If \(E=\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), then
\[
E=\chi u_5I+\chi v_5S,
\]
so
\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
(\chi u_5)v_5-u_5(\chi v_5)
=
0.
\]
However
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2\chi v_5.
\]
On a \(v_5\ne0\) patch this is nonzero for \(\chi\ne0\).  The hidden coordinate
changes by
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\quad\mapsto\quad
T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
Thus the quotient identifies states with different \(\Phi_K\)-visible
transform data.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Layer separation]
\label{rem:quotient-layer-separation-bc}
The quotient determinant layer and the physical transform layer see different
functionals:
\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f,
\qquad
\Phi_K(E)=2f.
\]
The kernel of the former is not contained in the kernel of the latter.  Hence
quotient-horizontal Bottleneck~C can close the mixed four-point scalar-exit
branch while still leaking in the physical \(T\)-coordinate.
\end{remark}
```

---

## Edit 5 — Insert finite-\(s\) carrier / endpoint-symmetrization no-go subsection

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 4, before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Finite-\(s\) carrier and endpoint-symmetrization no-go}
\label{subsec:finite-s-carrier-endpoint-symmetrization-no-go}

The remaining possible repair is to alter the finite-\(s\) carrier before
projection.  This also fails inside the present transform-faithful framework.

Write
\[
N_{12}
=
\frac{n_+}{s^2},
\qquad
n_+
=
\sin\Delta+q_+s\cos\Delta,
\]
and
\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{n_-}{s^2},
\qquad
n_-
=
\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta.
\]
For a pure \(\eta_i\eta_j\) source variation, the relevant variation is through
\(\Delta\).  Holding \(q_\pm\) fixed in this Hessian row,
\[
\partial_\Delta n_\pm
=
\cos\Delta-q_\pm s\sin\Delta,
\qquad
\partial_\Delta^2 n_\pm
=
-\sin\Delta-q_\pm s\cos\Delta
=
-n_\pm.
\]
Therefore
\[
\partial_\Delta^2N_{12}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
-\frac{q_+\cos\Delta}{s},
\]
whereas
\[
\partial_\Delta^2N_{21}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_-\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]
These are exact finite-\(s\) identities, not artifacts of Taylor truncation.

For a general linear endpoint carrier
\[
C_{a,b}:=aN_{12}+bN_{21},
\]
one obtains
\[
\partial_\Delta^2 C_{a,b}
=
\frac{(b-a)\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{(bq_- - aq_+)\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]
Thus identical cancellation requires
\[
b-a=0,
\qquad
bq_- - aq_+=0.
\]
For a nonzero carrier this forces \(q_-=q_+\), which is not a generic
finite-\(s\) identity.

The common endpoint combinations illustrate the obstruction:
\[
N_{12}+N_{21}
=
\frac{(q_+-q_-)\cos\Delta}{s},
\]
so
\[
\partial_\Delta^2(N_{12}+N_{21})
=
-\frac{(q_+-q_-)\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]
This cancels the \(\sin\Delta/s^2\) part but leaves the endpoint-gradient
term.  Similarly,
\[
q_+N_{21}+q_-N_{12}
=
\frac{(q_- - q_+)\sin\Delta}{s^2},
\]
so
\[
\partial_\Delta^2(q_+N_{21}+q_-N_{12})
=
\frac{(q_+ - q_-)\sin\Delta}{s^2}.
\]
This cancels the \(q_\pm\cos\Delta/s\) part but leaves the phase-gap term.
Endpoint balancing can remove one component of the Hessian, but not both.

At the matrix level, define
\[
B_\pm
:=
\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{q_\pm\cos\Delta}{s}.
\]
The off-diagonal second-Hessian matrix is
\[
H_{\eta\eta}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-B_+\\
B_-&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Writing
\[
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
X=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
H_{\eta\eta}=AJ+DX,
\]
where
\[
A=\frac{B_++B_-}{2}
=
\frac{\sin\Delta}{s^2}
+
\frac{(q_++q_-)\cos\Delta}{2s},
\]
and
\[
D=\frac{B_- - B_+}{2}
=
\frac{(q_- - q_+)\cos\Delta}{2s}.
\]
Neither \(A\) nor \(D\) is generically zero.  The skew part \(AJ\) is the
endpoint-average obstruction, while the symmetric part \(DX\) removes the
\(\sin\Delta/s^2\) term but retains endpoint-gradient data.

The active left whitening coefficient is
\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}
=
-\frac{1}{24\pi q^3}E_{22}.
\]
Since
\[
E_{22}J=E_{21},
\qquad
E_{22}X=E_{21},
\]
both endpoint-skew and endpoint-symmetric Hessian pieces feed the same leading
row after left multiplication.  Thus
\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}(AJ)W_{+,0}
=
-\frac{A}{24\pi q^3}E_{21}W_{+,0},
\]
and
\[
\Lambda^-_{2,0}(DX)W_{+,0}
=
-\frac{D}{24\pi q^3}E_{21}W_{+,0}.
\]
After fixed-sector symmetrization,
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\operatorname{Sym}(E_{21}W_{+,0})
=
wI+uS,
\]
up to the same normalization convention used in
Subsection~\ref{subsec:concrete-odd-etaeta-top-row-obstruction}.  Hence any
nonzero endpoint-symmetrized coefficient remains \(S\)-visible on a patch with
\(u\ne0\).

\begin{proposition}[Endpoint-symmetrized finite-\(s\) carrier no-go]
\label{prop:endpoint-symmetrized-carrier-no-go}
Let a finite-\(s\) endpoint carrier be formed from \(N_{12},N_{21}\) by smooth
endpoint-symmetric linear combinations and endpoint or Gram normalizations
that do not explicitly depend on the source variation direction.  If the
carrier remains transform-faithful, then its pure \(\eta_i\eta_j\) second
\(\Delta\)-Hessian has a nonzero lower-row component.  After the active
left-whitening slot \(\Lambda^-_{2,0}\), this produces a fixed-sector term
\[
-\frac{\mu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
for some endpoint coefficient \(\mu_{\eta\eta}\).  In particular, unless
\(\mu_{\eta\eta}\) is forced to vanish by a genuine zeta identity, the
physical \(S\)-coefficient
\[
f_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\mu_{\eta\eta}
\]
survives.
\end{proposition}

\begin{remark}[Nonlinear carriers do not repair the obstruction]
\label{rem:nonlinear-carriers-do-not-repair-etaeta-row}
Ratio, logarithmic, determinant-normalized, and phase-coordinate carriers do
not supply a transform-faithful repair.  A ratio or logarithmic carrier
normalizes the Hessian but leaves a nonzero endpoint-curvature term.  A phase
coordinate such as \(\Delta\) is affine in the source and therefore has zero
second \(\Delta\)-Hessian, but reconstructing the physical finite-\(s\) kernel
requires applying
\[
\Delta\mapsto \sin\Delta+q_\pm s\cos\Delta,
\]
whose second derivative is exactly the missing Hessian.  Thus the bad row is
either visible in the carrier, reintroduced by reconstruction, or hidden only
by losing the physical \(S\)-visible transform readout.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\subsection{Local Bottleneck-C ledger after repair attempts}
\label{subsec:local-bottleneck-c-ledger-after-repairs}

Combining
Subsections~\ref{subsec:source-convention-rebuild-etaeta-row},
\ref{subsec:invariant-quotient-no-go-s-visible-defect}, and
\ref{subsec:finite-s-carrier-endpoint-symmetrization-no-go}, the present local
ledger is as follows.

Changing the source convention from the raw far tail to the full non-core
zero source
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\mathrm{aux},R}+T_{\mathrm{far},R}
\]
is coherent under the stated tagging and grading hypotheses, but it reproduces
the same \(\eta\eta\) top-row obstruction form.  Replacing the scalar local
invariant hides the defect only if it discards the physical \(T\)-direction.
Quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is legitimate for mixed
four-point scalar exits but not for the full transform state.  Finally,
endpoint symmetrization and alternative finite-\(s\) carriers either preserve
the second-\(\Delta\) Hessian, reintroduce it during reconstruction, or lose
transform faithfulness.

Therefore, within the present transform-faithful finite-\(s\) off-diagonal
kernel architecture, Bottleneck~C closes only if the physical aggregate
\(S\)-visible coefficient of the \(\eta\eta\) top row vanishes.  In the rebuilt
full non-core zero-source convention this means
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0,
\]
or equivalently
\[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
=
0.
\]
No currently proved identity supplies this vanishing.  Thus the present local
route remains open-negative: it requires a new global zero-source cancellation
theorem, or else the Bottleneck-C architecture fails at this row.
```

```latex
The only remaining local rescue is a genuine physical aggregate
\(S\)-coefficient cancellation, not a formal package counterterm.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:05:10)

_Thought for 20s_

Yes. They are probably related, but not in the simple sense “the global identity will rescue Bottleneck C.” The cleaner interpretation is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The global zero identity is the obstruction class of the Bottleneck-C architecture.}
}
\]

So option 3 attacks the obstruction directly:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
\]

Option 2 asks whether we can build a proof architecture in which that obstruction class is no longer the gate.

## What we now know

The local Bottleneck-C condition has collapsed to a very specific statement. On a good patch,

\[
E_{A,Y}^{\rm agg}=eI+fS,
\qquad
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]

Therefore physical Bottleneck-C closure is equivalent to

\[
f=0.
\]

For the active \(\eta\eta\) top row,

\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\rm agg}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg},
\]

so local closure is equivalent to

\[
\boxed{\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.}
\]

This was formalized as the final local decision theorem. 

We also know that the standard repair moves failed:

- The row is isolated in the frozen table.
- One-pair zeta source jets do not force the needed locking law.
- Far exterior zero-pair sources approximate the bad \(r=u^2\) germ.
- Package redesign and counterterms cannot hide \(f\) without losing transform faithfulness.
- Rebuilding the source split with \(G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\) is coherent but reproduces the same obstruction form.
- Local invariant replacement fails because every transform-faithful invariant sees \(f\).
- Quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is valid only for the mixed four-point scalar-exit layer, not for the full \(T\)-visible transform state.
- Endpoint symmetrization and alternative finite-\(s\) carriers cannot remove the second-\(\Delta\)-Hessian row without losing transform faithfulness.    

So inside the current architecture, the global identity is not optional:

\[
\boxed{
\text{current Bottleneck-C route survives only if } \nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
}
\]

## How options 2 and 3 are related

Option 3 says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Prove the obstruction class vanishes.}
}
\]

That means prove a global zero-tail identity of the form

\[
\frac{q_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q_0''}{6}
-
\frac{2q_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0,
\]

or in the rebuilt source convention,

\[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
=0.
\]

Option 2 says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Stop using a proof architecture whose local gate is this obstruction class.}
}
\]

That does **not** necessarily mean the obstruction disappears mathematically. It means the proof no longer needs local diagonal-merger \(T\)-horizontal closure as a gate.

The two become related if the global identity is actually the shadow of a better global structure. For example:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
\]

may be a local coordinate expression of some deeper conservation law, flatness condition, index identity, argument-principle balance, or global variational identity. If so, attacking the global identity directly could reveal the new architecture.

In that scenario, option 3 is not just “prove a random miracle identity.” It becomes a probe for option 2.

## The key distinction

There are two very different ways a new architecture could relate to the global identity.

### 1. Strong relation: the global identity is a conservation law

Then the current obstruction is not an accident. It is a local curvature/residue term of a globally conserved quantity. The current Bottleneck-C architecture fails because it asks for the conservation law in a bad coordinate, namely the local \(T\)-horizontal coordinate.

In this case, the right new architecture would not abandon the identity. It would **derive it naturally** from a global invariant.

This is the optimistic branch.

Schematic form:

\[
\text{global invariant is constant}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{local obstruction density vanishes or is exact}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0.
\]

### 2. Weak relation: the identity is an artifact of the failed coordinate

Then \(\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0\) is not a true zeta theorem. It is merely the condition needed to force the current local \(T\)-coordinate to merge.

In this case, option 2 means: stop requiring this local \(T\)-horizontal condition. Use another route to contradiction that does not need the diagonal merger to be \(T\)-flat.

This is the pessimistic but probably more realistic branch.

Schematic form:

\[
\text{current local package requires } \nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}=0,
\]

but

\[
\text{RH strategy can be recast without that local requirement.}
\]

## My current judgment

They are related as **obstruction versus architecture**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Option 3 studies the obstruction. Option 2 asks whether the proof can avoid that obstruction.}
}
\]

The evidence so far suggests the identity is **not** a hidden consequence of the current local machinery. The ODE, source-split, finite-tail, carrier, invariant, and quotient attacks all failed. So if option 3 is true, it is likely to be a genuinely global zeta identity, not a local Bottleneck-C fact.  

That means the best next attack is not “try another Bottleneck-C patch.” It is to investigate whether

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\rm agg}
\]

has a global interpretation: as a derivative of a zero-counting identity, a residue of a meromorphic conservation law, an exact \(m\)-derivative, a positivity defect, or a curvature/connection form.

If it has such an interpretation, option 3 may generate option 2. If it does not, option 2 likely means abandoning the diagonal-merger \(T\)-horizontal framework entirely.

# Shared background for all four agents

```text id="shared-global-obstruction-background"
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft and recent agent audits.

We are no longer trying to patch the existing Bottleneck-C package locally. The following routes have already been tested and failed inside the current transform-faithful finite-\(s\) off-diagonal-kernel architecture:

1. Frozen row-table cancellation.
2. One-pair source-jet locking.
3. \(\Theta_\pm\) normal coordinates / formal counterterms.
4. Raw far-tail global ODE.
5. Renormalized-complement ODE.
6. Source rebuild with
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]
7. Local invariant replacement.
8. Quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).
9. Alternative finite-\(s\) carriers.
10. Exact endpoint symmetrization.

The current local Bottleneck-C obstruction is the \(S\)-visible \(\eta\eta\) top row. In the rebuilt full non-core zero-source convention, its aggregate coefficient is
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right],
\]
where
\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The physical \(S\)-coefficient is
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]

Because
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c,
\]
the current Bottleneck-C architecture closes only if
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

However, no current local mechanism proves this. Therefore we now treat
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
as a possible global obstruction class.

The strategic question is whether options 2 and 3 are related:

2. Abandon the Bottleneck-C architecture and search for a proof strategy that does not require diagonal-merger \(T\)-horizontal closure.

3. Attack the global zero identity directly as a separate deep theorem.

Working hypothesis:
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
may be either:
- a genuine global conservation-law density that should vanish;
- an exact derivative / residue / curvature term whose integral or cohomology class vanishes;
- a nonzero obstruction showing the Bottleneck-C architecture is the wrong local gate;
- or a signal for a different proof architecture where nonzero \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\) is used rather than cancelled.

Do not repeat prior local repair attacks. Do not propose cosmetic paper edits. Produce mathematical derivations, reductions, or no-go statements.
```

## Agent 1 — Global Exactness / Conservation-Law Agent

```text id="prompt-global-exactness-agent"
You are the Global Exactness / Conservation-Law Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared global obstruction background.

Your task:
Determine whether the obstruction density
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
is an exact derivative, conservation-law density, or boundary term for the full non-core zero source.

Known:
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
\]

Also
\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]
where
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Treat
\[
A_2(m)=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4(m)=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}
\]
as functions of the midpoint \(m\). Determine whether, for fixed source set,
\[
A_4=\frac{1}{12}A_2''
\]
holds, and identify all correction terms caused by moving cutoffs, moving core windows, or \(m\)-dependent tagging.

2. Rewrite the obstruction in terms of \(A_2,A_2'',q,q''\):
\[
\nu
\sim
\frac{q}{2880}A_2A_2''
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2.
\]
Check constants exactly.

3. Search for a quantity \(\mathcal H(m)\), built from \(A_2,q,q'\), such that
\[
\mathcal H'(m)
\]
or
\[
\mathcal H''(m)
\]
contains the obstruction density. In particular test expressions of the form:
\[
(qA_2A_2')',
\qquad
(q'A_2^2)',
\qquad
(q^2A_2^2)',
\qquad
(A_2'/A_2)',
\qquad
\left(q\frac{A_2'}{A_2}\right)'.
\]

4. Determine whether the required identity
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
\]
is equivalent to a second-order ODE for \(A_2\):
\[
qA_2''
+
20\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2
=0,
\]
up to exact constants.

5. Check whether this ODE has any conservation law compatible with the actual zero-source formula for \(G^{\new}\).

6. If exactness holds only after integrating over \(m\), determine whether the proof needs pointwise vanishing or whether an integrated identity could replace Bottleneck-C.

7. If no exactness exists, state the obstruction:
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
is not an exact local derivative in the current variables.

Deliverable:
Either an exact derivative/conservation-law formula for \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\), or a theorem-ready no-go that it is not exact in the natural midpoint calculus.
```

## Agent 2 — Meromorphic / Residue-Class Agent

```text id="prompt-meromorphic-residue-class-agent"
You are the Meromorphic / Residue-Class Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared global obstruction background.

Your task:
Interpret
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
as a possible residue, principal-part coefficient, or cohomology class of the meromorphic zero-tail field. Decide whether global residue calculus could force it to vanish.

Known:
The source atoms are zero-pair contributions of the form
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

The full non-core zero source is
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
=
\sum_{\alpha\in Z_{\rm ext}}w_\alpha f_\alpha.
\]

The aggregate obstruction depends on
\[
G''(m),\qquad G^{(4)}(m),
\qquad q_0^{\new},\qquad (q_0^{\new})''.
\]

Tasks:
1. Write \(G''(m)\) and \(G^{(4)}(m)\) as meromorphic sums over zero-pair poles:
\[
G''(m)=\sum_\alpha c_{\alpha,3}(m-p_\alpha)^{-3}+\cdots,
\]
\[
G^{(4)}(m)=\sum_\alpha c_{\alpha,5}(m-p_\alpha)^{-5}+\cdots.
\]

2. Express
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
as a quadratic meromorphic expression in these sums.

3. Ask whether this quadratic expression is the residue or constant term of a meromorphic differential:
\[
d\Omega(m),
\qquad
\operatorname{Res}\Omega,
\qquad
\operatorname{CT}_m\Omega.
\]

4. Test whether the global residue theorem could force the sum to vanish. Pay attention to:
   - pole orders;
   - residues at zero-pair poles;
   - contribution at infinity;
   - functional-equation partner poles;
   - conjugate-pair cancellations;
   - multiplicities.

5. Prior ODE pole tests showed that a meromorphic identity
\[
G^{(4)}/G''
=
40q^2/3-10q''/(3q)
\]
fails by principal parts. Do not repeat that. Instead test whether the obstruction could be a globally exact residue class even though the pointwise ODE fails.

6. If the expression is not a residue/exact meromorphic derivative, identify the obstruction class precisely: pole order mismatch, nonzero residue at infinity, wrong parity, non-cancelling conjugate poles, etc.

7. If a residue interpretation exists, derive the exact global identity and check whether it gives pointwise vanishing or only integrated/cyclic cancellation.

Deliverable:
A residue/cohomology interpretation of \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\), or a no-go proving it is not killed by meromorphic global residue calculus.
```

---

## Agent 3 — Curvature / Connection Obstruction Agent

```text id="prompt-curvature-connection-agent"
You are the Curvature / Connection Obstruction Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared global obstruction background.

Your task:
Determine whether
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
is best understood as a curvature term of the current Bottleneck-C connection, and whether a different proof architecture could avoid requiring that curvature to vanish.

Background:
The current finite-\(s\) transform-faithful architecture requires diagonal-merger \(T\)-horizontal closure:
\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c.
\]
The \(\eta\eta\) top row produces
\[
f\propto \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]
Thus Bottleneck C asks for local flatness in the \(T\)-direction.

But prior attacks showed:
- local invariant replacements fail unless they discard \(T\);
- quotienting is valid for mixed four-point scalar exits but loses \(\Phi_K\)-visible transform data;
- endpoint symmetrization and carrier changes preserve the \(S\)-visible row.

Tasks:
1. Reinterpret \(T\) as a connection coordinate on the fixed-sector bundle:
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
T=v_7/c.
\]

2. Express the Bottleneck-C failure
\[
\partial_\kappa T\neq0
\]
as a curvature, torsion, holonomy, or connection-defect term.

3. Determine whether
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
is the local curvature component of this connection.

4. If yes, test whether the correct global theorem should be:
\[
\text{curvature}=0,
\]
or instead:
\[
\text{curvature is exact / has zero holonomy / integrates to an index}.
\]

5. Compare with the quotient determinant branch. There, the quotient coordinate kills line shifts by \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), but loses \(T\). Determine whether the quotient branch is a flat quotient connection while the full transform connection has nonzero curvature.

6. Ask whether a new architecture could use the curvature itself as the contradiction-producing object, rather than forcing it to vanish.

7. If the curvature must vanish for the existing proof but need not vanish in a different proof, describe the architecture pivot:
   - what replaces \(T\)-horizontal closure?
   - what global object absorbs or measures the curvature?
   - what local-to-global theorem would be needed?

Deliverable:
A curvature/connection classification:
either \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\) is a curvature term that must vanish, or it is an obstruction suggesting a different architecture where nonzero curvature is tracked globally instead of locally killed.
```

---

## Agent 4 — No-\(T\) Architecture / Alternative Proof-Gate Agent

```text id="prompt-no-t-architecture-agent"
You are the No-\(T\) Architecture / Alternative Proof-Gate Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared global obstruction background.

Your task:
Design or refute a proof architecture that does not require diagonal-merger \(T\)-horizontal closure.

Current architecture:
Bottleneck C requires
\[
f=0,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2 f/c,
\]
and therefore requires
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

Prior audits showed that \(T\) is physical for the full transform package, but quotient-gauge for the mixed four-point scalar exits. Therefore, one possible pivot is to build the global proof using only quotient-determinant / mixed-four-point / finite-core scalar-exit data, avoiding hidden-state \(T\)-reconstruction.

Tasks:
1. Reconstruct exactly where the current proof uses \(T\)-horizontal closure downstream.
   Identify every dependency on:
\[
T=v_7/c,
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\qquad
\text{hidden-state reconstruction}.
\]

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
or mixed four-point scalar exits:
\[
\Delta_7,
\qquad
ev_5-u_5f,
\qquad
\text{finite-core determinant data}.
\]

\[
f=0.
\]
It may require only
\[
ev_5-u_5f=0
\]
or a quotient finite-core non-concentration theorem.

4. Check whether this loses the RH-relevant transform-state information. In particular, can zeros off the line still be detected without \(T\)?

5. Determine whether the finite-core and interaction branches can be reinterpreted entirely in quotient terms.

6. If quotient-only architecture is impossible, identify the exact step where \(T\) becomes indispensable.

7. If a no-\(T\) architecture is possible, specify:
   - new local gate;
   - new global transfer statement;
   - which old branches survive;
   - which old Bottleneck-C obstruction becomes irrelevant.

Deliverable:
Either a concrete no-\(T\) proof architecture, or a no-go theorem proving that any RH-relevant local-to-global strategy in this framework must reconstruct \(T\), hence must face \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0\).
```

## Coordinator readout

This wave clarified the relationship between the two strategic options.

The global identity route and the “abandon Bottleneck-C” route are related because

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]

is best understood as the **vertical connection-defect / curvature-density** of the current \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C architecture.

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Option 2 asks whether the proof can use quotient/global geometry without requiring pointwise }T\text{-flatness.}
}
\]

The agents found no evidence that the obstruction is an exact derivative, residue theorem, or local conservation law. But Agent 3 gave a useful reinterpretation: the obstruction may be a curvature term that should be tracked globally rather than locally killed.   

---

## 1. Exactness/conservation attack: negative

Agent 1 rewrote the rebuilt obstruction using

\[
A_2=\frac{G''}{2},\qquad A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}}{24}.
\]

For a fixed source set,

\[
A_4=\frac{1}{12}A_2''.
\]

Thus the scaled obstruction is

\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
qA_2A_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2.
\]

Equivalently, if \(A_2\neq0\), vanishing requires the ODE

\[
A_2''
+
\left(
\frac{10}{3}\frac{q''}{q}
-
\frac{40}{3}q^2
\right)A_2
=0.
\]

Agent 1 then checked whether this density is exact. Integration by parts gives

\[
qA_2A_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2
=
\left(qA_2A_2'-\frac12q'A_2^2\right)'
-
q(A_2')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A_2^2.
\]

The last two terms are genuine bulk terms. So the obstruction is **not** a natural exact derivative or conservation-law boundary term in the midpoint calculus. 

Important consequence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Even an integrated conservation law would not rescue current Bottleneck C, because the current gate requires pointwise } \nu=0.
}
\]

---

## 2. Meromorphic/residue attack: negative

Agent 2 represented the full non-core zero source as

\[
G(m)=\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}\frac{C_p}{m-p}.
\]

Then

\[
A_2=\sum_p \frac{C_p}{(m-p)^3},
\qquad
A_4=\sum_p \frac{C_p}{(m-p)^5}.
\]

The obstruction becomes a quadratic pole-interaction field:

\[
\nu(m)
=
\frac{q(m)}{240}
\sum_{p,r}
\frac{C_pC_r}{(m-p)^3(m-r)^5}
+
\frac{K(m)}{144}
\sum_{p,r}
\frac{C_pC_r}{(m-p)^3(m-r)^3},
\]

where

\[
K=\frac{q''}{6}-\frac{2q^3}{3}.
\]

Agent 2 found that the natural differential \(\nu(m)\,dm\) has generically nonzero local residues. In a two-pole constant-\((q,K)\) model,

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_1}(\nu\,dm)
=
C_1C_2
\left(
\frac{q}{8(p_1-p_2)^7}
+
\frac{K}{12(p_1-p_2)^5}
\right),
\]

which is not identically zero. So \(\nu\,dm\) is not an exact meromorphic derivative. Global residue calculus may cancel the **sum** of residues, but it does not imply pointwise vanishing

\[
\nu(m)=0.
\]

Thus the global zero identity is not a residue theorem in disguise. 

---

## 3. Curvature interpretation: useful pivot

Agent 3 gave the best conceptual result.

The fixed-sector hidden coordinate is

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]

The current architecture asks for \(T\)-horizontal diagonal merger:

\[
\partial_\kappa T=0.
\]

But the active row gives

\[
\partial_\kappa T
=
a_1^2
\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi c(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]

Therefore, up to a nonzero good-patch scalar,

\[
\boxed{
\partial_\kappa T \sim \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
}
\]

Agent 3 classifies this not as ordinary antisymmetric curvature, but as the **vertical second fundamental form / symmetric curvature-density** of the \(T\)-horizontal connection. 

This reframes the situation:

Current Bottleneck C says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{curvature density must vanish pointwise.}
}
\]

A new architecture could instead say:

\[
\boxed{
\text{curvature density is transported, integrated, or indexed globally.}
}
\]

This is the strongest link between options 2 and 3.

Option 3 is “prove the curvature vanishes.”

Option 2 is “stop requiring local flatness; build a global holonomy/index theory for the curvature.”

---

## 4. No-\(T\) architecture: coherent but major pivot

Agent 4 found that a no-\(T\) architecture is coherent only as a **new quotient-determinant program**, not as a repair of the existing proof.

The quotient data are

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\]

where

\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

A shift

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

preserves \(\Delta_7\), but changes

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]

So \(T\) is not recoverable from quotient data. A no-\(T\) proof must therefore abandon hidden-state reconstruction and formulate the global contradiction entirely through quotient determinant data, mixed four-point scalar exits, and finite-core determinant data. 

The replacement local gate would be

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0,
\]

not

\[
f=0.
\]

That makes the old \(T\)-leak irrelevant only if the downstream proof never needs \(T\).

Agent 4’s conditional no-go is important:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If the proof requires hidden-state reconstruction, then no quotient-only architecture works.}
}
\]

So the no-\(T\) architecture is possible only if we can rebuild the finite-core/global contradiction using quotient data alone.

---

## 5. Updated strategic map

We now have three branches.

### Branch A — Pointwise flatness theorem

Try to prove

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

The agents found no exactness, residue, ODE, or local conservation mechanism. This branch remains possible only as a genuinely new pointwise global zero-complement identity.

Low probability, but direct.

### Branch B — Curvature / holonomy architecture

Accept

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\neq0
\]

as a curvature density. Replace pointwise \(T\)-flatness by a global statement:

\[
\int \mathcal K = 0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Hol}(\mathcal K)=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Index}(\mathcal K)=0,
\]

or an off-line-zero contradiction based on nonzero holonomy.

This is conceptually promising, but requires proving that

\[
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\,dm
\]

is a well-defined global curvature/connection density under changes of patch, core, source window, and normalization.

### Branch C — No-\(T\) quotient architecture

Abandon \(T\)-horizontal closure entirely. Use only quotient data:

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\]

mixed four-point scalar exits, and quotient finite-core geometry.

This makes the \(T\)-leak irrelevant, but transfers the burden to quotient finite-core non-concentration and quotient interaction rigidity.

---

## Recommendation

Do **not** continue trying to prove the pointwise identity first. The exactness/residue agents made that look structurally unlikely.

The best next attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can we define a global curvature/holonomy object from }
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\text{ that replaces pointwise }T\text{-flatness?}
}
\]

In parallel, we should ask whether the quotient-only architecture can still detect off-line zeros. If yes, it avoids the obstruction entirely. If no, the curvature route becomes the only viable pivot.

## Edit 1 — Add this subsection after the current local ledger

**Where:** Immediately after the paragraph ending:

```latex
No currently proved identity supplies this vanishing.  Thus the present local
route remains open-negative: it requires a new global zero-source cancellation
theorem, or else the Bottleneck-C architecture fails at this row.
```

and immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Global obstruction-class interpretation of the Bottleneck-C defect}
\label{subsec:global-obstruction-class-bottleneck-c-defect}

The preceding local ledger shows that the present transform-faithful
finite-\(s\) Bottleneck-C architecture closes only if the rebuilt aggregate
coefficient
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
\]
vanishes pointwise.  The next question is whether this coefficient is a hidden
boundary term, residue identity, or global conservation-law density.  The
current evidence is negative: it is better understood as a bulk vertical
connection-defect density for the \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C connection.

For this subsection write, for readability,
\[
G:=G^{\new}=q_{\mathrm{aux},R}+T_{\mathrm{far},R},
\qquad
A_2:=\frac{G''(m)}{2},
\qquad
A_4:=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]
and
\[
q:=q_0^{\new},
\qquad
q'':=(q_0^{\new})''.
\]
The rebuilt obstruction is
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

\begin{proposition}[No natural exactness for the rebuilt Bottleneck-C defect]
\label{prop:no-natural-exactness-rebuilt-bc-defect}
Assume the source set is fixed as \(m\) varies, so that
\[
A_4=\frac{1}{12}A_2''.
\]
Then
\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
qA_2A_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2.
\]
This density is not an exact first-order local derivative in the natural
midpoint variables \((A_2,A_2',q,q')\).  More precisely,
\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
\left(
qA_2A_2'
-
\frac12 q'A_2^2
\right)'
-
q(A_2')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)
A_2^2.
\]
The final two terms are genuine bulk terms.  Hence
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
\]
is not a boundary term or conservation-law density in the ordinary midpoint
calculus.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Since \(A_2=G''/2\), fixed source tagging gives
\[
A_2''=\frac{G^{(4)}}{2},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}}{24}=\frac{1}{12}A_2''.
\]
Substitution into the formula for
\(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}\) gives the first displayed identity.
For the integration-by-parts decomposition, compute
\[
(qA_2A_2')'
=
qA_2A_2''
+
q(A_2')^2
+
q'A_2A_2',
\]
and
\[
(q'A_2^2)'=q''A_2^2+2q'A_2A_2'.
\]
Therefore
\[
qA_2A_2''
=
\left(
qA_2A_2'
-
\frac12q'A_2^2
\right)'
-
q(A_2')^2
+
\frac12q''A_2^2.
\]
Adding
\[
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2^2
\]
gives the claimed residual term
\[
-q(A_2')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A_2^2.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Moving source windows]
\label{rem:moving-source-windows-exactness-correction}
If the source set, cutoff, or core window depends on \(m\), write it as
\(G_m(t)\).  Then
\[
A_2(m)=\frac12\partial_t^2G_m(t)\big|_{t=m},
\]
and differentiation gives
\[
A_2''(m)
=
\frac12
\left(
\partial_m^2\partial_t^2
+
2\partial_m\partial_t^3
+
\partial_t^4
\right)G_m(t)\big|_{t=m}.
\]
Consequently
\[
A_4
=
\frac{1}{12}A_2''
-
\frac{1}{24}
\left(
\partial_m^2\partial_t^2
+
2\partial_m\partial_t^3
\right)G_m(t)\big|_{t=m}.
\]
Thus moving cutoffs or moving core windows introduce extra correction terms.
They do not by themselves create a conservation law; they add another
identity requirement.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The induced second-order equation]
\label{rem:induced-second-order-equation-bc-defect}
If \(A_2\ne0\), pointwise vanishing of
\(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}\) is equivalent, in the fixed-source-set
calculus, to
\[
qA_2''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A_2
=0,
\]
or
\[
A_2''
+
\left(
\frac{10}{3}\frac{q''}{q}
-
\frac{40}{3}q^2
\right)A_2
=0.
\]
This should be read as the unproved pointwise equation demanded by the current
Bottleneck-C gate, not as an already available zeta-side ODE.
\end{remark}
```

---

## Edit 2 — Add meromorphic/residue no-go immediately after Edit 1

**Where:** Immediately after the subsection inserted in Edit 1, before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Meromorphic residue no-go for the rebuilt obstruction}
\label{subsec:meromorphic-residue-no-go-rebuilt-obstruction}

There is also no current residue-theoretic mechanism forcing
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}(m)=0.
\]
The rebuilt source is a zero-pair pole field.  Locally write
\[
G(m)
=
\sum_{p\in P_{\mathrm{ext}}}\frac{C_p}{m-p},
\]
where \(P_{\mathrm{ext}}\) is the set of non-core zero-source poles and
\(C_p\) includes the residue and source weight.  Then
\[
A_2(m)=\sum_p\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^3},
\qquad
A_4(m)=\sum_p\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^5}.
\]
If
\[
K(m):=\frac{q''(m)}{6}-\frac{2q(m)^3}{3},
\]
then, up to the global factor \(Q^{-14}\),
\[
\nu(m)
:=
\frac{q(m)}{240}A_2A_4+\frac{K(m)}{144}A_2^2
\]
is the quadratic pole-interaction field
\[
\nu(m)
=
\frac{q(m)}{240}
\sum_{p,r}
\frac{C_pC_r}{(m-p)^3(m-r)^5}
+
\frac{K(m)}{144}
\sum_{p,r}
\frac{C_pC_r}{(m-p)^3(m-r)^3}.
\]

\begin{proposition}[The rebuilt obstruction is not residue-killed]
\label{prop:rebuilt-obstruction-not-residue-killed}
The meromorphic differential \(\nu(m)\,dm\) is not, in general, an exact
meromorphic derivative.  Its local residues at zero-source poles are
generically nonzero.  Hence the global residue theorem can at most give
cancellation of the sum of residues; it does not imply the pointwise condition
\[
\nu(m)=0
\]
required by Bottleneck~C.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Fix a pole \(p\) and write \(\tau=m-p\).  Decompose
\[
A_2=C_p\tau^{-3}+a(\tau),
\qquad
A_4=C_p\tau^{-5}+b(\tau),
\]
where \(a,b\) are holomorphic at \(\tau=0\).  Then
\[
A_2A_4
=
C_p^2\tau^{-8}
+
C_pb\,\tau^{-3}
+
C_pa\,\tau^{-5}
+
ab,
\]
and
\[
A_2^2
=
C_p^2\tau^{-6}
+
2C_pa\,\tau^{-3}
+
a^2.
\]
Thus \(\nu(m)\,dm\) has high-order poles, and its residue depends on Taylor
coefficients of \(q,K,a,b\) at \(p\).  There is no structural reason for this
residue to vanish.

Already in a two-pole constant-\((q,K)\) model, with poles \(p_1,p_2\),
residues \(C_1,C_2\), and \(d=p_1-p_2\), the analytic tail at \(p_1\) gives
\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_1}(\nu\,dm)
=
C_1C_2
\left(
\frac{q}{8d^7}
+
\frac{K}{12d^5}
\right),
\]
which is generically nonzero.  Therefore \(\nu(m)\,dm\) is not an exact
meromorphic derivative.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What residue calculus can and cannot give]
\label{rem:residue-calculus-limit-bc-obstruction}
Functional-equation pairing and conjugation may pair or cancel residues in a
global sum.  Such cancellation is compatible with the global residue theorem,
but it is much weaker than the pointwise identity
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}(m)=0.
\]
The Bottleneck-C gate is pointwise because
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}},
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]
Thus an integrated or cyclic residue cancellation cannot close the present
\(T\)-horizontal gate.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 3 — Add curvature/connection interpretation after Edit 2

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 2 and before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Connection-defect interpretation and possible architecture pivot}
\label{subsec:connection-defect-interpretation-bc}

The preceding no-go results suggest a different interpretation.  The
coefficient
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
\]
is not merely a bad scalar coefficient; it is the vertical defect of the
current \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C connection.

Recall that
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
\qquad
T=\frac{v_7}{c}.
\]
For a residual
\[
E=eI+fS,
\]
the physical readout satisfies
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\]
and the Bottleneck-C exceptional slope is
\[
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2\frac{f}{c}.
\]
For the rebuilt non-core zero-source convention, the active \(\eta\eta\) row
gives
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}.
\]
Hence, on a good patch,
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
a_1^2
\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi c(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}.
\]

\begin{definition}[Bottleneck-C vertical defect density]
\label{def:bottleneck-c-vertical-defect-density}
Define
\[
\mathcal K_{\eta\eta;\kappa}
:=
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal K_{\eta\eta;\kappa}
=
C_{\rm geom}\,
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}},
\qquad
C_{\rm geom}
=
a_1^2
\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi c(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}.
\]
On a good patch,
\[
C_{\rm geom}\ne0.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Curvature versus second fundamental form]
\label{rem:curvature-versus-second-fundamental-form-bc}
The active row is symmetric in the source directions \(\eta_i,\eta_j\).  Thus
\(\mathcal K_{\eta\eta;\kappa}\) is not ordinary antisymmetric gauge curvature
by itself.  It is better regarded as the vertical second fundamental form, or
quadratic curvature-density, of the diagonal-merger horizontal distribution in
the \(T\)-coordinate.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Local flatness equivalence]
\label{prop:local-flatness-equivalence-bc}
Within the current transform-faithful Bottleneck-C architecture, local
\(T\)-horizontal closure of the rebuilt \(\eta\eta\) row is equivalent to
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Definition~\ref{def:bottleneck-c-vertical-defect-density},
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
C_{\rm geom}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}.
\]
On a good patch \(C_{\rm geom}\ne0\).  Therefore
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}=0
\]
if and only if
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Possible curvature/holonomy pivot]
\label{rem:possible-curvature-holonomy-pivot}
The current Bottleneck-C architecture demands pointwise flatness:
\[
\mathcal K_{\eta\eta;\kappa}=0.
\]
A different architecture could attempt to treat
\[
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}\,dm
\]
as a global curvature or holonomy density, replacing pointwise \(T\)-flatness
by a global statement such as
\[
\int \mathcal K_{\eta\eta;\kappa}\,dm=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Hol}_T(\mathcal K)=0,
\qquad
\text{or}\qquad
\operatorname{Index}(\mathcal K)=0.
\]
This would be a genuine architecture pivot, not a repair of the present local
Bottleneck-C gate.  To make such a pivot meaningful, one would first need to
prove transformation laws showing that
\[
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}\,dm
\]
is a globally defined connection or curvature density under changes of patch,
core window, source convention, and normalization.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 4 — Add no-\(T\) quotient architecture note after Edit 3

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 3 and before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{No-\(T\) quotient-determinant architecture as a possible pivot}
\label{subsec:no-t-quotient-determinant-architecture}

A second possible pivot is to abandon the \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C gate
entirely and formulate the local-to-global argument using only quotient
determinant data.  This is not a repair of Bottleneck~C; it is a different
proof architecture.

The fixed-sector data are
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S.
\]
The quotient determinant coordinate is
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]
A shift
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
preserves \(\Delta_7\), but changes
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\quad\mapsto\quad
T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
It also changes
\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\]
by \(2\chi v_5\).  Thus \(T\) is not quotient-invariant.

A quotient-only architecture would use as local moduli
\[
\mathcal Q(h)
=
\left(
c(h),u_5(h),v_5(h),\Delta_7(h)
\right),
\]
or equivalently the quotient class
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]
\in
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Its local gate would be
\[
ev_5-u_5f=0,
\]
not
\[
f=0.
\]

\begin{remark}[What a no-\(T\) architecture would require]
\label{rem:no-t-architecture-requirements}
A no-\(T\) architecture can make the \(T\)-leak irrelevant only if every
downstream RH-relevant detection step is reformulated through quotient data:
\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\]
mixed four-point scalar exits, and finite-core determinant geometry.  It
cannot use
\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\]
or hidden-state reconstruction as independent data.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Conditional no-go for quotient-only architecture]
\label{prop:conditional-no-go-quotient-only-architecture}
If a downstream local-to-global step requires reconstruction of \(T\) or
\(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\), then no quotient-only architecture can replace
the current Bottleneck-C gate.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The quotient identifies representatives
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{and}\quad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
These representatives have the same \(\Delta_7\), but their \(T\)-coordinates
differ by
\[
\chi\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
On a \(v_5\ne0\) patch this is nonzero for \(\chi\ne0\).  Therefore no
function of the quotient data can recover \(T\) or
\(\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})\).  Any proof step depending on those quantities
cannot be performed in the quotient-only architecture.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Relation to the Bottleneck-C obstruction]
\label{rem:no-t-relation-to-bc-obstruction}
The no-\(T\) quotient program would make the obstruction
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
\]
irrelevant only by removing \(T\)-horizontal closure from the proof.  It would
not prove
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]
The burden would instead move to quotient finite-core non-concentration and
quotient interaction rigidity using only \((c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7)\) and the
mixed four-point scalar exits.
\end{remark}
```

# Shared background for all six agents

```text id="shared-background-curvature-quotient-wave"
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft.

We are no longer trying to locally patch Bottleneck C inside the current transform-faithful finite-\(s\) off-diagonal-kernel architecture. The following repair paths have already failed or reduced to the same obstruction:

1. Frozen row-table cancellation.
2. One-pair source-jet locking.
3. \(\Theta_\pm\) normal coordinates / formal counterterms.
4. Raw far-tail global ODE.
5. Renormalized-complement ODE.
6. Source rebuild with
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]
7. Local invariant replacement.
8. Quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) as a repair of the full transform state.
9. Alternative finite-\(s\) carriers.
10. Exact endpoint symmetrization.
11. Exactness / conservation-law interpretation in the local midpoint calculus.
12. Meromorphic residue theorem interpretation.

The coherent source rebuild is:
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]
It is conditionally lower-gate safe, but the rederived \(\eta\eta\) top row has the same obstruction form:
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right],
\]
where
\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The physical \(S\)-coefficient is
\[
f_{\eta\eta}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]

Because
\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c,
\]
the current Bottleneck-C gate closes only if
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

Latest interpretation:
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
is best viewed as a vertical connection-defect / curvature-density of the current \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C connection. More precisely,
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg},
\]
where
\[
C_{\rm geom}
=
a_1^2
\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi c(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}
\]
is nonzero on a good patch.

The latest exactness and residue attacks were negative:
- In fixed-source midpoint calculus,
\[
A_4=\frac1{12}A_2'',
\]
so
\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
qA_2A_2''
+
20\left(\frac{q''}{6}-\frac{2q^3}{3}\right)A_2^2.
\]
Integration by parts leaves genuine bulk terms:
\[
-q(A_2')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A_2^2.
\]
So the obstruction is not a natural boundary term in midpoint calculus.

- Meromorphically,
\[
G(m)=\sum_{p\in P_{\rm ext}}\frac{C_p}{m-p},
\]
so
\[
A_2=\sum_p\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^3},
\qquad
A_4=\sum_p\frac{C_p}{(m-p)^5}.
\]
The obstruction is a quadratic pole-interaction field, and \(\nu(m)\,dm\) has generically nonzero local residues. Global residue calculus can cancel sums of residues, but it does not imply pointwise vanishing.

Strategic fork:
A. Prove the pointwise global zero-source identity
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]
This now looks unlikely as a hidden local identity.

B. Replace the current pointwise \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C gate with a global curvature/holonomy/index architecture.

C. Abandon \(T\)-horizontal closure and build a no-\(T\) quotient-determinant architecture using only
\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7,
\]
mixed four-point scalar exits, and finite-core quotient data.

Your task is not to patch Bottleneck C locally. Your task is to test whether a new architecture is mathematically viable.
```

# Agent 1 — Curvature Transformation-Law Agent  
**Clone:** Zeta / Agent C

```text id="prompt-agent1-curvature-transformation"
You are Curvature Agent 1. Work only from the latest draft and the shared background.

Your task:
Determine whether
\[
\mathcal K(m):=
C_{\rm geom}(m)\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}(m)
\]
can be promoted from a local coefficient to a genuine global curvature / connection-density object.

Known:
\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg},
\]
with
\[
C_{\rm geom}
=
a_1^2
\frac{u^{\new}}{24\pi c(q_{\wh}^{\new})^3}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Identify the local bundle or fibre in which \(T=v_7/c\) lives.
   Clarify:
   \[
   A_7^{\mathfrak f}=u_7I+v_7S,
   \qquad
   T=v_7/c.
   \]

2. Define a candidate connection one-form \(\omega_T\) such that
   \[
   \omega_T(\partial_\kappa)=\partial_\kappa T
   \]
   plus any lower-order horizontal correction required by the draft.

3. Determine how \(T\), \(c\), \(u^{\new}\), \(q_{\wh}^{\new}\), and
   \[
   \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
   \]
   transform under:
   - patch changes \(m\mapsto\widetilde m\);
   - source-window changes;
   - fixed-core changes;
   - rescaling of the fixed-sector basis \(I,S\);
   - whitening renormalizations;
   - replacement of \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) by a scaled representative.

4. Test whether
   \[
   \mathcal K(m)\,dm
   \]
   has a coordinate-invariant transformation law.

5. If it does, formulate the global curvature object precisely:
   \[
   \mathcal K\in \Omega^1(\mathcal M,\mathcal L)
   \]
   or the appropriate line-bundle-valued form.

6. If it does not, identify the exact normalization defect: which factor prevents global covariance?

7. Decide whether a corrected density, for example
   \[
   \widetilde{\mathcal K}
   =
   \lambda(m)C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\,dm,
   \]
   can be made invariant by choosing a natural \(\lambda\).

Deliverable:
A transformation-law theorem or no-go. The output should say whether the curvature/holonomy architecture is even well-defined.
```

# Agent 2 — Curvature Holonomy / Index Agent  
**Clone:** Zeta / Agent C

```text id="prompt-agent2-curvature-holonomy"
You are Curvature Agent 2. Work only from the latest draft and the shared background.

Your task:
Assuming the local defect
\[
\mathcal K=C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]
is meaningful at least locally, determine whether a global holonomy or index theorem could replace pointwise \(T\)-flatness.

Current Bottleneck-C requires:
\[
\mathcal K(m)=0
\]
pointwise.

\[
\int_\Gamma \mathcal K\,dm=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Hol}_T(\Gamma)=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Index}(\mathcal K)=0,
\]
or another global condition.

Tasks:
1. Identify natural paths or cycles \(\Gamma\) in the draft’s geometry:
   - intervals between zero midpoints;
   - loops in the phase/kernel parameter space;
   - source-window deformation cycles;
   - finite-core transport paths;
   - Gram-block transport paths.

2. Determine whether
   \[
   \int_\Gamma \mathcal K\,dm
   \]
   is well-defined for any of these.

3. Test whether known global zeta/phase facts force such an integral or holonomy to vanish.

4. Conversely, test whether an off-line zero configuration would force nonzero holonomy.

5. Relate this to the quotient branch:
   the quotient determinant data may be flat while the full \(T\)-connection is curved. Determine whether the curvature holonomy measures exactly the lost \(T\)-data.

6. If possible, formulate a replacement proof gate:
   \[
   \text{off-line zero} \Rightarrow \operatorname{Hol}_T\ne0,
   \qquad
   \text{global zeta structure} \Rightarrow \operatorname{Hol}_T=0.
   \]

7. If impossible, explain whether the failure is:
   - no canonical cycle;
   - no invariant density;
   - holonomy not tied to zeros;
   - global structure does not force vanishing;
   - or off-line zeros do not force nonzero holonomy.

Deliverable:
A proposed curvature/holonomy proof architecture, or a no-go explaining why the curvature interpretation cannot replace Bottleneck C.
```

```text id="prompt-agent5-global-identity-last-chance"
You are Global Identity Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared background.

Run the last serious pointwise-flatness attack on

\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0,

but do not repeat prior exactness, residue, or ODE failures.

Could the identity be a special consequence of the **full non-core zero complement**
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}

and the rebuilt baseline
\[
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R},

\[

q=q_{\base}^{\new}+G^{\new},
\]
rewrite the required identity in terms of full \(q\) and baseline \(q_{\base}^{\new}\). Let
\[
G=q-b.
\]
Compute the identity in terms of:
\[
q,\quad b,\quad q'',\quad b'',\quad q^{(4)},\quad b^{(4)}.
\]

3. Test whether standard phase asymptotics, gamma/background terms, or the fixed-core definition of \(b=q_{\base}^{\new}\) makes the identity plausible.

4. Check whether the condition
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0
\]
can be reinterpreted as an equation defining the correct baseline \(b\). If so, decide whether this is legitimate or circular.

5. Determine whether a special choice of core/window can force the identity. If yes, check whether this violates source-tagging or lower-gate compatibility.

6. If the identity remains unsupported, state the strongest precise dependency:
\[
\text{Bottleneck C requires the full non-core zero complement to satisfy } \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

Deliverable:
Either a new exact coupling identity between \(G^{\new}\) and \(q_{\base}^{\new}\), or a final dependency/no-go for pointwise flatness.
```

# Agent 6 — Adversarial Architecture Decision Agent  
**Clone:** Zeta / Agent B

```text id="prompt-agent6-adversarial-decision"
You are the Adversarial Architecture Decision Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared background.

Your task:
Attack the entire fork adversarially and produce a decision recommendation.

The fork is:

A. Prove pointwise flatness:
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

B. Replace pointwise \(T\)-flatness by curvature/holonomy/index control.

C. Abandon \(T\) and build a quotient-only determinant architecture.

Tasks:
1. For Branch A, use known countermodels:
   - formal \(r=u^2\);
   - far exterior atoms;
   - finite-tail models;
   - source rebuild preserving the obstruction;
   - exactness/residue failures.
   Decide whether Branch A is plausible enough to keep attacking.

2. For Branch B, test what would be needed to make
   \[
   C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\,dm
   \]
   a global curvature density. Try to construct a counterexample where patch/source-window changes alter the density non-covariantly.

3. For Branch C, test whether quotient-only data
   \[
   (c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7)
   \]
   can distinguish an off-line zero configuration from an on-line one. If not, quotient architecture is dead.

4. Produce one explicit adversarial model for each branch:
   - Branch A: a model where \(\nu\neq0\);
   - Branch B: a model where curvature density is not invariant;
   - Branch C: two configurations with same quotient data but different \(T\)-state or RH-relevant hidden data.

5. Decide which branch should receive the next agent wave.

6. State the exact theorem needed for the selected branch.

Deliverable:
A decision memo:
- continue Branch A / B / C;
- or declare the current overall architecture nonviable.
```

## Coordinator verdict

This wave decisively changes the strategy.

The curvature interpretation is useful diagnostically, but it is **not yet a viable architecture** because the proposed curvature density is not globally covariant. The no-\(T\) quotient architecture is the only coherent next pivot, but it is a new proof program, not a repair of Bottleneck C.

The best current decision is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Stop attacking pointwise } \nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0 \text{ as the main route.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pivot to the quotient-determinant architecture and test whether RH detection survives without }T.
}

---

## 1. Branch A: pointwise flatness is no longer plausible as primary route

Branch A asks for:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0.
\]

The latest Global Identity Agent again found no hidden coupling identity from

\[
q=b+G,
\qquad
G=G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
b=q_{\base}^{\new}.
\]

The required identity becomes:

\[
G^{(4)}(m)
=
\left(
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}
\right)
G''(m),
\]

or, in \(Q=b+G\) notation,

\[
b_0
(Q''-b'')
(Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)})
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
(Q''-b'')^2
=0.
\]

This is an extra fourth-order pointwise constraint on the source/baseline split, not a consequence of the tautological decomposition \(Q=b+G\). 

Agent 6’s adversarial model also restates the core failure: take

\[
A_2^{\new}\neq0,\qquad A_4^{\new}=0,\qquad (q_0^{\new})''=0,\qquad q_0^{\new}\neq0.
\]

Then

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
-\frac{(q_0^{\new})^3}{216Q^{14}}(A_2^{\new})^2
\neq0.
\]

This model is compatible with the far-tail limiting behavior already found earlier. 

So Branch A is now a low-probability “miracle global identity” route.

---

## 2. Branch B: curvature/holonomy is not yet well-defined

Agent 3’s earlier interpretation was useful:

\[
\partial_\kappa T\big|_{\eta\eta}
=
C_{\rm geom}\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}.
\]

But Agent 1 has now shown that this local defect is not a globally defined curvature one-form. The main problem is the representative gauge:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Under this shift,

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c},
\]

so

\[
\partial_\kappa T
\mapsto
\partial_\kappa T
+
\partial_\kappa\!\left(\chi\frac{v_5}{c}\right).
\]

That is an **additive gauge defect**. No scalar normalization

\[
\lambda(m)\mathcal K(m)\,dm
\]

can remove it. 

Agent 2 confirmed the same at the holonomy level: there is no canonical cycle, no proved invariant density, and no theorem tying holonomy to off-line zeros. The curvature language is diagnostic, but not yet a replacement gate. 

So Branch B cannot be the next main branch unless we first construct either:

\[
\boxed{\text{a canonical }T\text{-gauge}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{a quotient curvature object avoiding }T.}
}
\]

That second option essentially becomes Branch C.

---

## 3. Branch C: quotient-only architecture is the only serious pivot

The quotient determinant data are:

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7),
\qquad
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

These are invariant under the line shift:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Indeed,

\[
(u_7+\chi u_5)v_5-u_5(v_7+\chi v_5)
=
u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]

So the quotient architecture has a clean gauge-invariant object. It discards

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c}
\]

and

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\]

as representative-level data. 

This is not a Bottleneck-C repair. It is a new architecture whose local gate is:

\[
ev_5-u_5f=0,
\]

not

\[
f=0.
\]

The old \(T\)-leak becomes irrelevant only if every downstream RH-detection step can be reformulated in quotient variables.

---

## 4. What survives in the quotient architecture

The following appear to survive:

\[
\boxed{\text{fixed-sector quotient data}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{projective determinant geometry}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{mixed four-point scalar exits}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\Delta_7\text{-based finite-core determinant data}}
\]

The natural quotient finite-core vector is:

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

Then define:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}),
\]

with split

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

The missing quotient finite-core theorem would be:

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\left\|
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta(m))
\right\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]

Agent 3 says this is coherent, but unproved. 

---

## 5. What remains unresolved under quotienting

Quotienting does **not** automatically solve finite-core or interaction.

### Finite-core issue

Quotient finite determinacy is weaker than full determinacy:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}=0
\]

means only that the finite-core anomaly is line-gauge:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

It does not imply the representative-level anomaly vanishes.

So quotient architecture must prove that quotient zero-anomaly is enough for RH detection.

That theorem is missing. 

### Interaction issue

Agent 4 found that mixed four-point closure is quotient-level, but the \(dd\)-interaction branch survives. The quotient scalar-exit geometry still has a kernel:

\[
K_{ij}^{dd,\quot}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2
\langle v_{\quot}(u_i),v_{\quot}(u_j)\rangle.
\]

The feature-balance condition remains:

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=0.
\]

For all balanced amplitudes this still forces

\[
v_{\quot}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\quot}(u_k).
\]

The spectral positivity obstruction also survives through the quotient-transverse feature. 

So the quotient architecture needs a new theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quotient }dd\text{-interaction feature-balance / cone-control / incidence-containment.}
}
\]

---

## 6. Decision

I agree with Agent 6’s recommendation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not continue Branch A as the main route.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not make Branch B the next main route until covariance is solved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Proceed with Branch C: no-}T\text{ quotient-determinant architecture.}
}
\]

This means the next wave should focus on two questions only:

### Question 1

Can quotient finite-core data detect RH-relevant anomalies?

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots)
\]

and

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
\]

must be defined and tested.

### Question 2

Can quotient interaction rigidity be proved?

Specifically, can we close or control:

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd,\quot}
\]

via feature balance, spectral cone control, or incidence containment?

If either answer is no because \(T\) is indispensable, then the overall architecture is likely nonviable.

# Agent 1 — Quotient Finite Determinacy Agent  
**Reuse:** Curvature Agent 1

```text id="agent1-quotient-finite-determinacy"
You are Agent 1: Quotient Finite Determinacy Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared quotient-architecture background.

Your task:
Determine whether finite determinacy survives after replacing representative fixed-sector data by quotient determinant data.

Current quotient variables:
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S.
\]

Define quotient coefficients:
\[
D_{2r+1}
:=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

In particular:
\[
D_5=0,
\qquad
D_7=\Delta_7.
\]

Candidate quotient finite-core vector:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)
=
(D_7,D_9,\ldots,D_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1})(\theta).
\]

Tasks:
1. Locate the existing full finite-determinacy statement in the draft:
\[
C_{\rm fd}=0
\Longleftrightarrow
H_{\core,\theta}\equiv0
\]
or its precise version.

2. Define the quotient zero-anomaly locus:
\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
:=
\{\theta:\ C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}(\theta)=0\}.
\]

3. Determine exactly what
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}=0
\]
means. Does it imply:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
for finitely many odd orders? Does it imply this for all odd orders by finite determinacy?

4. Prove or refute a quotient finite determinacy theorem:
\[
D_7=D_9=\cdots=D_{2R+1}=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
D_{2r+1}=0\text{ for all }r.
\]

5. Decide whether quotient finite determinacy is strong enough for RH detection.
Does quotient zero-anomaly still distinguish off-line zero configurations, or can an RH-relevant anomaly live entirely in the discarded \(T\)-line?

6. Identify any point where the proof needs representative data:
\[
T,\quad v_7,\quad \Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

7. If quotient finite determinacy works, state the theorem precisely.
If it fails, identify the first missing or false implication.

Deliverable:
A theorem-ready quotient finite determinacy statement, or a no-go showing that quotient data lose RH-relevant anomaly information.
```

# Agent 3 — Quotient Interaction Feature-Balance Agent

```text id="agent3-quotient-feature-balance"
You are Agent 3: Quotient Interaction Feature-Balance Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared quotient-architecture background.

Your task:
Determine whether the \(dd\)-interaction feature-balance obstruction survives in quotient variables.

The quotient \(dd\)-interaction kernel is expected to have the form:
\[
K_{ij}^{dd,\quot}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2
\langle v_{\quot}(u_i),v_{\quot}(u_j)\rangle.
\]

The old feature-balance condition was:
\[
\sum_i a_i v(u_i)=0
\quad
\text{for every balanced amplitude vector}
\quad
\sum_i a_i=0.
\]

In the quotient architecture, test the analogous condition:
\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=0.
\]

Tasks:
1. Identify the quotient-transverse feature \(v_{\quot}(u)\) from the mixed four-point / quotient scalar-exit formulas.

2. Prove the algebraic equivalence:
\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=0
\text{ for all }a\in\mathbf 1^\perp
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
v_{\quot}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\quot}(u_k).
\]

3. Determine whether quotient geometry forces
\[
v_{\quot}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\quot}(u_k)
\]
on every admissible same-scale finite core.

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.

\qquad

\qquad

\]

=

+

\right\}
\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.

feature balance, incidence containment, or cone control.
```
