# Agent 4 — Quotient Spectral Cone Agent  
**Reuse:** Quotient Agent 2

```text id="agent4-quotient-spectral-cone"
You are Agent 4: Quotient Spectral Cone Agent. Work only from the latest draft and the shared quotient-architecture background.

Your task:
Attack quotient spectral positivity / cone control for the \(dd\)-interaction kernel.

Expected quotient kernel:
\[
K_{dd}^{\quot}(t;m)
=
t^2
\left\langle
v_{\quot}\!\left(m+\frac t2\right),
v_{\quot}\!\left(m-\frac t2\right)
\right\rangle.
\]

Tasks:
1. Define the transported quotient feature curve \(v_{\quot}(u)\) from the quotient scalar-exit data.

2. Expand:
\[
v_{\quot}(m+h)
=
v_0+h v_1+\frac{h^2}{2}v_2+\frac{h^3}{6}v_3
+\frac{h^4}{24}v_4+O(h^5).
\]

3. Derive:
\[
K_{dd}^{\quot}(t;m)
=
\kappa_2t^2+\kappa_4t^4+\kappa_6t^6+O(t^8),
\]
with
\[
\kappa_2=\langle v_0,v_0\rangle,
\]
\[
\kappa_4=
\frac14
\left(
\langle v_0,v_2\rangle-\langle v_1,v_1\rangle
\right),
\]
\[
\kappa_6=
\frac{1}{192}\langle v_0,v_4\rangle
-\frac{1}{48}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle
+\frac{1}{64}\langle v_2,v_2\rangle.
\]

4. Under unit quotient-feature normalization
\[
\langle v_{\quot}(u),v_{\quot}(u)\rangle=1,
\]
verify whether
\[
\kappa_4=-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle\le0
\]
and
\[
\kappa_6=-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

5. Determine whether quotient geometry forces the needed sign:
\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\le0
\]
in the negative-type convention.

6. Test the unit curve countermodel:
\[
v_{\quot}(u)=(\cos\phi(u),\sin\phi(u)),
\qquad
\phi(u)=au+bu^3.
\]
Does it violate quotient spectral positivity without triggering quotient incidence?

7. If spectral positivity fails, formulate the required quotient cone theorem:
conditional positivity, negative type, moment/Hankel positivity, or incidence containment.

Deliverable:
A quotient spectral positivity theorem, or a coefficient-level obstruction showing the quotient \(dd\)-interaction branch remains live.
```

```text id="agent5-rh-detection-lost-t"
   - essential representative-level data;
   - replaceable by quotient determinant data;
   - cosmetic notation only.

A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{and}\quad

with identical quotient data but different \(T\)-states, such that one is RH-relevant and the other is not.

\[

\[

without losing the contradiction mechanism.

\Rightarrow

with no appeal to \(T\).
```

## Coordinator readout

The quotient wave did **not** close the proof, but it clarified the next kill switches.

The no-\(T\) quotient architecture remains the only coherent pivot, but it is now blocked by three theorem dependencies:

\[
\boxed{\text{quotient RH-detection}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{quotient sampled non-concentration}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{quotient }dd\text{-interaction rigidity}}
\]

The key result is that quotienting is algebraically coherent, but it is not yet a proof architecture.

---

## 1. Quotient finite determinacy survives, but only qualitatively

Agent 1 found that quotient finite determinacy works in the Noetherian/analytic sense.

Define

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]

Then there is a finite depth \(R_{\Theta_k}^{\quot}\) such that

\[
D_7=\cdots=D_{2R_{\Theta_k}^{\quot}+1}=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
D_{2r+1}=0\quad\forall r.
\]

So the quotient zero-anomaly locus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
=
\{\theta:\ D_{2r+1}(\theta)=0\ \forall r\}
\]

is finitely cut out. 

But this only means

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\forall r.
\]

It does **not** imply representative-level vanishing:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0,
\qquad
T=0,
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})=0.
\]

So quotient finite determinacy is valid but weaker. The first missing theorem is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{pure }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{-line anomalies are gauge-trivial for RH detection.}
}
\]

---

## 2. Quotient sampled non-concentration remains open

Agent 2 found that quotienting does not remove the finite-core alignment problem.

The quotient vector is

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\quot}
=
P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot},
\]

and the needed theorem is

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}
\Longrightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\quot}(m,Q).
\]

But the same cancellation pattern survives:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}.
\]

A formal quotient good-patch model can make

\[
0<
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\quot}+J_{\rm fd}^{\quot}\|_\infty
<
\Lambda_{\quot}
\]

while staying outside the quotient zero locus unless a new incidence/non-alignment theorem is proved. 

So quotienting cleans up gauge bookkeeping, but it does not solve sampled non-concentration.

---

## 3. Quotient interaction rigidity is still unresolved

Agent 3 found that feature-balance survives quotienting.

The quotient \(dd\)-kernel is

\[
K_{ij}^{dd,\quot}
=
(u_i-u_j)^2
\langle v_{\quot}(u_i),v_{\quot}(u_j)\rangle.
\]

Feature balance still requires

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=0
\quad
\text{for all } \sum_i a_i=0,
\]

which is equivalent to

\[
v_{\quot}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\quot}(u_k).
\]

Quotienting does not force this. The model

\[
u=(-1,0,1),
\qquad
a=(1,-2,1),
\qquad
v_{\quot}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

gives

\[
\sum_i a_i v_{\quot}(u_i)=2\varepsilon w\neq0.
\]

Thus the quotient interaction branch

\[
\mathfrak Z_{\rm int}^{dd,\quot}
\]

remains live unless feature balance, incidence containment, or cone control is proved. 

Agent 4 confirmed the spectral cone side is also unresolved. Under unit quotient-feature normalization,

\[
\kappa_4=-\frac12\langle v_1,v_1\rangle\le0,
\]

but

\[
\kappa_6=-\frac{1}{24}\langle v_1,v_3\rangle.
\]

The needed sign is

\[
\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\le0,
\]

and quotient geometry does not currently force it. The unit curve

\[
v_{\quot}(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3))
\]

violates the sign when

\[
b>\frac{a^3}{6}.
\]

So the interaction obstruction survives almost unchanged, but in quotient variables.

---

## 4. Lost-\(T\) is the central risk

Agent 5 found the biggest problem: quotient data do not currently prove RH-detection.

The quotient architecture keeps

\[
(c,u_5,v_5,\Delta_7,D_9,\ldots)
\]

but discards

\[
T=\frac{v_7}{c},
\qquad
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f}),
\qquad
v_7.
\]

For any \(\chi\),

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\mapsto
A_7^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

preserves

\[
\Delta_7,
\]

but changes

\[
T\mapsto T+\chi\frac{v_5}{c},
\]

and changes

\[
\Phi_K(A_7^{\mathfrak f})
\]

by

\[
2\chi v_5.
\]

So quotient data contain an entire affine line of possible hidden \(T\)-states. 

The current scalar pipeline

\[
H_m(s)=\Phi_K(\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m))
\]

is representative-level, not quotient-level. A quotient replacement would be something like

\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
).
\]

But the proof would need a new theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH violation} \Rightarrow \text{nonzero quotient anomaly}
}
\]

with no appeal to \(T\), \(v_7/c\), or \(\Phi_K\). That theorem is missing. 

---

## 5. Decision from Agent 6

Agent 6’s synthesis is correct.

Branch C remains the best remaining pivot, but only for **one more focused quotient wave**. It has strict kill criteria:

1. If quotient data cannot detect off-line zeros, kill Branch C.
2. If quotient finite determinacy does not imply useful quotient RH-detection, kill or redesign.
3. If quotient sampled non-concentration remains unchanged and unsupported, downgrade Branch C.
4. If quotient feature/spectral countermodels survive outside incidence, Branch C remains blocked.
5. If any downstream theorem requires \(T\), kill the no-\(T\) architecture. 

The synthesis also correctly says that mixed four-point quotient closure is the strongest positive evidence for Branch C, but mixed four-point closure alone is insufficient. 

---

## Current strategic status

The no-\(T\) quotient architecture is coherent, but it has not yet shown that it can prove RH.

The next attack should be a **kill-switch wave** focused on exactly two questions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can quotient data detect RH-relevant off-line anomalies?}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can quotient interaction/non-concentration be controlled without }T?
}
\]

If either answer is no, the current proof program is probably nonviable.

## Recommended next agents

Use four agents, not six:

1. **Quotient RH-Detection Agent**  
   Attack whether \(H_m^{\quot}\) can replace \(H_m=\Phi_K(\cdots)\).

2. **Line-Gauge Anomaly Agent**  
   Attack whether a pure \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomaly can be RH-relevant.

3. **Quotient Non-Concentration Agent**  
   Try to force \(\mathcal N_{k,\quot}^{\rm align}\subseteq\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}\).

4. **Quotient Interaction Incidence Agent**  
   Try to place feature-balance and spectral failures into quotient incidence.

The first two are the kill switches. If they fail, stop the quotient architecture.

# Agent 1 — Quotient finite determinacy / RH-detection strengthening

```text
\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}
=

\]

\[
\mathcal Z_k
=
\{\theta:\ A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0\ \forall r\}.
\]
We know
\[
\mathcal Z_k\subseteq\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}.
\]

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\forall r.
\]
What does this mean for the fixed-sector odd germ? Is it geometrically trivial, or can it encode nontrivial transform behavior?

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}\setminus\mathcal Z_k
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\quot}.
\]

\[

\Rightarrow
\text{not RH-relevant}
\]
or equivalently:
\[
\text{RH-relevant anomaly}
\Rightarrow
\theta\notin\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}.
\]
```

```text
D_{2r+1}.

4. Determine whether the analytic properties used for \(H_m\) still hold:
   - holomorphy in \(s\);
   - parity/oddness;
   - finite-order determinacy;
   - sampled-value reconstruction;
   - error/tail bounds;
   - local-to-global transfer.

5. Identify which properties fail because \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) itself depends on \(m\), source data, or normalization.

6. Determine whether \(H_m^{\quot}\) detects off-line zeros. Specifically:
does
\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\]
allow nontrivial representative-line anomalies that could still correspond to off-line zeros?

7. If \(H_m^{\quot}\) can replace \(H_m\), state the replacement pipeline.
If not, identify the indispensable lost-\(T\) step.

Deliverable:
A proof that \(H_m^{\quot}\) can replace \(H_m\), or a no-go showing quotient scalar readout loses RH-relevant detection.
```

```text
   - continue quotient RH-detection;

continue Branch C, narrow it, or kill it.
```

## What the six agents established

=

one gets

while avoiding the natural quotient incidence conditions on a Zariski-open set. So

without automatically triggering quotient incidence.

## The explicit failure mode

Assume a good patch with

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}=u_5I+v_5S,
\qquad
v_5\neq0,
\qquad
c\neq0.
\]

A pure line-gauge anomaly has

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\qquad
\forall r.
\]

Then the quotient determinants vanish:

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\]

while

\[
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})\neq0,
\qquad
T_{2r+1}\neq0.
\]

This is not a corner case; it is exactly the direction the quotient construction throws away.

The no-\(T\) architecture needed a theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Pure }A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{-line anomalies are RH-irrelevant.}

Equivalently:

H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\text{no RH-relevant anomaly remains.}
}
\]

The final kill-switch found no such theorem. Worse, the formal fixed-sector category gives a direct countermodel to detection: quotient-invisible but transform-visible line anomalies. 

So the quotient architecture loses precisely the signal that the original transform-faithful package treated as physical:

\[
\Phi_K(E)=2f,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]

Declaring that direction gauge would require a completely new proof explaining why the earlier \(T\)-visible transform data were never needed for RH detection. We do not have that.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:46:49)

The key constraint is algebraic: no scalar that is invariant under arbitrary shifts by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) can also detect anomalies lying exactly in that line. So the next object cannot be a plain quotient scalar; it must either fix a canonical representative, or promote the discarded line motion into separate global data.

_Thought for 21s_

The key algebra says a **plain quotient scalar cannot be the answer**.

If the equivalence relation is

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}+\chi A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then every quotient-invariant scalar necessarily kills the pure line anomaly

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

But that line anomaly is still visible to

\[
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})=2\lambda_{2r+1}v_5,
\qquad
T_{2r+1}=\lambda_{2r+1}v_5/c.
\]

That is why \(H_m^{\quot}\) fails as a replacement: it is quotient-invariant but incomplete. 

So the missing object must be one of the following.

---

## Candidate 1 — A canonical representative, not a quotient

Instead of quotienting by \(\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), choose a canonical section

\[
\sigma:
\mathfrak f_h/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\to
\mathfrak f_h.
\]

Then every state decomposes uniquely as

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{2r+1}^{\perp}
+
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The quotient scalar detects \(A_{2r+1}^{\perp}\), while \(\lambda_{2r+1}\) becomes a **canonical longitudinal coordinate**, not an arbitrary \(T\)-gauge.

The natural way to define this is with the Gram/whitened metric:

\[
\langle A_{2r+1}^{\perp},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}=0,
\]

so

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\langle A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Then the invariant package is not just

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

but the pair

\[
\boxed{
\left(
D_{2r+1},
\lambda_{2r+1}
\right).
}
\]

This is the most plausible replacement. It is gauge-independent **if** the whitening/Gram inner product is canonical. It is complete for both transverse and line anomalies.

But it may reintroduce the Bottleneck-C \(S\)-visible obstruction through \(\lambda\). That is the first thing to test.

---

## Candidate 2 — A connection on the \(A_5\)-line bundle

The line

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

may be the true geometric object. Then line motion is not discarded; it is measured by a connection.

Write

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{2r+1}^{\quot}
+
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Instead of treating \(\lambda\) as a scalar coordinate, define a covariant derivative

\[
\nabla \lambda
\]

using a canonical connection on \(L\). The invariant would be something like

\[
\boxed{
\left(
D_{2r+1},
\nabla \lambda_{2r+1}
\right)
}
\]

or globally

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Hol}(L,\nabla).
}
\]

This could reconcile the previous tension:

- quotient data miss line motion;
- \(T\) sees line motion but is gauge-dependent;
- a connection/holonomy may capture line motion gauge-covariantly.

The obstruction \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}\) then becomes not something to vanish pointwise, but a contribution to the curvature of this line bundle. Earlier curvature agents found the raw \(T\)-curvature was not globally covariant because of representative gauge. A canonical \(L\)-connection is the missing structure. 

This is the best “curvature” continuation.

---

## Candidate 3 — A two-component scalar readout

The old readout

\[
H_m=\Phi_K(\cdots)
\]

is complete but exposes the bad \(S\)-row.

The quotient readout

\[
H_m^{\quot}
=
\omega_h(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega,A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]

is gauge-invariant but incomplete.

So the replacement may need to be vector-valued:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right),
}
\]

where

\[
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\frac{
\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

This keeps both:

\[
\text{transverse quotient anomaly}
\]

and

\[
\text{longitudinal line anomaly}.
\]

The question becomes whether this **two-component readout** has better Bottleneck-C behavior than \(\Phi_K\). It may not require \(T\)-horizontal closure in the old sense; it may allow longitudinal motion to be transported by a canonical rule.

This is probably the most practical next mathematical object to test.

---

## Candidate 4 — A projective curve plus scale

The quotient scalar only sees the projective direction of the fixed-sector curve relative to \(A_5\). A pure line anomaly gives a constant projective direction, so it disappears.

To recover completeness, one needs the projective curve **plus scale along the line**:

\[
\boxed{
\left(
[A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s)],
\,
\|A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s)\|_{\wh}
\right).
}
\]

Or, more locally,

\[
\boxed{
\left(
\frac{D_{2r+1}}{\|A_5^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2},
\,
\frac{\langle A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\|A_5^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2}
\right).
}
\]

This is essentially the same as Candidate 1, phrased projectively.

It is worth testing because the current proof already has projective/determinant geometry; this may be the least disruptive extension.

---

## Candidate 5 — Declare the \(A_5\)-line physical and stop quotienting it

This is the blunt conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ is not gauge.}
}
\]

If pure \(A_5\)-line anomalies are RH-relevant, then quotienting was the wrong move. The missing invariant is simply the **full fixed-sector vector**

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in \operatorname{span}\{I,S\},
\]

but equipped with a different Bottleneck-C architecture that does not demand pointwise \(T\)-flatness.

That means returning to a full two-dimensional fixed-sector state, not \(\Phi_K\) alone and not the quotient alone.

The right object would be:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s)
=
\sum_r A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}s^{2r+1}
\in \mathfrak f_h.
}
\]

Then the proof must use a vector-valued analytic object rather than scalarizing too early.

This is a plausible “new invariant” direction: do not choose \(\Phi_K\), do not choose quotient determinant; keep the whole vector-valued germ and prove a vector-valued positivity/nonconcentration theorem.

---

# My ranking

### Most promising: Candidate 1 / 3

A canonical decomposition

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{2r+1}^{\perp}
+
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

with readout

\[
\boxed{
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
}
\]

is the clearest next object.

It is complete enough to detect pure line anomalies, but still respects the quotient geometry.

### Second most promising: Candidate 2

A canonical connection on the \(A_5\)-line bundle could make the line anomaly globally meaningful without reverting to arbitrary \(T\)-coordinates.

### Less promising: pure quotient

We now have a direct counterexample class:

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\quad\text{but}\quad
H_m\neq0.
\]

So pure quotient scalarization is not enough. 

---

# The next concrete attack

The next object to test should be:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
\omega_h(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\,
\frac{
\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
\right).
}
\]

Then ask four questions:

1. Is the whitening inner product canonical enough?
2. Does this readout detect both quotient and line anomalies?
3. Does Bottleneck C still require pointwise vanishing of the line component?
4. Does the \(\eta\eta\) obstruction become a controlled connection term rather than fatal local non-flatness?

If the answer to 3 is “yes, pointwise vanishing still required,” then we are back to the old obstruction. If the answer is “no, line motion is transported by a canonical connection,” then this may be the missing architecture.

```text
captures longitudinal line data.

1. canonical enough;
2. complete enough for RH detection;
3. compatible with finite-core and interaction machinery;
4. capable of replacing pointwise \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C with a controlled line-bundle/connection architecture.

Do not attack \(\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}=0\) again directly.
Do not revive pure quotient-only architecture.
Do not use \(H_m^{\quot}\) alone.
The target is the split readout and the canonical \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line decomposition.
```

```text
\[
```

```text
),

\[
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\frac{
\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),

}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m)
=

\[

\sum_r D_{2r+1}s^{2r+1},

H_m^{\parallel}(s)
=
\sum_r \lambda_{2r+1}s^{2r+1}.

\[
\mathcal H_{m,\odd}^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\frac12(\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)-\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(-s)).

5. Determine whether finite determinacy applies to the vector sequence
\[
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots).

   - \(H_m\) detects \(\Phi_K\)-visible anomalies;
   - \(H_m^{\quot}\) detects only transverse quotient anomalies;
   - does \(\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}\) detect both?

7. If the split scalar can replace the old pipeline, state the replacement finite-core vector.
If not, identify the analytic or detection failure.

Deliverable:
A proof or no-go for replacing \(H_m\) by the vector-valued split scalar
\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}.
\]
```

```text
continue split readout, shift to line-bundle connection, return to full vector-valued fixed-sector germ, or declare the current proof program nonviable.
```

Here are the agent responses

## Assistant (2026-04-25 17:56:50)

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The split readout is the **right next object**, but it has not rescued the proof yet.

It fixes the pure quotient failure:

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\not\Rightarrow
H_m\equiv0,
\]

because it records both quotient-transverse data and longitudinal \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line data. But that longitudinal component is exactly where the old \(T\)-visible obstruction lives. So the split readout is complete, but not automatically useful.

The decisive question is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the longitudinal component }\lambda\text{ be canonically transported rather than killed pointwise?}
}
\]

If no, the split readout just repackages the original Bottleneck-C obstruction.

---

## 1. What the split readout achieves

Define

\[
D(A)=\omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

and

\[
\lambda(A)
=
\frac{
\langle A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

On a good patch, the pair

\[
\boxed{(D(A),\lambda(A))}
\]

recovers the full fixed-sector vector

\[
A\in\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

Agent 1 proved the local recovery statement: \(D\) determines the metric-orthogonal transverse component, and \(\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) determines the longitudinal component. 

Agent 2 confirmed the analytic pipeline is viable:

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right)
\]

is vector-valued holomorphic in \(s\), its odd coefficients are

\[
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1}),
\]

and Cauchy sampling / finite determinacy can be run componentwise. 

So this object fixes the fatal weakness of pure quotienting:

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

is no longer invisible.

---

## 2. The bad news: Bottleneck C returns through \(\lambda\)

Agent 3 computed the active row in split coordinates.

For

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=e_{\eta\eta}I+f_{\eta\eta}S
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]

the split components are

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
(wv_5-u u_5),
\]

and

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Generically at least one of these is nonzero when

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}\neq0.
\]

If split closure means

\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\qquad
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0,
\]

then, since \((D,\lambda)\) recovers \(E\), this requires

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

hence

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

So pointwise split-closure is **not** an improvement over Bottleneck C. It is stronger than the old \(f=0\) condition in form, and equivalent to killing the same active row in this case. 

The only possible escape is to **not** require \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0\) pointwise. Instead, \(\lambda\) must become a transported line-bundle coordinate.

---

## 3. The line-bundle connection is coherent but still missing the theorem

Agent 4 gave the correct formulation.

Let

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Assuming the whitening metric is canonical, define the local connection one-form

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}
{\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}}.
\]

If a line section is

\[
s=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

then

\[
\nabla^L s=(d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L)A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Under

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
\lambda\mapsto \mu^{-1}\lambda,
\]

the covariant derivative transforms correctly:

\[
\nabla^L\lambda\mapsto \mu^{-1}\nabla^L\lambda.
\]

So the line-bundle architecture is mathematically coherent **if** the whitening metric is canonical. 

But it does not close the proof. It only reframes the obstruction:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
\]

becomes a longitudinal forcing / second fundamental form term in the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line bundle.

To make this useful, we need a new theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{longitudinal Bottleneck-C motion is transported or globally controlled, not killed pointwise.}
}
\]

No such theorem is currently present.

---

## 4. Finite-core and interaction difficulties remain

Agent 5 found that the split finite-core vector

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots)
\]

is essentially equivalent to the full fixed-sector vector on a good patch.

Thus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}=\mathcal Z_k
\]

at the fixed-sector level, unlike the too-large quotient zero locus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\quot}.
\]

That is good for detection.

But the sampled non-concentration problem returns in full:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
\]

is still possible formally. 

The \(dd\)-interaction problem also returns. The split feature curve

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
=
(v_{\quot}(u),v_{\parallel}(u))
\]

still requires feature balance or cone control. The usual countermodel

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

survives. Spectral cone problems also survive via the same \(\langle v_1,v_3\rangle\) obstruction. 

So the split readout fixes quotient incompleteness but does not simplify the hard finite-core / interaction problems.

---

## 5. Current decision

Agent 6’s synthesis is right:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Continue only if } \lambda \text{ is canonical and transportable.}
}
\]

The two kill conditions are:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\text{ is noncanonical / whitening-gauge dependent}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\text{ must vanish pointwise.}
}
\]

If either holds, the split architecture is just a repackaging of the old obstruction. 

The positive continuation is narrow:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Build a canonical } A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{-line connection and show Bottleneck-C line motion is transported, not killed.}
}
\]

---

## What to do next

Run a focused **line-bundle transport wave**. Do not attack source splitting, pure quotienting, or \(\nu=0\) again.

The next theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^L \lambda_{\eta\eta}
=
\text{controlled source/transport term}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Hol}(L,\nabla^L)
=
\text{global invariant incompatible with off-line zeros}.
}
\]

Concretely, we need to answer:

1. Is the whitening metric canonical enough globally?
2. Does \(\lambda_{\eta\eta}\) transform covariantly under patch/source/core changes?
3. Is the Bottleneck-C forcing term an allowed covariant acceleration in \(L\), or a fatal local defect?
4. Is there a global holonomy/index theorem for \(L\)?
5. Can the finite-core and interaction branches be expressed with \(D\) and \(\nabla^L\lambda\), rather than pointwise \(\lambda\)?

If the line-bundle transport theorem fails, the current architecture should be marked nonviable.

```text
on
\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S.
\]

2. Determine whether the whitening metric is canonical under:
   - patch changes;
   - source/core window changes;
   - fixed-sector basis changes;
   - positive-square-root branch choices;
   - Gram normalization choices;
   - scalar rescaling of the full odd germ.

3. Compute the transformation of
\[
\alpha_L
\]
under
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto\mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Verify whether
\[
\alpha_L\mapsto\alpha_L+d\log\mu
\]
or the appropriate Hermitian analogue holds.

4. Determine whether
\[
\nabla^L\lambda=d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L
\]
is covariant under this scaling.

5. Check whether non-conformal changes of the whitening metric change
\[
\lambda
\]
and
\[
\alpha_L
\]
in an uncontrolled way.

6. If the metric is not canonical globally, identify the exact obstruction and whether it can be fixed by:
   - normalizing \(\|A_5^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}=1\);
   - choosing a positive Gram-square-root branch;
   - restricting to a canonical good-patch atlas;
   - using the unnormalized section \(\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) instead of \(\lambda\).

7. Deliver one of:
   - a theorem proving \((L,\nabla^L)\) is canonical on good patches;
   - a conditional theorem with exact hypotheses;
   - a no-go showing the line connection is gauge-dependent.

Deliverable:
A transformation-law theorem or no-go for the line-bundle connection
\[
\nabla^L.
\]
```

# Agent 2 — Bottleneck-C longitudinal transport law

```text
\[

\[

The longitudinal projection is
\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=

\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.

   determine whether
\[

\]

\[

\[

=
\partial_\kappa\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa).

   - a forcing term in \(\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda\);

   - a second fundamental form;
   - or an uncancelled pointwise defect.

\[

=
F_{\eta\eta},
\]

6. If pointwise vanishing is still required, prove that split-readout Bottleneck C is equivalent to the old obstruction.

7. If nonzero forcing is allowed, formulate the replacement Bottleneck-C gate:
for example, a prescribed transport equation, holonomy constraint, or global boundary condition.

Deliverable:
```

# Agent 5 — Split interaction / feature and spectral control

```text
\[

=

\langle v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_i),v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_j)\rangle_{\mathrm{split}}.

\[

\quad\forall \sum_i a_i=0
\]
is equivalent to
\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_k).

\qquad

\qquad

obstruction survive?
```

# Agent 6 — Architecture synthesis / final decision

```text
You are Agent 6: Architecture Synthesis / Final Decision Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Synthesize the split-readout / line-bundle transport wave and decide whether the architecture is viable.

Tasks:
1. State the proposed architecture:
   - split scalar
\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}=(H_m^{\quot},H_m^{\parallel});
\]
   - line bundle
\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f};
\]
   - connection
\[
\nabla^L;
\]
   - finite-core vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}};
\]
   - interaction kernel
\[
K_{dd}^{\mathrm{split}}.
\]

2. List the theorem dependencies:
   - canonical whitening metric;
   - canonical line connection;
   - longitudinal Bottleneck-C transport law;
   - split finite-core non-concentration;
   - split interaction feature/spectral control;
   - global holonomy/boundary theorem if needed.

3. Define hard kill criteria:
   - if \(\lambda\) is noncanonical, kill split architecture;
   - if \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) must vanish pointwise, kill or downgrade;
   - if no line-bundle transport law exists, kill;
   - if split non-concentration is no easier than full vector and remains unsupported, downgrade;
   - if interaction countermodels survive, mark blocked.

4. Compare split architecture to:
   - old \(\Phi_K\)-scalar architecture;
   - pure quotient architecture;
   - curvature/holonomy architecture.

5. Decide the next action:
   - continue line-bundle transport;
   - return to full vector-valued fixed-sector proof;
   - attempt a new invariant;
   - or declare current architecture nonviable.

Deliverable:
A final decision memo with exact theorem dependencies and next-step recommendation.
```

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The split-readout wave reached a precise state:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The split readout is locally complete, but not yet a proof architecture.}
}
\]

It fixes the pure quotient blind spot by recording both

\[
D_{2r+1}
\]

and

\[
\lambda_{2r+1}.
\]

But if the longitudinal component \(\lambda\) must vanish pointwise, the old Bottleneck-C obstruction returns. The only possible continuation is a **line-bundle transport architecture**.

---

## 1. Positive result: split readout is locally complete

For

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S,
\]

define

\[
D(A)=\omega_h(A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]

and

\[
\lambda(A)
=
\frac{
\langle A,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Agent 1 and Agent 2 agree that on a good patch,

\[
\boxed{
(D(A),\lambda(A))\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad A.
}
\]

So the split readout

\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),
H_m^{\parallel}(s)
\right)
\]

is detection-complete for the fixed sector, assuming the whitening metric is canonical and nondegenerate. It repairs the quotient failure:

\[
H_m^{\quot}\equiv0
\not\Rightarrow
H_m\equiv0.
\]

The odd coefficients are

\[
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1}),
\]

and componentwise holomorphy/Cauchy sampling survives.  

---

## 2. Canonicity is conditional

The line connection candidate is

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Agent 1 in the latest wave confirmed the local gauge law:

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

implies

\[
\alpha_L\mapsto \alpha_L+d\log\mu,
\]

and

\[
\nabla^L\lambda
=
d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L
\]

transforms covariantly. 

But the whitening metric remains the condition:

\[
\boxed{
\lambda\text{ and }\alpha_L\text{ are canonical only if the whitening metric is canonical up to conformal rescaling on }\mathfrak f_h.
}
\]

If different allowed whitening/core/window choices induce non-conformal changes on \(\mathfrak f_h\), the split is only a gauge-fixed coordinate choice, not a global invariant.

---

## 3. Bottleneck C reappears through \(\lambda\)

Agent 3 computed the split projection of the bad row.

The active row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

Its longitudinal component is

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]

Agent 2 in the latest line-bundle wave confirmed that this is an **inhomogeneous forcing term** in the line component. It is not currently cancelled by the connection term

\[
\lambda\alpha_L(\partial_\kappa).
\]

So if the split architecture requires

\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})=0
\]

pointwise, then generically it again requires

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

That is the old obstruction.  

---

## 4. Holonomy/global transport is not yet available

Agent 3 in the line-bundle wave found no current replacement gate.

There is no established:

\[
\text{canonical path/cycle},
\]

no global boundary condition for \(\lambda\), and no theorem tying off-line zeros to line-bundle holonomy.

The natural holonomy

\[
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)
=
\exp\int_\Gamma \alpha_L
\]

is locally meaningful, but there is no canonical RH-relevant \(\Gamma\) and no theorem forcing prescribed holonomy. 

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{line-bundle holonomy is a coherent language, but not yet a proof gate.}
}
\]

---

## 5. Finite-core and interaction remain hard

Agent 4 found that split finite-core is essentially the full fixed-sector vector in better coordinates:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
=
(D_7,\lambda_7,D_9,\lambda_9,\ldots).
\]

Thus

\[
\mathcal Z_k^{\mathrm{split}}=\mathcal Z_k
\]

on a good patch, which is good for detection.

But sampled non-concentration remains:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{split}}
\]

is still a live formal obstruction. 

Agent 5 found the interaction branch also survives. The split feature curve

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)
\]

still requires feature balance, i.e.

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_1)=\cdots=v_{\mathrm{split}}(u_k),
\]

or spectral/cone control. The standard countermodels survive, including

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)=v_0+\varepsilon u^2w
\]

and the unit curve spectral obstruction

\[
v_{\mathrm{split}}(u)=(\cos(au+bu^3),\sin(au+bu^3)).
\]

So split readout improves detection but not the downstream hard analysis.

---

## 6. Current architecture status

Agent 6’s synthesis is correct:

\[
\boxed{
\text{split readout: algebraically complete, not a proof gate.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{line-bundle transport: only possible positive continuation.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{pointwise split closure: failed, because it returns to }E_{\eta\eta}=0.
}
\]

The decisive remaining theorem would have to say something like:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda_{\eta\eta}
=
\text{controlled covariant forcing}
}
\]

together with a global boundary/holonomy/index theorem showing that this forcing is compatible with RH detection.

Without that theorem, the split architecture is just the full fixed-sector architecture in canonical coordinates, and the original obstruction remains.

---

## Decision

Do **one final focused attack** only if we want to test line-bundle transport itself:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can } \lambda(E_{\eta\eta}) \text{ be an allowed forcing term in a global line-bundle transport equation?}
}
\]

The attack should not revisit source splitting, quotienting, or finite-core expansion. It should focus on:

1. Whether the whitening metric is globally canonical.
2. Whether \(\nabla^L\lambda\) is genuinely covariant.
3. Whether the \(\eta\eta\) forcing is exact/covariantly integrable.
4. Whether there is a canonical boundary/holonomy condition.
5. Whether off-line zeros force a contradiction in that transported line coordinate.

If this fails, the current RH proof program should be marked nonviable in its present family of architectures.
## User (2026-04-25 18:02:48)

OK give prompts for Agents 1-6

```text id="shared-line-transport-final"
=

}{

}.

E_{\eta\eta}

\]
one expects

\qquad

Last wave found:
- The line connection is locally coherent if the whitening metric is canonical.
- It is not yet globally proved canonical under patch/source/core/whitening changes.
- The Bottleneck-C longitudinal defect is an inhomogeneous forcing term.
- No canonical holonomy/path/boundary theorem is currently known.
- Split finite-core and interaction problems remain, but the final question is whether line transport can replace pointwise Bottleneck-C flatness.

This wave’s target:
Decide whether the line-bundle transport architecture can genuinely replace pointwise Bottleneck-C closure.

Do not:
```

```text id="agent2-covariant-bottleneck-c-forcing"
or
```

```text id="agent3-boundary-canonical-paths"
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)=1.
\]

6. Determine whether off-line zeros force nonzero transported line anomaly:
\[
\operatorname{Hol}_L(\Gamma)\neq1
\]
or nonzero endpoint mismatch.

7. If no canonical path/boundary exists, state the no-go.

Deliverable:
A global line-transport / holonomy architecture, or a no-go showing no canonical path/boundary theorem is currently available.
```

```text id="agent6-final-synthesis-line-bundle"
   - transported interaction branch.

   - global covariance of whitening metric;
   - line connection transition law;
   - covariant Bottleneck-C forcing equation;
   - exactness/boundary/holonomy control;
   - transported finite-core non-concentration;
   - transported interaction rigidity.

   - \(\lambda\) noncanonical;
   - \(\nabla^L\) non-covariant;
   - \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) must vanish pointwise;
   - no canonical path or boundary;
   - forcing not exact and not globally controlled;
   - transported finite-core loses anomaly detection;
   - interaction countermodels survive.

4. Decide whether the next step is:
   - continue line-bundle transport;
   - return to full vector-valued fixed-sector proof;
   - invent a different invariant;
   - or declare the current proof architecture nonviable.

5. Be explicit about what would count as a positive result:
   one concrete theorem that makes nonzero longitudinal Bottleneck-C forcing acceptable.
```

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The final line-bundle transport wave is negative.

The line-bundle formulation is locally coherent, but it does **not** currently give a viable proof architecture.

The key result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Bottleneck-C longitudinal defect is covariant as a local line-valued forcing term, but it is not globally controlled.}
}
\]

So the architecture still collapses back to pointwise Bottleneck-C vanishing unless we introduce a new global transport theorem that is not presently available.

---

## 1. Local connection works, global covariance is missing

Agent 1 confirmed the positive local fact. For

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

the candidate connection

\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
\]

has the correct local frame transformation:

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto gA_5^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\alpha_L\mapsto \alpha_L+d\log g.
\]

Thus

\[
\nabla^L\lambda=d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L
\]

is locally covariant. 

But global covariance requires two unproved facts:

\[
A_{5,j}^{\mathfrak f}=g_{ij}A_{5,i}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

on patch overlaps, and conformal compatibility of the whitened fixed-sector metric:

\[
\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\wh,j}
=
\rho_{ij}\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\wh,i}
\]

on \(\mathfrak f_h\).

If source/core/whitening transitions rotate \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) to a genuinely different line or change the metric non-conformally, then \(\lambda\) and \(\alpha_L\) acquire non-tensorial corrections. 

So the line-bundle connection is valid only on a fixed good patch with fixed conventions.

---

## 2. Bottleneck-C forcing is covariant locally, but not harmless

Agent 2 found that the bad row defines a covariant line-valued forcing section.

The bad row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS).
\]

Its longitudinal forcing is

\[
s_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}
A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

This is the correct covariant object: the scalar coordinate rescales under a change of line frame, while the section \(s_{\eta\eta}\) is invariant. 

But this only packages the defect. It does not remove it.

A forced equation such as

\[
\nabla_\kappa^L\lambda
=
F_{\eta\eta}
\]

would need global boundary, holonomy, exactness, or index control. No such theorem is present. Without it, the local architecture still requires

\[
s_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

which generically returns to

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]

---

## 3. No canonical path, boundary, or holonomy gate exists

Agent 3 found no canonical global path or cycle that could turn the line forcing into a useful holonomy theorem.

Candidate paths exist formally:

\[
[m_i,m_{i+1}],
\]

\(\kappa\)-paths, source-window loops, core deformation cycles, and Gram/whitening loops. But none currently supplies all three required ingredients:

\[
\text{canonical path/cycle},
\]

\[
\text{endpoint or holonomy boundary condition},
\]

\[
\text{theorem linking off-line zeros to nontrivial holonomy}.
\]

Midpoint intervals are natural, but they are not cycles and lack endpoint conditions for \(\lambda\). Source/window and Gram loops are not canonical without the missing covariance theorem. 

Thus line-bundle holonomy is a coherent language, not a proof gate.

---

## 4. Longitudinal forcing is not exact

Agent 4 tested the best possible exactness route.

With

\[
A=A_2^{\new},
\qquad
q=q_0^{\new},
\qquad
K=\frac{q''}{6}-\frac{2q^3}{3},
\]

the obstruction has the scaled form

\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
qAA''
+
20KA^2.
\]

The old integration-by-parts obstruction survives after multiplying by the longitudinal projection factor

\[
\Gamma_5/q^3.
\]

The longitudinal forcing decomposes into a covariant derivative plus bulk terms, including

\[
-\frac{\Gamma_5}{q^2}(A')^2
\]

and

\[
\frac{\Gamma_5}{q^3}
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A^2,
\]

plus transport multiplier terms. These do not vanish or become exact under the current line connection. 

So

\[
F_{\eta\eta}\neq \nabla^L\Psi
\]

for the natural local potentials tested.

This kills the “maybe it is a boundary term” route.

---

## 5. Transported finite-core does not improve downstream problems

Agent 5 found that replacing \(\lambda\) by

\[
\nabla^L\lambda
\]

is incomplete: it misses covariantly constant line anomalies unless anchor or boundary data are added.

So a transported finite-core object would need something like

\[
(D,\ R^L=\nabla^L\lambda-F^L,\ \lambda_{\rm boundary/holonomy}).
\]

That is a new global transport program, not a local proof. 

Moreover, even with transport, the old sampled non-concentration and \(dd\)-interaction countermodels survive:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{tr}}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\mathrm{tr}},
\]

and feature/spectral countermodels remain available.

So transport does not simplify finite-core or interaction; it only shifts the longitudinal coordinate into a global boundary/anchor problem.

---

## 6. Final decision

Agent 6’s synthesis is correct:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The line-bundle transport architecture is coherent as a final diagnostic, but not viable as a proof architecture.}
}
\]

A positive result would have required a theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\begin{minipage}{0.86\linewidth}
On the good-patch atlas, \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) carries a canonical global connection. The Bottleneck-C longitudinal contribution satisfies a covariant transport equation whose forcing is globally controlled by a boundary, holonomy, exactness, or index law. Therefore nonzero \(\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})\) is prescribed transport rather than local failure.
\end{minipage}
}
\]

The agents found none of the necessary components:

\[
\boxed{\text{global covariance: missing}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{canonical path/boundary: missing}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{exactness: false in current variables}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{finite-core/interaction simplification: absent}}
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If no new external idea enters, the current family of architectures should be marked nonviable.}
}
\]

---

## Current proof-state ledger

We have now exhausted the main architecture family:

\[
\text{pointwise }T\text{-horizontal Bottleneck C}
\]

failed due to the \(S\)-visible \(\eta\eta\) row.

\[
\text{source rebuild}
\]

reproduced the same obstruction.

\[
\text{pure quotient}
\]

lost \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies.

\[

\]

restored completeness but reintroduced the obstruction.

\[

\]

made the longitudinal defect locally covariant but not globally controlled.

The clean conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{This RH proof route is blocked at the local-to-global fixed-sector architecture level.}
}
\]

The remaining viable future work is not another patch of this architecture. It would require a genuinely new invariant or proof mechanism outside the current scalar/quotient/split/line-bundle family.

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:12:29)

_Thought for 8s_

Yes: **keep Gate A and Gate B, but downgrade their role.**

They are no longer “the route to RH.” They become **validated local algebraic lemmas** that any future route may reuse. The problem is not that Gate A/B were wrong; the problem is that the architecture downstream of them kept forcing an impossible or unsupported fixed-sector closure condition.

The failure point is now sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B local algebra can close, but the fixed-sector local-to-global readout cannot.}
}
\]

The latest line-bundle wave showed that the final attempted repair made the longitudinal \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line defect locally covariant but not globally controlled. There is no canonical global connection/holonomy/boundary theorem, the forcing is not exact, and transported finite-core/interaction branches do not simplify.    

So I would keep:

\[
\boxed{\text{Gate A as a local aggregate-cancellation lemma.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Gate B as a conditional local algebra / quotient-line lemma.}}
\]

But I would **stop treating Bottleneck C as the natural next gate**.

---

## What the new invariant might need to be

The next invariant cannot be any of these alone:

\[
\Phi_K
\]

because it sees the \(S\)-row and forces the bad \(T\)-flatness condition.

\[
H_m^{\quot}
\]

because it misses pure \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies.

\[
(H_m^{\quot},H_m^\parallel)
\]

because it restores completeness but reintroduces the same Bottleneck-C obstruction unless one has a global line-transport theorem.

So the new invariant must avoid the trap:

\[
\boxed{
\text{complete enough to detect RH-relevant anomalies, but not requiring pointwise fixed-sector flattening.}
}
\]

That suggests several directions.

---

# 1. Use a global index, not a local vanishing gate

The most natural replacement is an **index-type invariant**.

Instead of asking:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
f=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

ask whether the local obstruction contributes to a global index:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Index}
=
\sum_{\text{patches}}
\operatorname{sgn}(\text{local fixed-sector defect})
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Index}
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}\int d\log \mathcal I
}
\]

for some globally defined \(\mathcal I\).

Why this might work: the local obstruction kept refusing to vanish pointwise. That may mean pointwise vanishing is the wrong ask. But a sign/winding/counting invariant might still be globally constrained.

What to test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can }E_{\eta\eta}\text{ or }\nu_{\eta\eta}\text{ be interpreted as a local index density?}
}
\]

This is different from the exactness/residue attacks already run. Those asked whether \(\nu\) itself was exact or residue-killed. Here the object would be a **sign, winding, Maslov index, or spectral-flow contribution** built from the fixed-sector family.

Possible invariant names/structures:

\[
\text{Maslov index}
\]

\[
\text{spectral flow}
\]

\[
\text{winding of a determinant line}
\]

\[
\text{intersection number of fixed-sector curve with a discriminant}
\]

This is probably the best conceptual pivot.

---

# 2. Replace fixed-sector scalarization with a determinant-line spectral flow

The fixed-sector data live in

\[
\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S.
\]

Every scalarization we tried chose either:

\[
\Phi_K(A)
\]

or

\[
\omega_h(A,A_5)
\]

or the split pair \((D,\lambda)\).

A new invariant could instead track the **motion of the whole line**:

\[
\ell_r(m):=\mathbf C A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\in \mathbf P(\mathfrak f_h).
\]

Then compare it to

\[
\ell_5(m):=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

The quotient determinant

\[
D_{2r+1}=\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]

detects intersection of these projective lines. It failed because it ignores scale along the line. But a projective **path invariant** could still matter:

\[
m\mapsto [A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)]\in \mathbf P^1.
\]

Then RH could be attacked via:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zeros force projective winding / crossing}
}
\]

versus

\[
\boxed{
\text{global zeta symmetry forbids that winding / crossing.}
}
\]

This avoids demanding pointwise vanishing of either quotient or longitudinal components.

What to test:

\[
\operatorname{Wind}\left([A_{7}^{\mathfrak f}(m)],[A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)]\right)
\]

or

\[
\operatorname{Cross}\left(\ell_7,\ell_5\right).
\]

This is close to the quotient geometry but upgraded from a pointwise determinant to a **global projective motion invariant**.

---

# 3. Use the full vector-valued germ and avoid scalar gates

Another possibility is to stop scalarizing entirely.

The natural object is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s;m)
=
\sum_{r\ge0} A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r+1}
\in \mathfrak f_h.
}
\]

The scalar gates failed because every scalar projection either loses data or exposes a fatal local component. A vector-valued analytic proof might use:

\[
\|\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}\|^2,
\]

or vector-valued interpolation, or a two-component zero theorem.

Caution: \(\|\cdot\|^2\) is not holomorphic. But componentwise holomorphic vector-valued sampling is possible.

The replacement theorem would be something like:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv0
\Rightarrow
\text{finite vector sample cannot be too small}
}
\]

without choosing \(\Phi_K\), quotient, or line coordinate as the privileged gate.

This reuses Gate A/B as local expansion tools, but the endgame becomes vector-valued finite-core non-concentration rather than Bottleneck-C scalar closure.

Problem: the agents already found split finite-core non-concentration is essentially the full-vector problem and remains hard. So this is coherent, but not obviously easier.

---

# 4. Move from local diagonal merger to an energy/positivity inequality

Bottleneck C tried to force a local merger condition. The obstruction may indicate that the right local-to-global statement is not equality but inequality.

A replacement could be an energy:

\[
\mathcal E(m)
=
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\wedge A_5^{\mathfrak f}\|^2
+
\|\operatorname{proj}_{A_5}A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|^2
\]

or more generally

\[
\mathcal E(m)
=
\sum_r w_r\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|^2.
\]

Then the bad \(\eta\eta\) row might become a positive contribution rather than an obstruction.

What to test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the } \eta\eta \text{ row have a sign in an energy norm?}
}
\]

This is different from previous spectral cone tests, which focused on \(dd\)-interaction kernels. Here the question is whether the fixed-sector Bottleneck-C defect contributes with a useful sign to a global energy.

Possible theorem shape:

\[
\text{off-line zeros}
\Rightarrow
\mathcal E(m)>0,
\]

but

\[
\text{global xi symmetry / phase constraints}
\Rightarrow
\mathcal E(m)=0
\]

or an integral contradiction.

This is promising only if the energy can be tied to zero geometry and not just be nonnegative tautologically.

---

# 5. Use a relative monodromy / connection on the full fixed-sector bundle

The line-bundle \(L=\mathbf C A_5\) was too narrow and lacked global covariance. A more natural object may be the full rank-two fixed-sector bundle:

\[
\mathcal F \to \mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_m=\mathfrak f_h(m).
\]

Instead of trying to define a connection only on \(L\), define a connection on \(\mathcal F\), with \(A_5\) as a section. Then the obstruction is not a defect of a line coordinate but part of the full connection matrix:

\[
\nabla A_5,\qquad
\nabla A_7.
\]

The invariant could be the curvature trace/determinant of this rank-two connection:

\[
\operatorname{tr}F_\nabla,
\qquad
\det F_\nabla,
\qquad
\operatorname{Hol}_\nabla.
\]

Why this may work: the line-bundle failed because \(A_5\)-line transitions were not canonical. A rank-two bundle may transform naturally even when the line rotates. Then line motion is not a gauge defect; it is part of the connection.

This is a strong candidate.

The new object:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\text{ on the full fixed-sector bundle}
}
\]

instead of

\[
\nabla^L\text{ on } \mathbf C A_5.
\]

Then ask:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Is the Bottleneck-C } \eta\eta \text{ row a component of }F_{\nabla^{\mathfrak f}}?
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does global zeta geometry constrain }\operatorname{Hol}(\nabla^{\mathfrak f})?
}
\]

This avoids the need for \(A_5\)-line preservation across patches.

---

# 6. Move the proof away from fixed-sector \(A_5,A_7\) entirely

The harshest conclusion is that the fixed-sector odd-germ architecture is the wrong invariant family.

Then Gate A/B may still be useful as local algebra, but the proof should pivot to a different geometric object, for example:

### Pair-correlation / de Branges space structure

Use the Hilbert space/kernel positivity more directly, avoiding local diagonal-merger coordinates.

### Canonical system / Hamiltonian

RH is equivalent to positivity/de Branges-type properties in some formulations. If your kernel construction is close to a canonical system, the right invariant may be the Hamiltonian or transfer matrix, not the fixed-sector \(T\)-coordinate.

### Total positivity / ECT global structure

A lot of your current machinery mentions ECT, finite-core determinacy, and projective curves. A more plausible route might be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zeros violate extended complete Chebyshev / total positivity globally}
}
\]

without requiring Bottleneck-C local \(T\)-flatness.

This would preserve some finite-core work but change the local gate.

---

## Do we keep Gate A and Gate B?

Yes, but with careful labels.

### Keep Gate A as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A: local aggregate cancellation / homogeneous-grade closure.}
}
\]

It is useful local algebra. It tells us the first obstruction is not there.

### Keep Gate B as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B: conditional local quotient/fixed-sector algebra through order 7.}
}
\]

But do **not** say Gate B proves the local package closes physically. We now know the actual physical closure gets stuck at the \(S\)-visible \(\eta\eta\) row and its descendants.

I would write:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B are validated local reductions, not sufficient gates for the proof.}
}
\]

They become **lemmas feeding future architectures**, not the main proof skeleton.

---

## My top two next ideas

### Idea A: full rank-two fixed-sector connection

This is the best next mathematical object.

Instead of scalar \(\Phi_K\), quotient \(D\), split \((D,\lambda)\), or line connection \(L\), define a connection on the full fixed-sector bundle

\[
\mathfrak f_h.
\]

Then the obstruction may become a coordinate component of a globally meaningful curvature. This directly addresses the failure of the line-bundle approach: the line was not stable enough, but the full plane may be.

Prompt target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Construct }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\text{ and test whether }E_{\eta\eta}\text{ is a curvature component.}
}
\]

### Idea B: projective/spectral-flow invariant of the fixed-sector curve

Track

\[
m\mapsto [A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)],\quad [A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)]
\]

as projective curves, and look for winding/intersection/monodromy.

Prompt target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does an off-line zero force nontrivial projective monodromy?}
}
\]

This might avoid pointwise vanishing while preserving quotient geometry.

---

## Bottom line

The missing invariant probably is **not a scalar**.

It is likely one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a rank-two fixed-sector connection/holonomy}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a projective spectral-flow / Maslov-type index}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{a vector-valued energy/positivity invariant}
}
\]

And yes: keep Gate A and Gate B, but demote them to local algebraic lemmas. The future proof must not pass through pointwise Bottleneck-C \(T\)-flatness.

```text
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R},
\]
the aggregate obstruction coefficient is
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\agg}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right],
\]
with
\[
A_2^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4^{\new}=\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The current \(T\)-horizontal Bottleneck-C architecture requires
\[
f=0,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]
Since the active row has
\[
f_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{\eta\eta},
\]
physical local closure requires
\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0
\]
on a good patch.

Prior repair attempts failed:

- source rebuild reproduces the obstruction;
- one-pair source locking fails;
- global pointwise ODE/exactness/residue routes fail;
- \(\Theta_\pm\) coordinates and counterterms merely move the obstruction;
- pure quotient \(H_m^{\quot}\) misses \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies;
- split readout \((D,\lambda)\) is locally complete but reintroduces the obstruction;
- line-bundle \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) transport is locally coherent but lacks global covariance, canonical paths, boundary data, exactness, and holonomy control;
- finite-core sampled non-concentration and \(dd\)-interaction feature/spectral rigidity remain unresolved in full, quotient, and split variables.

Conclusion so far:
The current family of scalar / quotient / split / line-bundle Bottleneck-C architectures is nonviable unless a new external invariant is introduced.

Important strategic reset:

Keep Gate A and Gate B only as local algebraic lemmas:
\[
\boxed{\text{Gate A/B are useful reductions, not sufficient proof gates.}}
\]

Do not attempt another Bottleneck-C repair. Do not try to prove \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\) directly unless your prompt explicitly asks for a comparison. Do not introduce another scalar readout of the same fixed-sector defect.

This wave tests three new invariant families:

1. A rank-two fixed-sector connection on the whole bundle
\[
\mathcal F_m=\mathfrak f_h(m)=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S.
\]

2. A projective / spectral-flow / Maslov-type invariant of the projective fixed-sector curves
\[
m\mapsto [A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)],
\qquad
m\mapsto [A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)].
\]

3. A vector-valued energy / positivity / total-positivity invariant using the full fixed-sector odd germ
\[
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s;m)
=
\sum_r A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r+1}.
\]

Your task is to determine whether one of these invariant families can replace pointwise Bottleneck-C \(T\)-flatness.
```

# Agent 1 — Rank-two fixed-sector connection constructor

```text
You are Agent 1: Rank-Two Fixed-Sector Connection Constructor.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Construct a candidate connection on the full rank-two fixed-sector bundle
\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_m=\mathfrak f_h(m)=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S,
\]
instead of the failed line bundle
\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Motivation:
The line-bundle approach failed partly because the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line may rotate under patch/source/core/whitening changes. A full rank-two connection may remain meaningful even when the line is not preserved.

Tasks:
1. Identify the natural base \(\mathcal B\):
   - midpoint \(m\);
   - collision parameter \(\kappa\);
   - source/core window;
   - Gram/whitening data;
   - finite-core parameter \(\theta\);
   - or a reduced good-patch base.

2. Define the fibre:
\[
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b).
\]

3. Identify the natural trivializations:
\[
I_b,\quad S_b,
\]
and determine how they transform across good patches.

4. Construct a candidate connection
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]
on \(\mathcal F\), using one of:
   - Gram/whitening transport;
   - orthogonal projection from the ambient kernel/jet bundle;
   - the finite-\(s\) transform state;
   - the Cauchy/jet basis transport;
   - another canonical construction in the draft.

5. Compute how \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\), \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\), and the bad row
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
transform under \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\).

6. Determine whether \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is a component of:
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
F_{\nabla^{\mathfrak f}},
\qquad
\text{second fundamental form},
\qquad
\text{torsion/curvature of }\mathcal F.
\]

7. Decide whether the rank-two connection avoids the line-bundle covariance defect.

8. If it is viable, state the exact connection theorem.
If it is not viable, identify the first obstruction.

Deliverable:
A candidate rank-two fixed-sector connection \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\), its transformation laws, and a verdict on whether the Bottleneck-C defect becomes a globally meaningful connection/curvature component.
```

# Agent 3 — Projective spectral-flow / Maslov index agent

```text
You are Agent 3: Projective Spectral-Flow / Maslov Index Agent.

Objects:
\[

\]
\[
\ell_7(m):=[A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)]\in\mathbf P(\mathfrak f_h),

and more generally
\[
\ell_{2r+1}(m):=[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)].
\]

\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
\]
as an intersection/transversality condition:
\[
D_{2r+1}=0
\iff
\ell_{2r+1}=\ell_5.
\]

\[
\ell_{2r+1}=\ell_5
\]
with nonzero scale.

4. Define candidate global invariants:
   - winding of \(\ell_7\) around \(\ell_5\);
   - intersection number of \(\ell_7\) with \(\ell_5\);
   - Maslov index of the path \(\ell_r(m)\);
   - spectral flow of the pair \((A_5,A_7)\);
   - projective monodromy of the fixed-sector curve.

5. Determine whether the Bottleneck-C bad row changes projective direction, line scale, or both.

6. Check whether off-line zeros force nontrivial projective winding/intersection.

7. Check whether global zeta symmetry or endpoint conditions force the projective index to vanish.

8. If projective index cannot see pure line anomalies, decide whether it must be paired with a scale/energy invariant.

A candidate projective/Maslov/spectral-flow invariant and a verdict on whether it can replace Bottleneck-C local \(T\)-flatness.
```

```text
=

=
```
```text
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2,

=
\sum_r w_r\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2.

E_{\eta\eta}
=

\]
to the first variation or second variation of the energy.

or a monotonicity/convexity statement.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:25:46)

_Thought for 6s_

## Coordinator readout

The new-invariant wave did not produce a proof gate yet, but it identified the **least-bad next architecture**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two fixed-sector connection on } \mathcal F_m=\mathfrak f_h(m).
}
\]

Everything else is either incomplete or equivalent to an already-failed branch.

The key shift is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{stop choosing scalar / quotient / line coordinates; track the full fixed-sector plane.}
}
\]

---

## 1. Rank-two fixed-sector connection is the best next object

Agent 1’s result is the most important. The rank-two bundle

\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus \mathbf C S_b
\]

avoids the fatal line-bundle defect. The \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line may rotate under patch/source/core changes, but the full plane can still transform by a \(GL_2\)-transition.

A local connection can be constructed by projecting the ambient jet/kernel derivative:

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f} A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}\widetilde A).
\]

In a local frame \(E=(I,S)\),

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f} A
=
d
\begin{pmatrix}
a_I\\
a_S
\end{pmatrix}
+
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
\begin{pmatrix}
a_I\\
a_S
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If the frame comes from whitening \(E=E^{\rm raw}W\), then formally:

\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}=W^{-1}dW
\]

when the raw frame is fixed. 

The Bottleneck-C row becomes a clean vector-valued section:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in \Gamma(\mathcal F).
\]

That is better than every scalarization tried so far.

But this is still conditional. We need a theorem that the planes \(\mathfrak f_h(b)\) form a canonical rank-two bundle over the good-patch atlas, with canonical \(GL_2\)-transition maps. 

---

## 2. The bad row is not ordinary curvature

Agent 2 clarified that the row is not standard curvature.

Ordinary curvature is antisymmetric:

\[
F_{\nabla^{\mathfrak f}}(X,Y).
\]

But the active row is symmetric in source directions:

\[
\eta_i\eta_j.
\]

So

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
\]

is better classified as a **symmetric source-Hessian forcing / second fundamental form component**, not as a usual curvature two-form. 

The replacement equation would therefore be affine/forced transport, not flatness:

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f} A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}
+
\text{controlled lower terms}.
\]

A rank-two proof would need a global theorem controlling this forced transport. Ordinary trace curvature, determinant curvature, or homogeneous holonomy does not directly control a vector-valued inhomogeneous forcing term. 

So the rank-two route is promising as a **language**, but not yet a proof.

---

## 3. Projective/Maslov alone is incomplete

Agent 3’s projective result is useful but negative as a standalone route.

The quotient determinant is exactly projective incidence:

\[
D_{2r+1}=0
\iff
[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_5^{\mathfrak f}].
\]

So projective geometry recovers the quotient story.

Its failure is the same as the quotient failure: pure line anomalies

\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

are projectively invisible but still \(T\)- and \(\Phi_K\)-visible. 

Therefore a projective/Maslov invariant cannot be sufficient by itself. It needs a scale/energy/rank-two companion.

Best use:

\[
\boxed{
\text{projective spectral flow as a derived invariant of the rank-two connection, not as the main object.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Vector-valued germ is complete but not new enough

Agent 4 confirmed that the full vector-valued fixed-sector odd germ is the cleanest complete local object:

\[
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s;m)
=
\sum_{r\ge0} A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r+1}
\in \mathfrak f_h.
\]

It preserves holomorphy, parity, Cauchy recovery, and finite determinacy componentwise. 

But it is equivalent to the split/full fixed-sector formulation on good patches. It does not remove the key hard theorem:

\[
\theta(m)\notin\mathcal Z_k^{\vec f}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\vec f}
\Rightarrow
\|P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}+J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\vec f}(m,Q).
\]

The aligned branch remains:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}.
\]

So the vector-valued germ should be the **section** of the rank-two bundle, but not the proof mechanism by itself. 

---

## 5. Energy/positivity did not work

Agent 5 tested natural energies such as

\[
\mathcal E_7=\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2
\]

and

\[
\mathcal E_{\odd}=\sum_r \omega_r\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2.
\]

The bad row is detected, but not usefully.

For

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=\gamma(wI+uS),
\]

the first variation

\[
\delta\mathcal E_7
=
2\operatorname{Re}\left[
\gamma\langle A_7^{\mathfrak f},wI+uS\rangle_{\wh}
\right]
\]

is sign-indefinite. The second variation is positive, but tautological:

\[
\delta^2\mathcal E_7
=
2|\gamma|^2\|wI+uS\|_{\wh}^2\ge0.
\]

There is no global theorem forcing the energy to vanish, no monotonicity formula, and no endpoint condition. 

So energy is descriptive, not a proof gate.

---

## 6. Gate A and Gate B status

Keep them, but demote them.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A remains a local aggregate-cancellation lemma.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate B remains a conditional local quotient/fixed-sector algebra lemma.}
}
\]

They should feed the rank-two/vector-valued local expansion. They should no longer be presented as sufficient gates for the proof.

The failure is downstream:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the fixed-sector local-to-global readout architecture failed.}
}
\]

---

## 7. Recommended next wave

Run a **rank-two fixed-sector connection wave**, not another Bottleneck-C repair.

The exact targets should be:

### Theorem 1 — Fixed-sector bundle theorem

\[
\boxed{
\{\mathfrak f_h(b)\}_{b\in\mathcal B}
\text{ forms a canonical rank-two analytic bundle } \mathcal F\to\mathcal B.
}
\]

### Theorem 2 — Connection theorem

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal F
\text{ carries a canonical connection }
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ induced by corrected whitening / jet transport.}
}
\]

### Theorem 3 — Forcing tensor theorem

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}
\text{ is a tensorial symmetric source-Hessian / second fundamental form component of }
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
}
\]

### Theorem 4 — Global affine transport theorem

Something of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
}
\]

with a global boundary / holonomy / index / affine-displacement law.

Without Theorem 4, the rank-two route is only diagnostic.

---

## Bottom line

The best next idea is not a new scalar invariant. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{full rank-two fixed-sector affine transport.}
}
\]

Projective index and energy may become derived tools after the rank-two bundle/connection is built.

The next attack should answer:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the nonzero }E_{\eta\eta}\text{ be globally controlled as a vector-valued affine forcing term?}
}
\]

If not, this proof family is likely exhausted.

```text id="shared-rank-two-affine-transport"
\in \mathfrak f_h.

\[

-

(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].

Earlier routes failed:
- old \(\Phi_K\)-scalar is complete enough but forces bad pointwise \(T\)-flatness;
- pure quotient scalar \(H_m^{\quot}\) is invariant but misses \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies;
- split readout \((D,\lambda)\) is locally complete but reintroduces the obstruction through \(\lambda\);
```

# Agent 1 — Fixed-sector bundle and transition theorem

```text id="agent1-fixed-sector-bundle"
over the good-patch base.
```

# Agent 2 — Canonical rank-two connection construction


```text id="agent6-rank-two-synthesis"
   - specialize to projective/energy derived invariants;

   - or declare the current proof family nonviable.
```
