## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:31:58)

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The rank-two wave produced the clearest architectural state so far:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The rank-two fixed-sector bundle is the best remaining language, but not yet a proof route.}
}
\]

It improves on scalar, quotient, split, and line-bundle approaches because it treats

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]

as a full vector-valued section of

\[
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus \mathbf C S_b,
\]

rather than forcing it into a defective scalar coordinate. But the agents did **not** find the global affine transport theorem needed to make nonzero \(E_{\eta\eta}\) acceptable. 

---

## 1. Local rank-two bundle: yes

On a fixed good patch with fixed source/core/whitening conventions, the fixed-sector planes form a local analytic rank-two bundle:

\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B_{\rm loc},
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b).
\]

The frame

\[
(I_b,S_b)
\]

varies analytically, and fixed-sector coefficients such as

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad E_{\eta\eta}
\]

are local analytic sections. 

This is a real improvement over the line-bundle attempt: the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line may rotate, but the full plane can still be tracked.

---

## 2. Global bundle theorem: still missing

The first hard dependency is now:

\[
\boxed{
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C)
}
\]

on good-patch overlaps, with \(G_{ij}\) canonical and satisfying the cocycle condition.

The unresolved issue is source/core/whitening transitions. If changing source/core convention changes the object being studied rather than merely its coordinates, then the fixed-sector planes are not charts of one global bundle. If whitening changes are noncanonical, the resulting \(GL_2\) transition is bookkeeping, not geometry. 

So the next theorem is not about RH yet. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{fixed-sector atlas theorem.}
}
\]

---

## 3. Local connection: conditionally available

A natural local connection is:

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f} A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\bigl(d_X^{\mathcal J} A\bigr).
\]

In a local frame \(E=(I,S)\),

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A
=
d
\begin{pmatrix}
a_I\\
a_S
\end{pmatrix}
+
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
\begin{pmatrix}
a_I\\
a_S
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

If

\[
E=E^{\rm raw}W,
\]

then

\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W+W^{-1}dW.
\]

The connection has the correct transition law if the \(GL_2\) transitions exist:

\[
\Gamma_j
=
G_{ij}^{-1}\Gamma_iG_{ij}
+
G_{ij}^{-1}dG_{ij}.
\]

But canonicity is conditional on the ambient derivative, projection, whitening, and source/core conventions being functorial. 

---

## 4. The Bottleneck-C row becomes tensorial forcing

Assuming the bundle/connection exists, the bad row is a tensorial section:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}\in \Gamma(\mathcal F).
\]

This is the best conceptual gain of the rank-two formulation.

But the row is **not ordinary curvature**. Ordinary curvature is antisymmetric:

\[
F_{\nabla^{\mathfrak f}}(X,Y).
\]

The active row is symmetric in source directions \(\eta_i\eta_j\), so it is better classified as:

\[
\boxed{
\text{symmetric source-Hessian / second fundamental form / affine forcing.}
}
\]

The local equation should therefore be affine:

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f} A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

This is coherent, but it does not close the proof. If the local gate still requires zero forcing, then

\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]

which returns to

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0
\]

on a good patch. 

---

## 5. Global affine transport theorem: missing

Agent 4’s result is the decisive negative part.

If

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A=E,
\]

then along a path \(\Gamma:a\to b\),

\[
A(b)
=
U_\Gamma A(a)
+
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt.
\]

For this to become a proof gate, we need one of:

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical boundary values for }A(a),A(b),
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{canonical path/cycle }\Gamma,
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{path-independent affine displacement,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{global zeta constraint on affine holonomy/displacement,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zero } \Rightarrow \text{ nonzero affine displacement.}
}
\]

None is currently available. Midpoint intervals are natural but have no endpoint conditions. Zero-counting contours are not yet connected to the fixed-sector bundle. Source-window and Gram loops are convention-dependent unless the bundle/connection covariance theorem is proved first. 

So the rank-two architecture is still diagnostic, not proof-closing.

---

## 6. Projective and energy invariants are secondary

Projective/Maslov data recover the quotient determinant geometry:

\[
D_{2r+1}=0
\iff
[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_5^{\mathfrak f}].
\]

That makes them useful for crossings and incidence, but they are incomplete because pure line anomalies remain projectively invisible. They need scale/energy/rank-two data as a companion. 

Energy also does not close the route. Natural energies like

\[
\mathcal E_7=\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2
\]

detect the bad row, but the first variation is sign-indefinite and the second variation is only tautologically positive. There is no global zero-energy or monotonicity theorem. 

Thus projective and energy tools should be treated as derived diagnostics of a future rank-two transport system, not as the main route.

---

## 7. Current proof-state update

We now have a clear ladder:

### Local algebra retained

\[
\boxed{\text{Gate A: local aggregate-cancellation lemma.}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{Gate B: conditional local quotient/fixed-sector algebra lemma.}}
\]

These remain useful, but not proof-closing.

### Failed architectures

\[
\boxed{\Phi_K\text{-scalar Bottleneck C}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{pure quotient}}
\]

\[
\boxed{\text{split readout}}
\]

\[
\boxed{A_5\text{-line bundle transport}}
\]

### Best remaining architecture

\[
\boxed{\text{rank-two fixed-sector affine transport}}
\]

but only if it gets a global theorem.

---

## 8. Recommended next attack

The next wave should be **extremely narrow**. Do not ask for more scalar or quotient repairs.

Attack this theorem first:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-sector atlas theorem:}
\quad
\mathfrak f_h(b)
\text{ forms a canonical rank-two analytic bundle over the good-patch atlas.}
}
\]

Concretely, agents should answer:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do all admissible source/core/whitening transitions induce canonical }GL_2\text{ transitions on }\mathfrak f_h?
}
\]

If yes, proceed to:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Connection theorem:}
\quad
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A=\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\text{ is globally canonical.}
}
\]

If that succeeds, then attack:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Affine transport theorem:}
\quad
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E_{\eta\eta}(t)\,dt
\text{ is globally constrained or index-detecting.}
}
\]

If the fixed-sector atlas theorem fails, the current proof family should be marked nonviable.

Below are six prompts for the **fixed-sector atlas theorem wave**. This wave is intentionally narrow. It should decide whether the rank-two architecture has a globally meaningful object to work with.

The last wave showed that rank-two fixed-sector affine transport is the best remaining language, but still conditional: locally \(\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus \mathbf C S\) is a clean rank-two bundle, and \(E_{\eta\eta}\) is naturally a section; globally we still need canonical \(GL_2\)-transition maps across patch/source/core/whitening changes. If that atlas theorem fails, the rank-two route collapses into another local coordinate formalism.

# Shared background for all six agents

```text
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft.

Current accepted local algebra:
1. Gate A is aggregate-closed under the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention.
2. Gate B is conditionally closed through ordinary order 7 at the formal/quotient-local level.
3. The \(M_A,M_C\) connection-table branch is conditionally closed under source-grade reflection and the corrected mixed-block swap.
4. Mixed four-point quotient closure is valid at the determinant/scalar-exit layer.

However, the downstream Bottleneck-C / fixed-sector local-to-global architecture has failed in every scalarized form.

The active obstruction is the \(S\)-visible \(\eta\eta\) top row:
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h.
\]

The old \(T\)-horizontal architecture required pointwise vanishing:
\[
f=0,
\qquad
\partial_\kappa T=-a_1^2f/c.
\]
Since
\[
f_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{u}{24\pi q^3}\nu_{\eta\eta},
\]
the old gate effectively required
\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0
\]
on a good patch.

Prior routes failed:
- source rebuild \(G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}\) reproduces the obstruction;
- one-pair source locking fails;
- ODE / exactness / residue attacks do not prove pointwise \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\);
- \(\Theta_\pm\) and counterterms merely move the obstruction;
- pure quotient \(H_m^{\quot}\) misses \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies;
- split readout \((D,\lambda)\) is locally complete but reintroduces the obstruction;
- line-bundle \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is locally coherent but lacks global covariance, canonical paths, boundary data, exactness, and holonomy control;
- vector-valued fixed-sector germ is complete but equivalent to full fixed-sector/split data and does not solve non-concentration or interaction;
- projective/Maslov data are useful but incomplete because pure line anomalies are projectively invisible;
- energy/positivity detects the row but has sign-indefinite first variation and no global zero-energy theorem.

The best remaining architecture is:
\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

The rank-two architecture treats
\[
E_{\eta\eta}\in\Gamma(\mathcal F)
\]
as a vector-valued affine forcing / symmetric source-Hessian term, not as a scalar defect to vanish.

Local positive result:
On a fixed good patch with fixed source/core/whitening conventions, the fixed-sector planes form a local analytic rank-two bundle. The frame
\[
(I_b,S_b)
\]
varies analytically, and
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad E_{\eta\eta}
\]
are local analytic sections.

Global missing theorem:
For overlapping good patches \(i,j\), we need canonical transition matrices
\[
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C)
\]
such that
\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\]
with the cocycle condition
\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

The unresolved question:
Do all admissible patch/source/core/whitening transitions induce canonical \(GL_2\)-transitions on the same fixed-sector bundle \(\mathcal F\), or do they change the object being studied?

This wave targets only the fixed-sector atlas theorem.

Do not:
- attack \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\);
- propose another scalar, quotient, split, or line-bundle readout;
- redo source splitting;
- redo finite-core or interaction except insofar as it affects the atlas;
- assume the rank-two bundle is global without proving its transition laws.

Your task is to determine whether
\[
\{\mathfrak f_h(b)\}_{b\in\mathcal B}
\]
forms a canonical global rank-two analytic bundle over the good-patch atlas.
```

# Agent 2 — Whitening and Gram transition agent

```text
You are Agent 2: Whitening and Gram Transition Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Determine whether changes of whitening or Gram normalization induce canonical \(GL_2\)-transitions on the fixed-sector plane.

Setup:
Suppose a local fixed-sector frame is produced by whitening:
\[
E_i=(I_i,S_i)=E_i^{\rm raw}W_i.
\]
On another patch,
\[
E_j=E_j^{\rm raw}W_j.
\]

Tasks:
1. Locate the draft’s whitening definition:
\[
W=G^{-1/2}
\]
or its actual analogue.

2. Determine whether the positive square-root branch is canonical on each connected good patch.

3. Suppose two patches share the same raw frame but different whitening matrices \(W_i,W_j\). Compute:
\[
G_{ij}=W_i^{-1}W_j
\]
and check whether
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij}.
\]

4. If raw frames also differ, identify the raw transition:
\[
E_j^{\rm raw}=E_i^{\rm raw}R_{ij}.
\]
Then compute:
\[
G_{ij}=W_i^{-1}R_{ij}W_j
\]
or the correct formula.

5. Check whether \(G_{ij}\) is canonical or depends on arbitrary whitening choices.

6. Determine whether Gram normalization changes act internally on \(\mathfrak f_h\), or mix fixed-sector and non-fixed-sector components.

7. Check the cocycle condition:
\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

8. If whitening changes are not canonical, identify whether they are at least gauge-equivalent in a harmless \(GL_2\)-sense.

Deliverable:
A whitening/Gram transition theorem or no-go:
\[
\text{whitening changes induce canonical }GL_2\text{ transitions on }\mathfrak f_h
\]
or they do not.
```

# Agent 4 — Ambient projection and functoriality agent

```text
You are Agent 4: Ambient Projection and Functoriality Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Determine whether the fixed-sector projection
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}:\mathcal J_b\to\mathfrak f_h(b)
\]
is functorial across good-patch transitions.

The rank-two connection later wants:
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}\widetilde A).
\]
This requires \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\) and the ambient bundle \(\mathcal J\) to be compatible with transitions.

Tasks:
1. Define the ambient corrected jet/kernel-state bundle \(\mathcal J\) from the draft.

2. Identify how \(\mathcal J_i\) and \(\mathcal J_j\) are related on overlapping patches:
\[
T_{ij}:\mathcal J_i\to\mathcal J_j.
\]

3. Locate the fixed-sector projection:
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}:\mathcal J_i\to\mathfrak f_{h,i}.
\]

4. Check whether:
\[
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j}.
\]

5. Check whether the projections commute with transition:
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
=
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}
\]
on the relevant subspace, or identify correction terms.

6. Determine whether the kernel of \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\) is preserved by ambient derivative:
\[
d_X^{\mathcal J}(\ker\Pi_{\mathfrak f})
\subseteq
\ker\Pi_{\mathfrak f}.
\]
If not, projected connection depends on lift.

7. Decide whether
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}\widetilde A)
\]
is well-defined and functorial.

Deliverable:
A functoriality theorem or no-go for \(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\) and the ambient projected connection.
```

# Agent 5 — Cocycle and atlas consistency agent

```text
You are Agent 5: Cocycle and Atlas Consistency Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Assume candidate transition maps
\[
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C)
\]
have been identified from frame/whitening/source/core transitions. Test whether they define a true bundle atlas.

Tasks:
1. Collect the possible transition maps:
   - midpoint chart transitions;
   - endpoint-ordering swaps;
   - whitening/Gram transitions;
   - raw-frame transitions;
   - source/core transitions;
   - finite-core patch transitions.

2. For each transition type, express:
\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij}.
\]

3. On triple overlaps, test:
\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

4. Identify whether any transition produces an affine term, not a linear \(GL_2\)-term.

5. Identify whether any transition depends on path/history, e.g. moving source windows in different orders.

6. Determine whether the atlas can be restricted to avoid bad transitions:
   - fixed global source/core convention;
   - fixed positive whitening branch;
   - fixed endpoint orientation;
   - fixed finite-core patch type.

7. Decide whether such restrictions are mathematically legitimate or make the proof noncanonical/local only.

Deliverable:
A cocycle theorem or a precise obstruction to building the global fixed-sector bundle.
```

```text
\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b).
\]

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

3. List the theorem dependencies:
   - fixed-sector frame definition;
   - whitening/Gram transition;
   - source/core window transition;
   - ambient projection functoriality;
   - cocycle consistency;

   - source/core changes alter the object, not coordinates;
   - whitening changes mix fixed and non-fixed sectors noncanonically;

   - cocycle fails;
   - only a fixed local convention works.

   - proceed to constructing \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\);
   - restrict to a canonical fixed convention and accept a local proof object;
   - pivot to a different invariant;
   - or declare the rank-two route nonviable.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:38:37)

_Thought for 6s_

## Coordinator verdict

The fixed-sector atlas wave identified the first hard obstruction in the rank-two route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source/core transitions are not presently known to be coordinate changes.}
}
\]

The rank-two bundle is clean **locally**, and whitening/Gram transitions are manageable **if** the raw fixed-sector plane is already identified. But moving zeros into or out of the fixed core appears to change the corrected local object, not merely the frame.

So the rank-two route is now conditional on one theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source/core functoriality theorem.}
}
\]

Without it, the rank-two architecture is only local bookkeeping.

---

## 1. Local fixed-sector frame is fine

Agent 1 found that on a fixed good patch, with endpoint ordering, midpoint trivialization, source/core convention, transpose/parity convention, and whitening branch fixed, the frame

\[
(I_b,S_b)
\]

is an analytic local frame of

\[
\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus \mathbf C S_b.
\]

The frame has genuine local meaning: it is the transpose-invariant/fixed sector of the local \(2\times2\) block. It is not arbitrary. 

But global canonicity requires every allowed change of chart/convention to act by

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C).
\]

This is not yet proved.

---

## 2. Whitening/Gram transitions are conditionally safe

Agent 2 found that whitening itself is not the main problem.

If raw frames are already related by

\[
E_j^{\rm raw}=E_i^{\rm raw}R_{ij},
\]

and

\[
E_i=E_i^{\rm raw}W_i,
\qquad
E_j=E_j^{\rm raw}W_j,
\]

then

\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}=W_i^{-1}R_{ij}W_j.
\]

The cocycle follows if the raw-frame cocycle holds:

\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

So whitening supports the atlas **after** the raw fixed-sector plane has been identified. It cannot rescue cases where the raw planes differ by non-fixed-sector components. 

---

## 3. Source/core transitions are the sharp obstruction

Agent 3’s result is the most important negative result.

Moving a zero atom between non-core source and fixed core changes:

\[
q_{\core},
\]

the core local model,

\[
A_{\mathrm{val}},
\]

the corrected residual decomposition, and the source labels.

That is not naturally a \(GL_2\) frame change:

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij}.
\]

It changes the model being used to define the fixed-sector coefficients. 

There is one limited safe case: moving terms only between

\[
q_{\aux,R}
\quad\text{and}\quad
T_{\far,R}
\]

may be harmless if the fixed core is unchanged and the full non-core complement

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

is held fixed. But this still requires cutoff/error functoriality for

\[
E_{\est,R}.
\]

So the rank-two atlas cannot currently include arbitrary source/core changes.

---

## 4. Ambient projection functoriality is unproved

Agent 4 identified the required commutative diagram.

For ambient transitions

\[
T_{ij}:\mathcal J_i\to\mathcal J_j,
\]

we need

\[
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j},
\]

and

\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
=
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}.
\]

Without this, fixed-sector projection does not commute with patch transition, and the projected connection

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\]

is only a local formula. 

This functoriality is plausible for endpoint swaps, internal basis changes, and fixed whitening branches. It is not proved for source/core transitions or sector-mixing whitening changes.

---

## 5. Cocycle status

Agent 5 found that ordinary coordinate transitions, endpoint swaps, raw-frame changes, and whitening changes can satisfy the \(GL_2\) cocycle, provided the raw fixed-sector atlas exists.

The dangerous case is a transition of the form

\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij}+B_{ij},
\qquad
B_{ij}\neq0.
\]

That is affine, not linear. It would not define a rank-two vector bundle; it would define an affine/torsor structure instead, and would require a different architecture. 

Source/core moves are the likely source of such affine corrections.

---

## 6. Decision

The rank-two route can proceed only under a restricted fixed-convention base:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\{\text{midpoint/collision/finite-core parameters with fixed source/core convention, fixed endpoint orientation, fixed raw jet basis, and canonical whitening branch}\}.
\]

On this reduced base, \(\mathcal F\) is plausible.

But the full good-patch atlas theorem remains unproved.

The next theorem to attack is not the connection theorem yet. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Source/Core Functoriality Theorem}
}
\]

in the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Changing admissible source/core windows induces a canonical ambient transition }T_{ij}
}
\]

such that

\[
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j}
\]

and

\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}
=
T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}.
\]

If this fails, the global rank-two route fails.

---

## Current proof-state ledger

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-sector bundle: local yes, global conditional.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Whitening/Gram: conditionally safe after raw plane identification.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Source/core transitions: main unresolved obstruction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rank-two route: still the best remaining architecture, but blocked by source/core functoriality.}
}
\]

Next move: attack source/core functoriality directly.

# Shared background for all agents

```text
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft.

Current accepted local algebra:
1. Gate A is aggregate-closed under the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention.
2. Gate B is conditionally closed through ordinary order 7 at the formal/quotient-local level.
3. \(M_A,M_C\) connection-table closure is conditionally accepted under source-grade reflection and corrected mixed-block swap.
4. Mixed four-point quotient closure is valid at the determinant/scalar-exit layer.

However, all scalar / quotient / split / line-bundle Bottleneck-C repair routes failed.

The local obstruction is:
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h.
\]

The rank-two architecture is now the best remaining candidate:
\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

On a fixed good patch with fixed conventions, this is clean:
\[
(I_b,S_b)
\]
is a local analytic fixed-sector frame, and
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad E_{\eta\eta}
\]
are local analytic sections.

The global atlas theorem remains missing. For overlapping good patches \(i,j\), we need canonical transition matrices
\[
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C)
\]
such that
\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\]
with cocycle
\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

Previous atlas wave result:
- endpoint swaps, raw-frame changes, and whitening/Gram changes are conditionally safe if the raw fixed-sector plane is already canonically identified;
- whitening itself is not the main problem;
- the sharp obstruction is source/core transition.

Source/core decomposition currently has the form, up to notation,
\[
q
=
q_{\core}
+
q_{\aux,R}
+
T_{\far,R}
+
B_{\bg}
+
E_{\est,R},
\]
or equivalently the rebuilt convention
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

The key question:
If a zero atom is moved between core and source, or if the source/core window changes, does this induce a canonical ambient transition
\[
T_{ij}:\mathcal J_i\to\mathcal J_j
\]
such that
\[
T_{ij}\mathfrak f_{h,i}=\mathfrak f_{h,j},
\]
and
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f,j}T_{ij}=T_{ij}\Pi_{\mathfrak f,i}?
\]

If yes, source/core changes are coordinate changes and the rank-two global bundle can proceed.

If no, they change the corrected local object itself. Then the rank-two vector-bundle atlas fails. One might need either:
1. a globally fixed canonical source/core convention; or
2. a rank-two affine/torsor atlas with transitions
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij}+B_{ij},
\]
instead of purely linear transitions.

This wave should attack source/core functoriality directly.

Do not:
- attack \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\);
- propose a new scalar readout;
- redo Bottleneck-C repairs;
- redo finite-core or interaction unless needed for source/core transition;
- assume source/core changes are coordinate changes without proving it.

Focus on:
\[
q_{\core},\quad q_{\aux,R},\quad T_{\far,R},\quad B_{\bg},\quad E_{\est,R},
\]
the corrected kernel state,
\[
\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr},
\]
the fixed-sector projection,
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f},
\]
and whether source/core changes are functorial.
```

# Agent 2 — Single-zero transfer computation agent

```text
You are Agent 2: Single-Zero Transfer Computation Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Compute what happens when one zero atom is moved between source and core.

Let \(q_\rho\) denote the phase-derivative contribution of a single zero-pair/source atom.

Study the transition:
\[
q_{\core}^{(j)}
=
q_{\core}^{(i)}+q_\rho,
\]
\[
G_{\source}^{(j)}
=
G_{\source}^{(i)}-q_\rho,
\]
where \(G_{\source}\) denotes the relevant non-core source object, e.g.
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Write the corrected kernel state before and after the move:
\[
\widehat\Omega_i^{\corr},
\qquad
\widehat\Omega_j^{\corr}.
\]

2. Compute the difference:
\[
\Delta_\rho\widehat\Omega^{\corr}
=
\widehat\Omega_j^{\corr}-\widehat\Omega_i^{\corr}.
\]

3. Project to the fixed sector:
\[
\Delta_\rho A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f,j}(A_{2r+1}^{(j)})
-
\text{transported }\pi_{\mathfrak f,i}(A_{2r+1}^{(i)}).
\]

4. Determine whether this difference is:
   - zero;
   - representable as a linear \(GL_2\)-frame transition;
   - an affine additive correction
\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}=G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f}+B_{\rho};
\]
   - or a fully new object.

5. Check specifically what happens to:
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad E_{\eta\eta}.
\]

6. Determine whether the transfer correction \(B_{\rho}\), if present, is controlled by Gate A/Gate B or is a new obstruction.

7. Decide whether a single-zero source/core transfer can be part of a vector-bundle atlas, or whether it forces an affine/torsor architecture.

Deliverable:
An explicit single-zero transfer formula and a verdict:
\[
\text{linear transition / affine transition / object-changing transition.}
\]
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:46:20)

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The source/core functoriality wave came back **conditional-negative** for the full atlas, with one viable restricted path.

The rank-two global vector-bundle atlas cannot currently include arbitrary source/core moves. Moving zeros into or out of the fixed core changes the corrected local object, not just the frame. The only viable continuation is to **freeze a canonical core convention** and build the rank-two bundle on the reduced base where that core is stable. 

---

## 1. Classification of source/core transitions

The agents converged on this classification.

### Safe / plausibly coordinate-like

Near/far reallocations inside the **non-core** complement are safe if the fixed core is unchanged and

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]

is treated as the exact full non-core source. Then changing the cutoff only reallocates atoms between \(q_{\aux,R}\) and \(T_{\far,R}\), and the source moments

\[
A_2^{\new},\qquad A_4^{\new}
\]

are unchanged. 

### Conditional / error-sensitive

Cutoff changes involving

\[
E_{\est,R}
\]

are safe only if the error bookkeeping is functorial. Otherwise changing \(R\) introduces additive fixed-sector corrections, not a pure \(GL_2\)-transition. 

### Unsafe / object-changing

Moving a zero atom into or out of

\[
q_{\core}
\]

is not a \(GL_2\)-frame transition under the current framework. It changes:

\[
q_{\core},
\]

the local core model,

\[
A_{\mathrm{val}},
\]

the source labels, the corrected residual decomposition, and generally the fixed-sector coefficients themselves. 

At best, such a transfer has the form

\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{\rho,2r+1},
\]

which is affine, not linear. The affine cocycle for \(B_{\rho,2r+1}\) is not proved. 

---

## 2. Why single-zero core transfer fails as a vector-bundle transition

For a zero atom \(q_\rho\), moving it from source to core gives

\[
q_{\core}^{(j)}=q_{\core}^{(i)}+q_\rho,
\qquad
G_{\source}^{(j)}=G_{\source}^{(i)}-q_\rho.
\]

The total phase contribution is unchanged, but the corrected local construction is **not** a function only of total \(q\). It depends on what is treated as core baseline versus affine-subtracted source. 

At the level of source moments,

\[
A_2\mapsto A_2-\frac{q_\rho''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4\mapsto A_4-\frac{q_\rho^{(4)}(m)}{24},
\]

while the baseline jets change as

\[
q_0\mapsto q_0+q_\rho(m),
\qquad
q_0''\mapsto q_0''+q_\rho''(m).
\]

So the Bottleneck-C coefficient itself changes nontrivially. 

Thus arbitrary core transfer cannot be part of a rank-two **vector** atlas unless a new transfer/cocycle theorem is proved.

---

## 3. Affine torsor is possible but unproved

If source/core transitions are admitted, the natural structure is no longer

\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}=G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f},
\]

but

\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij}.
\]

This would define an affine torsor modeled on the rank-two bundle only if

\[
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik},
\]

and

\[
B_{ik}=G_{jk}^{-1}B_{ij}+B_{jk}
\]

with the correct convention. The agents found this plausible as a language but completely unproved, especially because moving zero atoms in different orders may change whitening and correction terms. 

So the affine torsor route is not ready.

---

## 4. Best viable continuation: reduced fixed-convention base

The cleanest path is to avoid source/core transitions by choosing a canonical core rule and working on strata where the selected core is stable.

The proposed reduced base is:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\{\text{good patches with fixed canonical core, fixed source convention, fixed endpoint orientation, fixed raw jet basis, and canonical whitening branch}\}.
\]

The best candidate core rule is a **canonical symmetric same-scale \(k\)-core** around the midpoint, with strict gap and nondegeneracy conditions. Core changes happen only at:

\[
d_k(m)=d_{k+1}(m),
\]

label swaps, equal-spacing degeneracies, endpoint-gap failures, Gram/whitening singularities, or symmetry-closure ambiguities. These must be placed in a controlled exceptional set

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

This is now the next theorem to attack.

---

## 5. Gate A and Gate B status

Gate A and Gate B remain valid only as **local convention-fixed lemmas**.

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B survive on } \mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

They do **not** prove source/core functoriality. They do not imply that different core choices are \(GL_2\)-equivalent. 

So the paper/ledger should now say:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B are stable local algebraic reductions under a fixed source/core convention.}
}
\]

not:

\[
\text{Gate A/B are globally transportable gates.}
\]

---

## Decision

Do **not** proceed to affine transport yet.

The exact next target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Core Convention Theorem}
}
\]

with the form:

\[
\boxed{
b\in \mathcal B_{\rm red}
\Longrightarrow
\mathfrak f_h(b)
\text{ is a canonical rank-two analytic bundle fibre.}
}
\]

On overlaps inside \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\),

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

And the boundary failure must satisfy:

\[
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

If this theorem fails, the rank-two global route fails.

# Shared background for all six agents

```text
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft.

Current accepted local algebra:

1. Gate A is aggregate-closed under the active homogeneous scalar-grade convention.
2. Gate B is conditionally closed through ordinary order 7 at the formal/quotient-local level.
3. \(M_A,M_C\) connection-table closure is conditionally accepted under source-grade reflection and corrected mixed-block swap.
4. Mixed four-point quotient closure is valid at the determinant/scalar-exit layer.

However, all scalar / quotient / split / line-bundle Bottleneck-C repair routes failed.

The local obstruction is:
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h.
\]

The best remaining route is the rank-two fixed-sector architecture:
\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

The previous source/core functoriality wave found:

- near/far reallocations inside the non-core complement are plausibly coordinate-like if the fixed core is unchanged and
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}
\]
is held fixed as the exact full non-core source;

- changing cutoff \(R\) is safe only if \(E_{\est,R}\) is functorial;

- moving a zero atom into or out of \(q_{\core}\) changes the local model, source labels, corrected residual, baseline/source jets, and generally the fixed-sector coefficients;

- such core moves are not currently \(GL_2\)-frame transitions. At best, they have affine form
\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{\rho,2r+1},
\]
and the affine cocycle for \(B_{\rho,2r+1}\) is unproved;

- therefore the global rank-two vector-bundle atlas cannot include arbitrary source/core moves under the current framework.

The viable continuation is to define a reduced base
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\]
with a fixed canonical core/source convention. On this reduced base, the selected core must be locally stable, the source/core decomposition must not change, and the fixed-sector frames should transition by canonical \(GL_2\)-matrices.

The next theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Canonical Core Convention Theorem}
}
\]

Desired form:

There exists a canonical core-selection rule such that, away from a controlled exceptional set
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]
the selected core is locally constant as a labeled symmetric same-scale zero cluster. On the reduced base
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]
the fixed-sector planes
\[
\mathfrak f_h(b)
\]
form a canonical rank-two analytic bundle with transitions
\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

Boundary failures must satisfy:
\[
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

Do not:
- attack \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\);
- propose another scalar, quotient, split, or line-bundle readout;
- redo Bottleneck-C repairs;
- assume arbitrary source/core functoriality;
- proceed to affine transport before the reduced base is established.

Focus on:
\[
q_{\core},
\quad
\text{canonical same-scale core selection},
\quad
\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\quad
\text{local stability of the selected core},
\quad
\text{compatibility with Gate A/B and finite-core determinacy}.
```

# Agent 1 — Canonical core-selection rule agent

```text
You are Agent 1: Canonical Core-Selection Rule Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Define the best possible canonical fixed-core rule and test whether it is genuinely canonical from the zeta/local-zero data.

Candidate rules include:
1. nearest zero pair;
2. fixed \(k\)-nearest symmetric same-scale zero cluster;
3. spacing-adapted window around \(m\);
4. \(Q\)-window;
5. analytic local zero-labeling;
6. hybrid rule: fixed \(k\)-nearest same-scale cluster with strict gap and symmetry closure.

Tasks:
1. List all plausible canonical core-selection rules available from the draft’s machinery.

2. For each rule, test:
   - canonical dependence on zeta data;
   - local stability under small changes of midpoint \(m\);
   - compatibility with functional-equation and conjugation symmetry;
   - compatibility with same-scale assumptions;
   - compatibility with endpoint separation;
   - compatibility with finite-core determinacy;
   - compatibility with Gate A/B source labels.

3. Decide which rule best defines a reduced base
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

4. If the recommended rule is the fixed \(k\)-nearest symmetric same-scale core, define it precisely:
\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\{\text{the canonical symmetric same-scale }k\text{-cluster nearest }m\}.
\]

5. State the strict inequalities needed for local stability:
\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]
same-scale bounds,
endpoint-gap bounds,
noncollision,
```

```text
   - patch boundary.

\[

\]
does not change labels under small perturbations.

4. Determine whether it can be included in the existing geometric exceptional set:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}.
\]

5. If not, define the enlarged set:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary}.
\]

6. Check whether adding \(\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary}\) destroys the good-patch argument by making the good set too small.

7. Prove or refute:
\[
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

Deliverable:
A stability theorem for the canonical core rule, with exact exceptional/boundary strata.
```

```text
   - Gram singularity unavoidable.

\[

and can be treated as controlled exceptional cases.

\[

\Rightarrow
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
```

```text
   - Gate A/B compatibility theorem;
   - RH-relevant good-patch existence theorem.

   - no canonical core rule;
   - core rule changes outside controlled incidence;
   - \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\) too small to contain RH-relevant configurations;
   - Gate A/B fail under the fixed canonical convention;
   - fixed-sector atlas still fails even on reduced base;

   - proceed to rank-two connection construction on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\);

is a canonical connection on \(\mathcal F_{\rm red}\).

\]
and the exact next theorem to attack.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:55:04)

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The canonical-core wave produced a **conditional positive** result.

The rank-two route is not dead, but it must now be restricted to a reduced base:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

On this base, the core is fixed, source labels are stable, and the rank-two fixed-sector atlas is plausible. Arbitrary source/core transitions remain non-functorial, so they must be excluded rather than transported.  

---

## 1. Best core rule

Use the **fixed \(k\)-nearest symmetric same-scale core**:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-atom zero cluster nearest }m.
}
\]

This rule is viable only where the selection is unique and stable. The necessary strict conditions are:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

same-scale bounds, endpoint-gap bounds, noncollision, symmetry closure, Gram/whitening nondegeneracy, and patch-interior conditions. 

This is the best available compromise: canonical from local zero data, compatible with symmetry, and stable on strata.

---

## 2. Reduced base and exceptional set

Define

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary},
\]

where \(\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary}\) includes:

\[
d_k=d_{k+1},
\]

nearest-neighbor ties, equal-spacing degeneracies, zero collisions, endpoint-gap collapse, symmetry-closure ambiguity, cluster-size jumps, Gram/whitening singularities, and patch-boundary failures. 

Then

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

Agent 2 showed that outside this set, the selected core is locally constant as a labeled symmetric zero cluster. This is because the strict core gap and other strict nondegeneracy inequalities persist under small perturbation. 

---

## 3. Reduced-base atlas is plausible

On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\), no zero moves into or out of

\[
q_{\core}.
\]

Therefore the dangerous additive source/core transfer terms

\[
B_{\rho,2r+1}
\]

do not arise.

The fixed-sector planes should form a rank-two analytic bundle

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b),
\]

with transitions

\[
(I_j,S_j)=(I_i,S_i)G_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik},
\]

provided the remaining transitions are only midpoint/endpoint/raw-frame/whitening/finite-core coordinate changes that preserve the fixed core. 

This means the rank-two route can proceed **conditionally** on the reduced base.

---

## 4. Gate A/B survive, but only locally

Gate A and Gate B remain valid as fixed-convention local algebraic lemmas on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\).

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate A/B are stable on each reduced fixed-core stratum.}
}
\]

They do not prove source/core functoriality across different core choices. They should be stated as local lemmas under a fixed canonical core/source convention. 

---

## 5. Remaining major dependency

The biggest remaining theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant good-patch existence.}
}
\]

We need:

\[
\boxed{
\text{RH-relevant/off-line-zero configuration}
\Longrightarrow
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
}
\]

or else the configuration must lie in a controlled exceptional incidence case.

Agent 5 found this plausible for nondegenerate off-line configurations, but not automatic. It can fail if all candidate midpoints lie on core-boundary strata, symmetry closure forces unstable core size, Gram singularity is unavoidable, or the exceptional set swallows all RH-relevant cases. 

So this is now the main kill switch.

---

## Decision

Proceed, but narrowly.

The next theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{RH-Relevant Reduced Good-Patch Existence Theorem}
}
\]

in the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every RH-relevant off-line zero configuration admits a reduced good patch }b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red},
}
\]

or lies in a previously controlled exceptional set

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

Only after this is proved should we build the rank-two connection

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\]

on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

If the reduced good-patch existence theorem fails, the rank-two global route has no reach.

# Agent 1 — RH-relevant configuration definition agent

```text
You are Agent 1: RH-Relevant Configuration Definition Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Precisely define what counts as an RH-relevant/off-line-zero configuration for the reduced-good-patch existence theorem.

Tasks:
1. Define the minimal RH-relevant object:
\[
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\qquad \beta\ne \frac12,
\]
together with all required symmetry partners:
\[
\bar\rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
\]

2. Determine whether the relevant local atom is:
   - a single off-line zero;
   - a functional-equation/conjugation packet;
   - a same-scale finite cluster;
   - a finite sampled core \(\Theta_k\);
   - or another object from the draft.

3. Define the associated midpoint \(m\). Is it:
\[
m=\gamma/2,
\]
a midpoint between ordinates,
a center of a finite cluster,
or a free local parameter chosen near the off-line packet?

4. Identify what must be true for such a configuration to be seen by the fixed-sector odd germ:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

5. Determine whether RH relevance requires:
   - off-line displacement \(\beta-\frac12\ne0\);
   - same-scale separation;
   - finite-core nondegeneracy;
   - nonzero fixed-sector anomaly;
   - nonzero quotient/projective anomaly;
   - nonzero rank-two affine forcing.

6. Separate:
\[
\text{RH-relevant configuration}
\]
from:
\[
\text{already exceptional / degenerate / incidence-controlled configuration}.
\]

7. Produce a definition suitable for the next agents:
\[
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
=
\{\text{RH-relevant configurations}\}.
\]

Deliverable:
A precise definition of RH-relevant configuration and the local data \((m,\mathcal C_k(m))\) that the reduced-good-patch theorem must produce.
```

# Agent 2 — Core-gap existence agent

```text
You are Agent 2: Core-Gap Existence Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Given an RH-relevant configuration, determine whether one can choose a midpoint \(m\) such that the canonical \(k\)-nearest symmetric same-scale core has a strict selection gap:
\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m).
\]

Tasks:
1. Let the candidate core be:
\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the symmetry-closed same-scale \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]

2. Define the distance scores:
\[
d_\alpha(m)
\]
for zero atoms/packets \(\alpha\).

3. Study the gap function:
\[
\Delta_k(m)=d_{k+1}(m)-d_k(m).
\]

4. Determine whether, near an off-line zero packet, there generically exists \(m\) with:
\[
\Delta_k(m)>0.
\]

5. Analyze tie walls:
\[
d_\alpha(m)=d_\beta(m).
\]
Are these discrete, codimension-one, semianalytic, or potentially unavoidable?

6. Check whether all possible choices of \(m\) near an RH-relevant packet could be trapped on tie walls.

7. If strict gap can fail only on a controlled boundary, state:
\[
\{\Delta_k=0\}\subseteq \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

8. If strict gap may fail for an entire RH-relevant family, give the countermodel.

Deliverable:
A proof, conditional proof, or no-go for existence of \(m\) with strict core gap around every RH-relevant configuration.
```

# Agent 3 — Same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry-closure agent

```text
You are Agent 3: Same-Scale / Endpoint / Symmetry-Closure Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Determine whether an RH-relevant off-line configuration can be placed in a reduced good patch satisfying same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry-closure requirements.

Tasks:
1. Given a candidate core \(\mathcal C_k(m)\), write the exact same-scale requirements:
\[
c_1 S(m)\le d_\alpha(m)\le c_2 S(m)
\quad
(\alpha\in\mathcal C_k(m)),
\]
or the draft’s exact version.

2. Determine whether an off-line zero packet and its symmetry partners naturally form a same-scale packet.

3. Analyze when symmetry closure forces extra atoms into the core:
\[
\rho\in\mathcal C_k(m)
\Rightarrow
\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\in\mathcal C_k(m).
\]

4. Determine whether symmetry closure can make the core size unstable or force a cluster-size jump.

5. Analyze endpoint separation:
\[
t_+\ne t_-,
\qquad
|t_\pm-\rho|\ge \delta_{\endpoint},
\]
or the draft’s exact endpoint nondegeneracy.

6. Determine whether endpoint-gap failure is avoidable by adjusting \(m\) or \(s\), or whether some RH-relevant configurations force endpoint collapse.

7. Place failures into:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm same\ scale}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}.
\]

8. Decide whether these exceptional sets are controlled incidence or too large.

Deliverable:
A theorem or no-go for satisfying same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry-closure conditions on RH-relevant reduced good patches.
```

```text
=

\]
or its exact analogue.

3. Determine whether \(\det G_{\core}(m)\) is analytic/semianalytic in the local zero/core parameters.

4. Determine whether Gram singularity is codimension-one/higher, or can be forced identically by off-line zero symmetry.

5. Given an RH-relevant off-line configuration, can one choose \(m\) or the local sample scale \(s\) to avoid:
\[
\det G_{\core}=0?
\]

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\]
or require enlargement:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
```

```text
\cup

\cup

   - analytic equality;
   - semianalytic inequality boundary;
   - finite-core incidence;
   - patch-boundary artifact;
   - actual geometric obstruction.

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\]
can be treated by existing finite-core incidence/nonconcentration methods.

\not\subseteq
```

```text
   - no canonical \(k\)-core;
   - strict gap unavailable;

\]
admits a canonical connection

=
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 18:58:42)

_Thought for 8s_

## Coordinator verdict

The reduced-good-patch existence wave is **conditionally positive, but not proof-complete**.

The agents established a plausible reduced base:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core},
\]

with a canonical core rule:

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]

But the decisive theorem is still missing:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet admits some }b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
}
\]

The reduced-base rank-two route can continue only if we prove this non-swallowing theorem. L1-L37

---

## 1. RH-relevant configuration is now well-defined

Agent 1 correctly sharpened the definition. The relevant object is not a lone zero

\[
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\qquad \beta\ne\frac12,
\]

but the symmetry packet

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)
=
\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\}.
\]

An RH-relevant configuration for this architecture is:

\[
(\mathcal P(\rho),m,\mathcal C_k(m),\Theta_k)
\]

such that the packet lies in a stable same-scale core and produces nonzero fixed-sector odd data:

\[
\exists r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0.
\]

This is important: “off-line zero exists” is not enough for this route. The off-line packet must be visible to the rank-two fixed-sector germ. L9-L74

---

## 2. Strict core gap is generic, not automatic

Agent 2 found that the strict gap condition

\[
\Delta_k(m)=d_{k+1}(m)-d_k(m)>0
\]

holds off the tie walls

\[
d_\alpha(m)=d_\beta(m).
\]

These walls are semianalytic and can be included in

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

So the gap failure is controlled as an exceptional condition.

But the unconditional statement is not proved. It remains possible, formally, that an RH-relevant packet is trapped on a tie wall for all admissible midpoint choices. This is probably non-generic, but we need a non-swallowing theorem, not just generic intuition. L149-L232

---

## 3. Same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry closure are conditionally OK

Agent 3 found no new fatal obstruction here.

For a nondegenerate off-line packet, the same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry-closure requirements are locally satisfiable after choosing the core as a symmetry-closed packet and choosing \((m,s)\) away from boundary walls.

Failures go into:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}.
\]

This is a useful result: symmetry closure does not by itself kill the reduced-base strategy. But we should count \(k\) by symmetry packets or symmetry-closed packet size, not naive individual-zero count. L274-L370

---

## 4. Gram/whitening nondegeneracy is generic, but still a dependency

Agent 4 found that Gram singularity is not visibly forced by off-line symmetry.

The bad set

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}
=
\{\det G_{\core}=0\}
\]

is analytic or semianalytic on a reduced stratum. Unless the determinant vanishes identically on the RH-relevant family, its complement is open and dense.

So the missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\not\equiv0
\text{ on every RH-relevant off-line packet family.}
}
\]

This is likely a finite-core independence lemma. But it is not yet proved. L438-L525

---

## 5. Exceptional set is controlled structurally, but non-swallowing is missing

Agent 5’s conclusion is the central one.

The enlarged exceptional set

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm tie}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm patch}^{\core}
\]

is structurally controlled: its components are analytic equalities, semianalytic boundaries, incidence conditions, or patch-boundary artifacts.

But we do not yet know:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

Nor do we know the stronger statement:

\[
\boxed{
\forall R\in\mathcal R_{\rm RH},
\quad
\exists b\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ associated to }R.
}
\]

This is the next kill switch. L571-L665

---

## 6. Decision

The rank-two reduced-base route remains alive, but only conditionally.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical core rule: viable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Core stability: viable off explicit boundary strata.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Same-scale/endpoint/symmetry: conditionally viable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gram/whitening: generically viable, needs non-identical-vanishing.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Exceptional non-swallowing: missing.}
}
\]

So do **not** proceed yet to constructing

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The next theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Exceptional Non-Swallowing Theorem}
}
\]

with the strongest useful form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet admits a nearby midpoint/sample choice }(m,s)
\text{ satisfying}
}
\]

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

\[
\text{same-scale, symmetry closure, endpoint separation, and }
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\ne0.
\]

If this succeeds, then the rank-two connection construction becomes the next step. If it fails, the reduced-base rank-two route has no global reach.

```text
\in\mathfrak f_h.

All scalar/quotient/split/line-bundle repairs failed:
- \(\Phi_K\)-scalar sees the obstruction and forces bad pointwise \(T\)-flatness.
- Pure quotient loses \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line anomalies.
- Split readout restores completeness but reintroduces the obstruction.
- Line-bundle transport is locally coherent but lacks global covariance, exactness, boundary, and holonomy control.

The remaining route is rank-two fixed-sector geometry:
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.

Because arbitrary source/core transitions are not functorial, we restrict to a reduced base with a fixed canonical core convention.

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-packet nearest }m.

\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=

\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup

\cup

\cup

\cup

\cup

\cup

\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne1/2.

is generic off tie walls

but not yet proved unavoidable for every RH-relevant packet.

3. Same-scale, endpoint, and symmetry-closure failures appear controllable as boundary/incidence conditions.

Current kill switch:
\[

\[

\]
such that:
\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]
same-scale conditions hold,
symmetry closure is stable,
endpoint separation holds,
\[
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\ne0,

and the fixed-sector signal is nonzero:

Equivalently:

\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
```

# Agent 5 — Fixed-sector visibility non-swallowing agent

```text
You are Agent 5: Fixed-Sector Visibility Non-Swallowing Agent.

Use the shared background.

Even if a reduced good patch exists geometrically, the rank-two route also needs the off-line packet to produce nonzero fixed-sector data:
\[
\exists r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)\ne0.
\]

Your task:
Determine whether an off-line packet can be completely invisible to the fixed-sector odd germ outside the exceptional set.

Tasks:
1. Define the fixed-sector finite vector:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R+1}^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

2. Identify what local source/core data from an off-line packet enter these coefficients.

3. Test whether symmetry could force:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad
\forall r
\]
for a genuine off-line packet.

4. Compare with prior toy/local obstruction results:
the off-line-like source row produced nonzero \(\eta\eta\) obstruction. Determine whether that implies fixed-sector visibility.

5. Attempt to prove:
\[
\text{off-line packet}
\Rightarrow
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\ne0
\]
outside a controlled incidence set.

6. If this fails, define the invisibility locus:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}.
\]

7. Determine whether \(\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}\) is controlled by finite determinacy/incidence or whether it could contain an open RH-relevant family.

8. Deliver a theorem or no-go for fixed-sector visibility.

Deliverable:
A fixed-sector visibility non-swallowing theorem or countermodel.
```

# Agent 6 — Exceptional non-swallowing synthesis agent

```text
You are Agent 6: Exceptional Non-Swallowing Synthesis Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Synthesize this wave and decide whether the reduced-base rank-two route can proceed.

Target theorem:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
}
\]

Stronger target:
Every nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet admits nearby \((m,s)\) such that:
\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]
same-scale holds,
symmetry closure is stable,
endpoint separation holds,
\[
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\ne0,
\]
and
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(m,s)\ne0.
\]

Tasks:
1. State Agent 1’s parameter-avoidance result.

2. State Agent 2’s symmetry-packet result.

3. State Agent 3’s same-scale result.

4. State Agent 4’s Gram determinant result.

5. State Agent 5’s fixed-sector visibility result.

6. Decide whether the theorem is:
   - proved;
   - conditionally proved under nondegeneracy assumptions;
   - false;
   - or still open with specific missing dependencies.

7. Define the final enlarged exceptional set if needed:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram,id}^{\core}
\cup
\cdots.
\]

8. Decide whether adding these sets is legitimate or swallows RH-relevant configurations.

9. If non-swallowing succeeds, state the next theorem:
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\text{ admits a canonical connection }
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
\]

10. If non-swallowing fails, state whether the current proof family should be marked nonviable.

Deliverable:
A decision memo:
\[
\text{Exceptional non-swallowing: proved / conditional / failed}
\]
and the exact next theorem to attack.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:02:46)

_Thought for 7s_

## Coordinator verdict

The exceptional non-swallowing wave is **still conditional**, but it narrowed the remaining kill switch substantially.

The rank-two reduced-base route now depends on one combined theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Packet Visibility and Independence Theorem}
}
\]

For every nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet

\[
\mathcal P(\rho)=\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad \rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne\frac12,
\]

there must exist nearby local parameters \((m,s)\) such that:

\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]

the packet-level core is same-scale and symmetry-stable,

\[
\det G_{\core}(m,s)\ne0,
\]

and the rank-two fixed-sector signal is nonzero:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(m,s)\ne0.
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}.
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram,id}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm forced\ scale}^{\core}.
\]

This is not yet proved. But the agents reduced the problem to a small list of concrete non-identical-vanishing / non-swallowing statements. L1-L39

---

## 1. Parameter avoidance is enough unless a wall is identically forced

Agent 1 showed that the local parameters

\[
(m,s)
\]

give enough freedom to avoid finitely many analytic or semianalytic exceptional walls, provided those walls are not identically forced by the packet geometry.

The relevant walls are:

\[
d_k=d_{k+1},
\]

same-scale boundary,

symmetry-closure boundary,

endpoint collision,

\[
\det G_{\core}=0,
\]

and fixed-sector invisibility

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0.
\]

Thus the problem is no longer generic avoidance. It is whether any of these bad conditions is **identically forced** on an RH-relevant packet family. L41-L143

---

## 2. Symmetry is not the kill switch if we order packets, not zeros

Agent 2 resolved an important technical issue.

Functional-equation and conjugation symmetries force equalities **inside** the packet

\[
\mathcal P(\rho).
\]

Those should not be treated as core-selection failures. The core rule must order symmetry packets, not individual zeros.

Define a packet score

\[
D_P(m)
\]

and choose the nearest \(k\) symmetry packets. Then internal packet ties disappear from the exceptional set. Only ties between distinct packets matter:

\[
D_P(m)=D_Q(m),
\qquad P\ne Q.
\]

Those are ordinary controlled boundary strata. So symmetry closure does **not** by itself swallow RH-relevant off-line packets. L182-L269

---

## 3. Same-scale is also conditionally safe

Agent 3 found that off-lineness

\[
\beta-\frac12\ne0
\]

does not itself force same-scale failure. The real danger is the surrounding zero environment: unrelated nearby packets may force the canonical \(k\)-core to mix multiple scales.

That is a real possibility, but it belongs to

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm scale}^{\core}
\]

unless it occurs on an open RH-relevant family.

So same-scale non-swallowing remains conditional, but there is no structural evidence that off-line packets are automatically scale-exceptional. L310-L413

---

## 4. Gram nondegeneracy is the strongest positive result

Agent 4 gave the best concrete positive result.

The relevant Gram determinants are built from Cauchy/jet-type source functions. Distinct Cauchy poles are linearly independent by principal-part/residue comparison. Confluent jet families are likewise independent unless poles collide, labels duplicate, endpoints collapse, jet depth is insufficient, or parity projection kills the family.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\not\equiv0
}
\]

on nondegenerate RH-relevant off-line packet strata, under the standard distinct-pole / sufficient-jet-depth hypotheses.

Gram failure is therefore a controlled incidence component, not a generic obstruction. L448-L542

This is useful. It removes one major kill switch, modulo the stated independence hypotheses.

---

## 5. Fixed-sector visibility remains the main unresolved theorem

Agent 5 identified the most serious remaining dependency.

Even if a reduced geometric patch exists, the rank-two route needs the off-line packet to be visible:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(m,s)
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\ne0.
\]

Define the invisibility locus:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}.
\]

The agents do **not** yet have a theorem excluding

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0
\]

for a genuine off-line packet family.

Prior Bottleneck-C computations strongly suggest actual source packets can generate nonzero fixed-sector rows, but that is not a universal visibility theorem. The required statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No nondegenerate off-line packet family is entirely contained in }
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}.
}
\]

This is now the main mathematical target. L548-L646

---

## 6. Decision

The reduced-base rank-two route is still alive, but the next wave must be very narrow.

Do **not** construct

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]

yet.

The exact next target is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Packet Visibility and Independence Theorem}
}
\]

Break it into two subtheorems:

### A. Source/jet independence

\[
\boxed{
\det G_{\core}\not\equiv0
}
\]

for nondegenerate off-line symmetry packets.

This is mostly supported by Agent 4 via Cauchy/jet independence.

### B. Fixed-sector visibility

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

for nondegenerate off-line symmetry packets outside controlled incidence.

This is still open and is now the true bottleneck.

---

## Current proof-state ledger

\[
\boxed{
\text{Canonical core rule: conditionally viable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Reduced good-patch geometry: generically viable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gram nondegeneracy: conditionally positive.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed-sector visibility: not proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Rank-two connection construction: deferred until visibility is proved.}
}
\]

If packet visibility fails, the reduced-base rank-two route has no RH-detection power. If it succeeds, we can finally proceed to the connection theorem on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}.
\]

# Shared background for all six agents

```text
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft.

Current state:

Gate A and Gate B remain accepted only as local fixed-convention algebraic lemmas:
\[
\text{Gate A: aggregate closure under homogeneous scalar-grade convention.}
\]
\[
\text{Gate B: conditional closure through ordinary order }7.
\]

All scalar/quotient/split/line-bundle Bottleneck-C repairs failed. The active obstruction is:
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h.
\]

The remaining architecture is rank-two fixed-sector geometry on the reduced base:
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red},
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

The canonical core convention is:
\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]

The enlarged exceptional set is:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core,+}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram,id}^{\core}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm forced\ scale}^{\core}.
\]

The last wave established:
1. Parameter freedom in \((m,s)\) avoids exceptional walls unless some wall is identically forced.
2. Symmetry closure is safe if the core is selected by symmetry packets, not individual zeros.
3. Same-scale failure is not intrinsic to off-lineness.
4. Gram nondegeneracy is conditionally positive via Cauchy/jet independence.
5. The remaining hard theorem is fixed-sector visibility:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\not\equiv0
\]
for nondegenerate off-line symmetry packets.

The RH-relevant packet is:
\[
\mathcal P(\rho)=\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne\frac12.
\]

At the source-atom level, a paired contribution has form:
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

The next theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Packet Visibility and Independence Theorem}
}
\]

Desired theorem:
For every nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet \(\mathcal P(\rho)\), there exists a nearby reduced good patch \(b=(m,s,\mathcal C_k(m))\in\mathcal B_{\rm red}\) such that:
\[
d_k(m)<d_{k+1}(m),
\]
same-scale / symmetry / endpoint / Gram conditions hold, and:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(b)\ne0.
\]

Equivalently:
\[
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}.
\]

Do not:
- attack \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\);
- propose another scalar, quotient, split, or line-bundle readout;
- redo Bottleneck-C repairs;
- proceed to \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\) construction yet;
- assume visibility without proving it.

Focus only on:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f},
\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},
\quad
\pi_{\mathfrak f},
\quad
\text{off-line packet source jets},
\quad
\text{non-identical vanishing of fixed-sector coefficients.}
```

# Agent 1 — Off-line packet jet expansion agent

```text
You are Agent 1: Off-Line Packet Jet Expansion Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Compute the local jet expansion of a nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet and identify which jet components can feed the fixed-sector odd coefficients
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Start from the paired source atom:
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Set local coordinate:
\[
x=2t-\gamma,
\qquad
x_m=2m-\gamma.
\]

2. Expand \(f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)\) around \(t=m\), or equivalently around \(x=x_m\).

3. Compute derivatives:
\[
f^{(j)}_{\beta,\gamma}(m)
\]
for \(j=0,1,2,3,4,5,\ldots\), at least symbolically enough to see dependence on:
\[
\delta=\beta-\frac12,
\qquad
x_m.
\]

4. Identify which parts are even/odd in:
\[
\delta
\]
and which vanish on the critical line \(\delta=0\).

5. Determine whether off-line displacement \(\delta\ne0\) necessarily produces a nonzero jet invariant at some finite order.

6. Connect these packet jets to source moments:
\[
A_2,\quad A_4,\quad A_6,\ldots
\]
and to candidate fixed-sector coefficients:
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots.
\]

7. Determine whether the packet jet sequence can vanish identically for \(\delta\ne0\) after symmetry closure.

8. If possible, identify the first order where off-line displacement must appear.

Deliverable:
A theorem or counterexample:
\[
\delta\ne0
\Rightarrow
\text{nonzero local source jet feeding the fixed-sector odd germ}
\]
outside collision / endpoint / symmetry degeneracy.
```

---

# Agent 2 — Fixed-sector projection non-annihilation agent

```text
You are Agent 2: Fixed-Sector Projection Non-Annihilation Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Determine whether the fixed-sector projection
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\]
can annihilate all off-line packet contributions to the odd fixed-sector germ.

The dangerous failure is:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad
\forall r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\]
for an actual off-line packet outside incidence.

Tasks:
1. Locate the local formula for the fixed-sector projection:
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(Z)
=
\frac{Z_{11}+Z_{22}}2 I+Z_{12}S
\]
or the draft’s exact analogue.

2. Determine which components of the packet-induced local matrix enter:
\[
I\text{-component},
\qquad
S\text{-component}.
\]

3. Test whether functional-equation/conjugation symmetry forces the packet-induced local matrix to lie entirely in the anti/fibre complement:
\[
\ker \pi_{\mathfrak f}.
\]

4. Use the known Bottleneck-C row shape:
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
as evidence: determine whether the same packet class can produce nonzero fixed-sector projection generically.

5. Prove or refute:
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(\text{off-line packet contribution})\not\equiv0
\]
as a function of \((\beta,m,s)\), for \(\beta\ne1/2\).

6. Identify exceptional cases where projection can vanish:
   - parity cancellation;
   - endpoint symmetry;
   - critical-line collapse \(\beta=1/2\);
   - Gram/whitening singularity;
   - source packet centered at a special \(m\);
   - insufficient finite order.

7. Decide whether those cases are controlled incidence:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]
or an open RH-relevant invisibility family.

Deliverable:
A projection non-annihilation theorem or a no-go showing fixed-sector projection may miss an open family of off-line packets.
```

# Agent 3 — First nonzero fixed-sector coefficient agent

```text
You are Agent 3: First Nonzero Fixed-Sector Coefficient Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Find the first finite odd order \(2r+1\) at which a nondegenerate off-line packet must contribute nontrivially to:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The visibility theorem only needs:
\[
\exists r\le R_{\Theta_k}
\quad
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

Tasks:
1. Starting from the packet jet expansion, identify candidate orders:
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_7^{\mathfrak f},\quad A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots.
\]

2. Determine whether \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) is baseline/reference only and should be excluded from the visibility vector, or whether it already detects off-line packet data.

3. Analyze \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\):
   - does the off-line packet produce a nonzero contribution there?
   - can Gate A/B cancellations erase it?
   - does symmetry force it into a line/quotient/anti sector?

4. If \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) can vanish, analyze \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\), \(A_{11}^{\mathfrak f}\), etc.

5. Determine whether there is a finite upper bound:
\[
R_{\Theta_k}
\]
such that an off-line packet cannot vanish in all controlled odd orders unless it is exceptional.

6. If the proof requires Noetherian/finite-determinacy logic, state it precisely:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0\quad(3\le r\le R)
\Rightarrow
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0\quad\forall r,
\]
then show why this contradicts off-line packet nontriviality.

7. If no finite first-order visibility can be guaranteed, provide a countermodel.

Deliverable:
A finite-order visibility theorem:
\[
\exists r\le R_{\Theta_k}\quad A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]
for nondegenerate off-line packets, or a precise no-go.
```

# Agent 4 — Analytic incidence / invisibility-locus agent

```text
You are Agent 4: Analytic Incidence / Invisibility-Locus Agent.

Treat the invisibility locus
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}

as an analytic incidence set and determine whether it can contain an open RH-relevant off-line family.

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

\[
\beta,\gamma,m,s,\theta.
\]

3. Prove that:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]
is analytic or semianalytic on each reduced stratum.

4. Determine what it would mean for invisibility to swallow an RH-relevant packet family:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0
\]
on an open set with \(\beta\ne1/2\).

5. Attempt to show this is impossible by analytic continuation:
   if the fixed-sector coefficients vanish on an open off-line family, do they vanish also in toy/source models known to produce nonzero \(E_{\eta\eta}\)?

6. Compare against known local obstruction models:
   - formal \(r=u^2\);
   - far-tail actual-source approximations;
   - Bottleneck-C \(\eta\eta\) row with nonzero \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\).

8. If invisibility is proper incidence, state:
\[
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}.
\]

Deliverable:
An analytic-incidence theorem showing invisibility is proper, or a counterexample where fixed-sector invisibility is open.
```

# Agent 5 — Adversarial visibility countermodel agent

```text
You are Agent 5: Adversarial Visibility Countermodel Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Try to kill the visibility theorem by constructing an off-line packet or formal packet family with:
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0
\]
outside the already controlled exceptional set.

Do not try to prove visibility. Try to break it.

Tasks:
1. Build formal packet models with \(\beta\ne1/2\) but symmetric source contributions.

2. Test whether conjugation/function-equation symmetry can cancel all fixed-sector odd terms.

3. Test special midpoint choices:
\[
m=\gamma/2,
\]
or shifted \(m\), where odd/even parity may annihilate fixed-sector terms.

4. Test special endpoint/sample choices \(s\) that make the packet contribution anti-fixed.

5. Test whether core normalization or whitening can absorb the packet contribution into baseline/reference data, leaving:
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0.
\]

6. Try to construct a formal family where nonzero off-line packet data lives entirely in anti/fibre sectors:
\[
A_{2r+1}\in\ker\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\quad
\forall r.
\]

7. Check whether such models necessarily trigger:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm sym}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm endpoint}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm Gram}^{\core},
\quad
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
\]
as controlled incidence.

8. Give a verdict:
   - visibility theorem survives adversarial tests;
   - or visibility fails by explicit countermodel.

Deliverable:
A countermodel or a strong adversarial report supporting the visibility theorem.
```
