## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:07:25)

_Thought for 8s_

## Coordinator verdict

The packet-visibility wave remains **conditional-positive**, but the bottleneck is now extremely narrow.

We do **not** yet have the theorem

\[
\mathcal R_{\rm RH}
\not\subseteq
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}.
\]

But the agents reduced it to one explicit computational target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute one finite fixed-sector coefficient, preferably }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ or }A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\text{ for an actual nondegenerate off-line packet and show it is not identically zero.}
}
\]

If that succeeds, packet visibility becomes a proper analytic-incidence theorem and the rank-two route can proceed to the connection theorem. If it fails because there is an open off-line family with

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0,
\]

then the rank-two route has no RH-detection power. L670-L746

---

## 1. Source-jet visibility is proved

Agent 1 showed that an off-line packet is **not source-jet invisible**.

For

\[
\delta=\beta-\frac12,
\]

the paired packet function is even in \(\delta\), so off-criticality enters through

\[
\delta^2,\delta^4,\ldots
\]

not linearly. This matters: any detector expecting a linear \(\delta\)-term is wrong.

But the post-affine source jet sequence is nontrivial. In particular, at the centered point \(x_m=0\),

\[
\rho_2
=
-4\left[
(1/2-\delta)^{-3}
+
(1/2+\delta)^{-3}
\right]\ne0,
\]

and

\[
\rho_4
=
16\left[
(1/2-\delta)^{-5}
+
(1/2+\delta)^{-5}
\right]\ne0.
\]

So a nondegenerate off-line packet supplies nonzero finite source moments such as

\[
A_2,\quad A_4.
\]

This does not yet prove fixed-sector visibility, but it proves the packet has nonzero local data capable of feeding the fixed-sector machinery. L1-L115

---

## 2. Projection annihilation looks unlikely, but still needs a formula

Agent 2 found no structural reason why

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\]

should annihilate all off-line packet contributions.

The strongest evidence is still the known Bottleneck-C row:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in\mathfrak f_h.
\]

This row proves that the same source architecture can produce a nonzero fixed-sector vector whenever

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}\ne0
\]

and

\[
wI+uS\ne0.
\]

Thus complete fixed-sector invisibility should be a proper analytic incidence condition, not an open generic phenomenon. But this remains conditional on proving that the actual off-line packet jets realize the same finite source directions used by the Bottleneck-C row. L116-L236

---

## 3. First live visibility coefficient is \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\)

Agent 3 gave the right finite-order target.

Do **not** use

\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]

as the visibility witness; it is the reference/baseline direction.

The first serious visibility candidate is

\[
\boxed{A_7^{\mathfrak f}.}
\]

The reason is that the known active row is order \(7\) and couples source moments

\[
A_2,\quad A_4
\]

into a fixed-sector vector. Generically,

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

But it can vanish on the septic locking hypersurface

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
\frac{10q^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q''}{18q},
\]

so \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) alone is not guaranteed pointwise.

The correct theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=A_9^{\mathfrak f}=\cdots=A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\Rightarrow
\text{controlled incidence or true invisibility.}
}
\]

By finite determinacy, it would be enough to prove that the full fixed-sector odd germ is not identically zero for a nondegenerate off-line packet. L237-L397

---

## 4. Invisibility is analytic incidence if one witness exists

Agent 4 clarified the analytic structure.

On a reduced stratum,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots,A_{2R_{\Theta_k}+1}^{\mathfrak f})
\]

is analytic in local packet/core/sample parameters. Therefore

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]

is an analytic incidence locus.

If we exhibit **one** nonzero fixed-sector coefficient on a connected off-line packet component, then

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\not\equiv0
\]

on that component, and invisibility is proper incidence.

Agent 4’s caveat is decisive: the known nonzero Bottleneck-C row is a witness only if it belongs to the same actual reduced off-line packet family, not merely to a formal/source-perturbative family. L398-L512

---

## 5. Adversarial search found no open invisibility countermodel

Agent 5 tried to break visibility and failed to produce a genuine open-family countermodel.

The strongest attempted attacks were:

\[
m=\gamma/2
\]

making the raw packet function even, endpoint/sample cancellation, anti-fixed-sector projection, and core-normalization absorption.

But midpoint evenness only kills raw odd source derivatives; the Bottleneck-C mechanism uses even source jets such as

\[
\rho_2,\rho_4
\]

to feed odd fixed-sector rows after finite-\(s\), whitening, and mixed-block operations.

Endpoint/sample cancellation appears incidence-like, not open. Anti-fixed-sector annihilation lacks a structural identity. Core-normalization absorption remains the most serious risk, but no open-family countermodel was found. L513-L668

So the visibility theorem survives adversarial testing, but is not proved.

---

## Decision

The rank-two route remains alive, but do **not** construct

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]

yet.

The next attack must be a direct coefficient computation:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Fixed-Sector Projection Non-Identity Theorem}
}
\]

Target form:

\[
\boxed{
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\equiv0
\Longrightarrow
\beta=\frac12
\text{ or controlled incidence.}
}
\]

Concrete near-term target:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Compute }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ for the actual off-line packet source model.}
}
\]

If \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is nonzero for one nondegenerate parameter choice, analyticity proves the invisibility locus is proper. If \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) vanishes because of the septic locking condition, compute

\[
A_9^{\mathfrak f}
\]

or the next odd coefficient.

---

## Next recommended wave

Use fewer agents or a very focused six-agent computation wave. The assignments should be:

1. derive the actual \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) coefficient map from packet jets;
2. evaluate it at a clean parameter point, e.g. \(x_m=0\), \(q''=0\), \(q\ne0\), \(\delta\ne0\);
3. check whether the result survives fixed-sector projection;
4. if \(A_7\) locks, compute \(A_9\);
5. adversarially test whether the coefficient can vanish identically;
6. synthesize the non-identity theorem.

The proof-state label should now be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet visibility: strongly plausible, adversarially unbroken, but still missing one explicit nonzero fixed-sector coefficient witness.}
}
\]

# Agent 1 — Actual \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) coefficient derivation

```text
You are Agent 1: Actual \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) Coefficient Derivation Agent.

Derive the actual order-7 fixed-sector coefficient contribution from a nondegenerate off-line packet source model.

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\quad\text{or the order-7 fixed-sector row generated by packet source moments.}

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]
with
\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

Tasks:
1. Identify precisely how the packet source moments
\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}
\]
enter the order-7 fixed-sector coefficient.

2. Specialize to a single nondegenerate off-line symmetry packet, or a symmetry-packet core, using:
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0,
\]
use:
\[
A_2=\rho_2
=
-4\left[

+
(1/2+\delta)^{-3}
\right],

A_4=\rho_4
=
16\left[
(1/2-\delta)^{-5}
+
(1/2+\delta)^{-5}
\right].
\]

4. Substitute into \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\).

5. Determine whether \(\nu_{\eta\eta}\) is nonzero for at least one explicit nondegenerate parameter choice:
\[
\delta\ne0,\quad q\ne0,\quad q''\text{ chosen/given},\quad Q\ne0.
\]

6. Avoid relying on artificial assumptions unless stated. If you set \(q''=0\), explain whether this is a legitimate local model point or only a witness in the analytic family.

7. Verify that
\[
wI+uS\ne0
\]
on the same good patch, or state the needed good-patch nondegeneracy.

8. Deliver either:
   - a concrete nonzero \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) / \(E_{\eta\eta}\) witness;
   - or a proof that \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) is locked/zero for the actual packet, forcing us to test \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\).

Deliverable:
An explicit order-7 fixed-sector coefficient computation showing nonzero visibility, or a precise obstruction at order 7.
```

```text
or the draft’s exact normalization, plus combinations of \(A_2,A_4,q,q'',q^{(4)}\), etc.

   - order 9 depends on a new independent source jet \(A_6\);
   - off-line packet jets satisfy no identity forcing \(A_6\) to the value needed for \(A_9\) cancellation;
   - therefore simultaneous \(A_7=A_9=0\) is codimension at least 2 unless structural identity exists.

6. Generalize:
\[
A_7=A_9=\cdots=A_{2R+1}=0
\]
should be a finite analytic incidence system, not an identity.

   - or a finite-determinacy/incidence theorem showing locking does not imply full invisibility.
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:12:17)

_Thought for 10s_

## Coordinator verdict

The packet-visibility wave produced a **conditional breakthrough**, but not a fully closed theorem.

We now have a concrete nonzero order-7 witness in the local off-line packet source-moment model:

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv0
}
\]

provided the known order-7 Bottleneck-C row is realized inside the **actual reduced-core packet coefficient map**. That last phrase is the remaining gap. 

---

## 1. What is now established

For the off-line packet

\[
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,
\qquad
\delta=\beta-\frac12\ne0,
\]

using the paired source atom

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

the centered packet moments at

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma=0
\]

are

\[
A_2
=
-4\left[
(1/2-\delta)^{-3}
+
(1/2+\delta)^{-3}
\right],
\]

\[
A_4
=
16\left[
(1/2-\delta)^{-5}
+
(1/2+\delta)^{-5}
\right].
\]

For the explicit choice

\[
\delta=\frac14,
\qquad
\beta=\frac34,
\qquad
q=1,
\qquad
q''=0,
\qquad
Q=1,
\]

the agents computed

\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\]

\[
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243},
\]

and the order-7 scalar coefficient

\[
\nu
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right]
\]

is nonzero, in fact negative.

The septic locking condition also fails:

\[
\frac{A_4}{A_2}
=
-\frac{3904}{63}
\ne
\frac{10}{9}
=
\frac{10q^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q''}{18q}.
\]

So, in the source-moment coefficient model,

\[
\boxed{
\nu\ne0.
}
\]

Then, assuming the good-patch vector

\[
wI+uS\ne0,
\]

the order-7 fixed-sector row

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]

is a nonzero vector in

\[
\mathfrak f_h.
\]

---

## 2. What this proves

This proves:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The order-7 fixed-sector coefficient formula is not identically zero in the off-line packet source-moment family.}
}
\]

Therefore, on any connected analytic reduced packet component containing this witness,

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots)
\]

is not identically zero.

Consequently,

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]

is a proper analytic incidence locus on that component.

This is the first real positive visibility result.

---

## 3. The remaining gap

The remaining gap is **not** generic visibility anymore. It is the realization bridge:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual reduced-core coefficient }A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ contain this same }(A_2,A_4)\text{-driven row?}
}
\]

The witness was computed in the packet **source-moment** chart. But the reduced-base architecture puts the canonical packet into the fixed core

\[
q_{\core}.
\]

So we still must verify that core normalization / baseline absorption does not remove the row from the actual reduced-core coefficient map.

The agents’ caveat is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{source-moment witness} \ne \text{certified actual reduced-core witness yet.}
}
\]

---

## 4. Do we proceed to \(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\)?

Not quite.

Proceed to the rank-two connection theorem only if we accept or prove:

\[
\boxed{
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
\text{ in the actual reduced-packet model contains the computed order-7 source-moment row.}
}
\]

If that is certified, then packet visibility is conditionally closed and the next theorem is:

\[
\boxed{

\[

```text
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale, \(k\)-packet nearest }m.

\[

\qquad

+

\qquad

\qquad

=
```

_Thought for 14s_

## Coordinator verdict

The wave did **not** close packet visibility, but it sharply localized the remaining gap.

\[
\boxed{
\text{The source-moment }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ witness is real, but actual reduced-core realization is still unproved.}
}
\]

The rank-two route remains alive, but we should **not** proceed to constructing

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}
\]

yet. The next step is a single-formula derivation:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
}
\]

Until this is computed in the actual reduced-core convention, packet visibility remains conditional. 

---

## What the agents established

### 1. Core absorption does not erase the packet jets at the raw level

Agent 1 made real progress. When the off-line packet is moved into

\[
q_{\core},
\]

its source moments become core phase derivatives:

\[
q_{\core}''(m)=2A_2,
\qquad
q_{\core}^{(4)}(m)=24A_4.
\]

At the clean witness

\[
\delta=\frac14,\qquad x_m=0,
\]

these are nonzero and large:

\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243}.
\]

So the packet is definitely **not core-jet invisible**.

Agent 1 also expanded the reduced-core finite-\(s\) numerator and found that order \(s^7\) contains terms involving

\[
A_2A_4,\qquad A_2^2,
\]

along with extra core terms involving higher derivatives such as \(q_6,q_8\). This means core absorption does **not** simply remove the relevant packet data.

But the raw reduced-core coefficient is not yet the final corrected, whitened, fixed-sector coefficient.

---

### 2. The source-row formula cannot simply be copied into the core chart

The known source-chart row is

\[
E_{\eta\eta}^{\source}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]

with

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right].
\]

But in the reduced-core chart, the packet is not an affine-subtracted non-core source. It is part of the baseline/core phase model. So the actual coefficient is

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
\]

Agent 2 correctly framed the missing bridge:

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
+
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\]

and we still do not know whether

\[
\Delta_{\core/\source}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
-A_{7,\source}^{\mathfrak f}
\]

identically. There is no evidence for such a cancellation, but there is also no theorem excluding it.

---

### 3. Full symmetry-packet cancellation is not the issue

Agent 3 cleared a major risk.

The paired atom

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
\]

already includes the functional-equation partner at ordinate \(+\gamma\). Adding the conjugate ordinate packet \(\gamma\mapsto-\gamma\) does not introduce a universal minus sign in

\[
A_2,\qquad A_4,\qquad \nu_{\eta\eta}.
\]

At symmetric midpoints, the even source moments add rather than cancel. Therefore full symmetry-packet closure does not structurally kill the order-7 witness. Any cancellation is an incidence condition, not a symmetry identity.

---

### 4. Whitening/projection survival is positive, conditional on the row existing

Agent 4’s result is clean.

If the actual reduced-core derivation produces a row of the form

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]

then whitening and fixed-sector projection do not kill it, because

\[
wI+uS\in\mathfrak f_h
\]

already.

So

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(wI+uS)=wI+uS.
\]

The row can vanish only if:

\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0,
\qquad
q=0,
\qquad
wI+uS=0,
\]

or a Gram/whitening degeneracy occurs. These are good-patch or incidence conditions.

Thus the remaining problem is **not projection**. It is whether the actual reduced-core coefficient contains the row before projection.

---

### 5. \(A_9\) fallback is plausible but unavailable without the formula

Agent 5 confirmed that if \(A_7\) cancels, \(A_9\) is the right fallback.

At the centered packet,

\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})\ne0
\]

for

\[
0<|\delta|<\frac12.
\]

The septic locking relation controls only

\[
A_2,\quad A_4,\quad q,\quad q'',
\]

not \(A_6\). So order 9 should generically restore visibility if the actual \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\) row has an \(A_6\)-channel.

But this remains unproved because the actual reduced-core \(A_9\) formula is missing.

---

## Decision

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not proceed to the rank-two connection theorem yet.}
}
\]

The route is still viable, but packet visibility remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{conditional / open.}
}
\]

The precise missing formula is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr,\core}(s;m),
}
\]

including:

\[
\text{core phase expansion, finite-}s\text{ correction, whitening, and fixed-sector projection.}
\]

If this coefficient is nonzero at the clean packet witness, then:

\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]

is a proper analytic incidence set, and the rank-two route can proceed.

If \(A_7\) cancels, the next formula is:

\[
\boxed{
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
}
\]

specifically the coefficient of the \(A_6\)-channel.

---

## Current proof-state label

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual reduced-core packet visibility is still unresolved, but the gap is now a single coefficient formula.}
}
\]

The next attack should be one derivation, not another architecture wave.

```text
Use the reduced-core convention:
\[
q=q_{\core}+G_{\rm nc},
\qquad
\mathcal P(\rho)\subseteq q_{\core}.
\]

Write the corrected finite-\(s\) object
\[
\widehat\Omega_{\zeta}^{\corr,\core}(s;m)
\]
as explicitly as the draft allows.

Identify all operations that occur before extracting \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\):
- finite-\(s\) numerator/kernel expansion;
- diagonal and off-diagonal entries;
- whitening / Gram normalization;
- subtraction of background or correction terms;
- fixed-sector projection
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}.
\]

2. Expand the core phase at a centered even packet.

Let
\[
u=t-m.
\]

For the centered packet \(x_m=0\), the core phase derivative has even expansion:
\[
q_{\core}(m+u)
=
q_0
+
\frac{q_2}{2}u^2
+
\frac{q_4}{24}u^4
+
\frac{q_6}{720}u^6
+
\frac{q_8}{40320}u^8
+\cdots,
\]
where
\[
q_2=q_{\core}''(m)=2A_2,
\]
\[
q_4=q_{\core}^{(4)}(m)=24A_4.
\]

For the clean packet:
\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243}.
\]

Also record:
\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})
\]
if order 9 becomes necessary.

3. Compute the raw finite-\(s\) order-7 coefficient.

Use the exact reduced-core numerator entries from the draft. At minimum, for the lower-left off-diagonal numerator, verify the expansion of:
\[
N_{21}
=
-\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2},
\]
where
\[
\Delta=\Phi(m+s/2)-\Phi(m-s/2),
\]
\[
q_-=q(m-s/2).
\]

With the centered even expansion, compute:
\[
\Delta
=
q_0s+\frac{q_2}{24}s^3+\frac{q_4}{1920}s^5+\frac{q_6}{322560}s^7+\cdots,
\]
and
\[
q_-
=
q_0+\frac{q_2}{8}s^2+\frac{q_4}{384}s^4+\frac{q_6}{46080}s^6+\cdots.
\]

Then derive or verify:
\[
[s^7]\frac{\sin\Delta+q_-s\cos\Delta}{s^2}
=
\frac{q_0^9}{36288}
-\frac{q_0^6q_2}{1728}
+\frac{q_0^4q_4}{4608}
+\frac{5q_0^3q_2^2}{3456}
-\frac{q_0^2q_6}{64512}
-\frac{q_0q_2q_4}{4608}
-\frac{5q_2^3}{41472}
+\frac{q_8}{9289728}.
\]

Substitute
\[
q_2=2A_2,
\qquad
q_4=24A_4,
\]
and isolate the \(A_2A_4\) and \(A_2^2\) channels.

Important:
The raw reduced-core coefficient is not automatically the final \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\). This step only proves whether the packet jets survive into the raw finite-\(s\) expansion.

4. Apply the actual correction / whitening / projection.

Now use the draft’s actual correction map.

Track how the raw order-7 coefficient changes under:
\[
G^{-1/2}\text{ or whitening},
\]
normalization by \(Q,q\), or related Gram factors,
background/core correction,
and
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}.
\]

You must explicitly answer:

Does the final corrected, whitened fixed-sector coefficient contain a row of the form
\[
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
with
\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
\right]?
\]

Or does the actual reduced-core coefficient contain a modified expression:
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\left[
c_{24}qA_2A_4
+
c_{22,1}q''A_2^2
+
c_{22,2}q^3A_2^2
+
\text{other core terms}
\right]I
+
\left[\cdots\right]S?
\]

If modified, give the exact coefficients and the extra terms.

5. Check for cancellation.

Determine whether core normalization produces an exact cancellation:
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\]
identically for the centered off-line packet family.

If cancellation occurs, identify the precise cancelling terms:
- baseline/core Taylor terms;
- whitening derivative terms;
- fixed-sector projection terms;
- \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-normalization terms;
- full symmetry-packet terms;
- or another term.

Do not merely say “could cancel.” Either derive the cancellation or state that no such cancellation follows from the formula.

6. Evaluate the clean witness.

At the clean values:
\[
\delta=\frac14,
\qquad
x_m=0,
\qquad
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27},
\qquad
A_4=\frac{3997696}{243}.
\]

Use the simplest legitimate good-patch normalization allowed by the draft. If you use:
\[
q=1,\qquad q''=0,\qquad Q=1,
\]
state whether this is:
- a permitted normalization;
- a local model witness;
- or not legitimate for actual reduced-core packets.

Evaluate whether:
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

Also verify the good-patch nondegeneracy:
\[
wI+uS\ne0
\]
or identify the corresponding exceptional set if not.

7. If \(A_7\) cancels, prepare the \(A_9\) fallback.

If the actual reduced-core \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\) vanishes identically or cannot be certified, derive the next required coefficient:
\[
A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^9]\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_{\zeta}^{\corr,\core}(s;m).
\]

At minimum, identify whether \(A_{9,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\) contains an \(A_6\)-channel:
\[

\quad
A_2A_6,
\quad
qA_2A_6,
\quad
\text{or another sixth-jet term}.
\]

Use:
\[
A_6=-64(a^{-7}+b^{-7})\ne0
\]
for
\[

\]

8. Final deliverable.

Give one of the following verdicts:

A. Visibility certified:
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\ne0
\]
for the actual reduced-core off-line packet at a clean good-patch witness. Then state:
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core}
=
\{C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}=0\}
\]
is a proper analytic incidence set.

B. Visibility conditionally certified:
The reduced-core formula contains the nonzero row under explicit assumptions, such as:
\[

\]
and no actual-core locking identity. List the exact assumptions.

C. \(A_7\) cancels, \(A_9\) needed:
Give the exact cancellation and the required \(A_9\) coefficient to compute.

D. Visibility fails:
Prove
\[

\]
for actual reduced-core off-line packets outside incidence. This would kill the rank-two route.

Be explicit. The goal is to decide whether the rank-two route can proceed to the connection theorem:
\[

=

\]
```

## Assistant (2026-04-25 19:34:45)

_Thought for 13s_

## Coordinator verdict

This is a substantial advance. The packet-visibility problem is no longer “find any visibility mechanism.” We now have **two concrete order-7 visibility mechanisms**:

\[
\boxed{\text{non-centered }q^{(7)}\text{ septic }K_1\text{ channel}}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{\text{centered one-whitening-slot }X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}\text{ channel}.}
\]

The centered raw \(N_7\) coefficient itself is **not** the witness: it is skew and killed by fixed-sector projection after leading whitening. But the one-whitening-slot channel converts the skew mixed block into a fixed-sector \(I\)-component and is explicitly nonzero under clean good-patch conditions. 

---

## 1. The centered \(A_2A_4\) raw witness was corrected

The raw reduced-core \(s^7\) numerator is nonzero, but the direct off-diagonal term has the form

\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
-1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

At a centered even packet, leading whitening gives

\[
X_0N_7^{\off}X_0
=
C_7(\det X_0)J,
\]

which remains skew. Therefore

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]

So the raw lower-left \(s^7\) coefficient is not itself a fixed-sector witness. 

---

## 2. The live centered channel is the one-whitening-slot channel

The key channel is

\[
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\]

where the skew quadratic mixed block is

\[
Y=yJ.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

With

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\]

the fixed-sector projection is

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}
\right)
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

The agents computed

\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)}
\]

and

\[
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

Thus this channel is nonzero when

\[
y\ne0,\qquad q''\ne0,\qquad g\ne h.
\]

For the centered off-line packet,

\[
q''=2A_2\ne0.
\]

The quadratic mixed-block coefficient is also nonzero:

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\ne0.
\]

For the clean packet \(\delta=1/4\), the agents also verified \(g\ne h\). So the centered corrected-whitening channel is explicitly nonzero at the channel level. 

---

## 3. Non-centered route is even cleaner

The non-centered route may be the stronger way forward.

The attack confirmed that the draft treats

\[
m
\]

as a free sampling midpoint:

\[
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]

not as a forced zero-packet center. The corrected whitening section uses denominators involving

\[
2m-\gamma_\rho,
\]

so \(x_m=2m-\gamma_\rho\) is a genuine local offset, not constrained to vanish. 

For non-centered \(m\),

\[
q^{(7)}(m)\ne0
\]

generically. Near \(x_m=0\), the seventh derivative has a simple zero:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m
+
O(x_m^3),
\]

so any sufficiently small nonzero perturbation activates the channel. The draft’s septic \(K_1\)-transport slice then gives actual reduced-core order-7 visibility, provided the \(K_1\) transport vector is nonzero. 

This means packet visibility is essentially closed on the visibility-positive reduced base

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\left(
\{x_m=0\}
\cup
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\cup
\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}
\right),
\]

assuming the reduced-good-patch conditions remain strict under small non-centering.

---

## 4. What remains open

The remaining issue is now very specific:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exclude exact cross-channel cancellation among the other order-7 convolution summands.}
}
\]

For centered packets, we have a nonzero channel

\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]

but the full coefficient is

\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\sum_{r+g+b=7}
X_{-,r}N_gX_{+,b}.
\]

So one must still rule out an identity where all other order-7 summands cancel the one-whitening-slot \(I\)-component.

For non-centered packets, the \(q^{(7)}\) \(K_1\)-transport channel is the cleaner witness, but the same formal issue exists: we need to record that cancellation of that channel is a proper analytic incidence condition, not a structural identity.

---

## Decision

The packet-visibility phase is now **effectively conditionally closed**, with the condition sharpened to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the nonzero order-7 visibility channel is not identically cancelled by other order-7 summands.}
}
\]

I would now attack one final local algebra theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Order-7 Channel Independence Theorem}
}
\]

Target form:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\sum_{r+g+b=7}
X_{-,r}N_gX_{+,b}
\not\equiv0
\]

on the reduced off-line packet family, because the nonzero \(K_1\) / one-whitening-slot channel occupies an independent jet/grade/symmetry slot that cannot be cancelled identically by the remaining order-7 terms.

If that theorem succeeds, proceed to the rank-two connection theorem on

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet visibility: channel-level proven; full }A_7^{\mathfrak f}\text{ non-identity awaits cross-channel independence.}
}
\]

Below are six prompts for the **Order-7 Channel Independence Wave**.

This wave attacks the remaining packet-visibility gap:

\[

}

The latest attack established that the direct raw \(N_7^{\off}\) channel is skew and killed by \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\), but the one-whitening-slot channel

\[
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}
\]

has nonzero fixed-sector projection under explicit clean good-patch conditions. The remaining issue is whether the full order-7 convolution can cancel it identically.

# Shared background for all agents

```text id="shared-order7-channel-independence"
We are working on a live RH proof attempt from the latest draft.

Current architecture:
We are on the reduced visibility-positive rank-two fixed-sector base
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\left(
\{x_m=0\}
\cup
\{q^{(7)}=0\}
\cup
\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}
\right),
\]
or, for the centered route, on the centered reduced-core packet with the one-whitening-slot visibility channel.

The fixed-sector bundle is
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to \mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

Packet visibility status:
The direct raw off-diagonal order-7 term
\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,\qquad
J=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\-1&0\end{pmatrix},
\]
is killed by leading whitening and fixed-sector projection:
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]

But the one-whitening-slot channel is live:
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}.
\]

At centered parity:
\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

Write
\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

Then
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
\]

The coefficient pieces are:
\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\qquad
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}),
\]
where
\[
g=\frac{q_0}{\pi},
\qquad
h=\frac1\pi\left(\frac13q_0^3+\frac16q''\right).
\]

The quadratic mixed-block coefficient satisfies, for the centered packet:
\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]

For the clean off-line packet \(\delta=1/4\):
\[
A_2=-\frac{7168}{27}\ne0,
\]
so
\[
q''=2A_2\ne0,
\qquad
y\ne0,
\qquad
g\ne h
\]
at the clean packet model. Therefore the channel
\[
-2yBr\,I
\]
is nonzero.

Remaining gap:
The full order-7 coefficient is
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\sum_{r+g+b=7}
X_{-,r}N_gX_{+,b}.
\]

We have shown one summand is nonzero. We have not yet ruled out exact cancellation by the other order-7 summands.

Target theorem:
\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Order-7 Channel Independence Theorem}
}
\]

Desired result:
The nonzero one-whitening-slot channel occupies an independent jet/grade/parity/transport slot, so it cannot be cancelled identically by the other order-7 summands. Therefore
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}\not\equiv0
\]
on the reduced off-line packet family, outside controlled analytic incidence.

Do not:
- propose another architecture;
- return to scalar/quotient/split/line-bundle repair;
- attack \(\nu=0\);
- proceed to global affine transport yet.

Focus only on the full order-7 convolution, channel independence, and cross-channel cancellation.
```

# Agent 1 — Full order-7 convolution inventory agent

```text id="agent1-order7-convolution-inventory"
You are Agent 1: Full Order-7 Convolution Inventory Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
List every summand in the full order-7 corrected-whitening convolution
\[
\Omega_7
=
[s^7]\left(X_-(s)N(s)X_+(s)\right)
=
\sum_{a+g+b=7}
X_{-,a}N_gX_{+,b}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Enumerate all triples:
\[
(a,g,b),\qquad a+g+b=7.
\]

2. Group the summands by:
   - direct raw numerator terms \(N_7\);
   - one-whitening-slot terms \(X_{\pm,1}N_6X_0\);
   - two-whitening-slot terms;
   - higher-whitening/lower-numerator terms;
   - diagonal versus off-diagonal \(N_g\);
   - fixed-sector, anti-sector, and skew-sector output.

3. Identify the already-live channel:
\[
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

4. Identify every other summand that can produce an \(I\)-component after \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\).

5. Identify every other summand that can produce the **same \(I\)-direction and same jet monomial** as
\[
-2yBr\,I.
\]

6. Mark which summands are ruled out by centered parity, fixed-sector projection, or sector type.

7. Deliver a complete table:
\[
(a,g,b),\quad \text{sector},\quad \text{jet content},\quad \pi_{\mathfrak f}\text{-visibility},\quad \text{can cancel }-2yBrI?
\]

Deliverable:
A full order-7 convolution inventory and a short list of only the summands that could possibly cancel the one-whitening-slot \(I\)-channel.
```

# Agent 2 — Jet-grade / monomial independence agent

```text id="agent2-jet-grade-independence"
You are Agent 2: Jet-Grade / Monomial Independence Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Determine whether the live channel
\[
-2yBr\,I
\]
contains a jet monomial that is independent of all other order-7 summands.

Known pieces:
\[

\[
y_{\rm lead}\propto q_0A_2^2,

and for the centered packet:
\[

\[
q_0 A_2^3 \cdot r \cdot I
\]
or, before substituting \(q''=2A_2\),
\[
q_0 A_2^2 q'' \cdot r \cdot I.
\]

Tasks:
1. Assign jet grades to:
\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad A_2,\quad A_4,\quad A_6,\quad y,\quad B,\quad r.
\]

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})=-2yBr\,I.
\]

3. Inspect all other possible order-7 summands and determine whether any contain the same monomial:
\[
q_0A_2^2q''\,r\,I
\]
or its reduced form
\[
q_0A_2^3 r\,I.
\]

4. If no other summand contains this monomial, prove channel independence.

5. If other summands contain the same monomial, compute their coefficients and signs.

6. Determine whether cancellation would require an algebraic identity such as:
\[
c_{\rm live}+c_{\rm other}=0
\]
with constants, or a nontrivial relation among independent jet variables.

7. If cancellation requires a relation such as:
\[
g=h,\quad A_2=0,\quad y=0,\quad q_0=0,
\]
classify it as incidence.

Deliverable:
A jet-monomial independence theorem or an explicit cancellation formula.
```

# Agent 3 — Sector/parity independence agent

```text id="agent3-sector-parity-independence"
and the commutator:

   - fixed \(I/S\);

5. Determine whether diagonal \(N_7\) terms can produce the same \(I\)-sector with the same parity.
```

# Agent 5 — \(K_1\)-transport isolation agent

```text id="agent5-k1-transport-isolation"
You are Agent 5: \(K_1\)-Transport Isolation Agent.

Use the shared background.

Your task:
Use the draft’s septic decomposition to isolate the \(K_1\)-transport contribution and show it is independent of \(K_5\), \(K_3\), and pure same-point sectors.

Known decomposition:
\[
A_7
=
A_{7,K_1}
+
A_{7,K_5}
+
A_{7,K_3}
+
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}.
\]

Known reductions:
\[
A_{7,K_5}^{\mathfrak f}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
\[
A_{7,K_3}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad \text{or vanishes after fixed-sector projection},
\]
\[
A_{7,\mathrm{pure}}^{\mathfrak f}=0
\quad \text{in the odd two-point germ},
\]
and quotient-level:
\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}]=[A_{7,K_1}^{\mathfrak f}]
\quad
\text{in }
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Tasks:
1. Verify these reductions from the draft.

2. Determine whether the live one-whitening-slot channel belongs to \(K_1\).

3. Prove that \(K_5\)-line terms cannot cancel \(K_1\) in the quotient:
\[
```

## Coordinator verdict

The global affine transport wave is **negative for path / boundary / holonomy / exactness / projective-index routes**, and **conditional for transported finite-core non-concentration**.

The local rank-two architecture is coherent:

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

But it still has no global proof gate. The least-bad continuation is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Transported finite-core non-concentration.}
}
\]

This is not because it is solved. It is because every other global route currently lacks a canonical path, endpoint condition, loop, exactness identity, or complete index invariant. 

---

## 1. Path / boundary route: currently blocked

Agent 1 found no canonical path \(\Gamma\subset\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) with known endpoint constraints for

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The natural local paths are:

\[
\kappa,\quad m,\quad s,\quad \theta.
\]

But none currently supplies endpoint data such as:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)=0,
\qquad
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)=0,
\]

or any prescribed relation between endpoints.

So the affine transport formula

\[
A(b)=U_{a\to b}A(a)+\int_a^bU_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt
\]

is locally valid but not proof-closing. 

---

## 2. Affine holonomy route: currently blocked

Agent 2 found no usable loop theorem.

The affine holonomy object would be:

\[
\operatorname{AffHol}_\Gamma
=
\left(
U_\Gamma,
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower})(t)\,dt
\right).
\]

But we do not currently have:

\[
\boxed{\text{canonical loop }\Gamma}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{global zeta-imposed affine holonomy constraint}}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{\text{off-line packet } \Rightarrow \Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}\ne0}.
}
\]

Loops around core-boundary, visibility, or Gram walls are formal diagnostics, not proof gates yet. 

---

## 3. Exactness / path-independence route: failed under current variables

Agent 3’s result is important and negative.

The scalar part of the active forcing satisfies:

\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
qAA''
+
20\left(\frac{q''}{6}-\frac{2q^3}{3}\right)A^2,
\qquad A=A_2.
\]

After integration by parts:

\[
qAA''+20KA^2
=
\left(qAA'-\frac12q'A^2\right)'
-
q(A')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A^2.
\]

The remaining bulk terms are uncontrolled. Rank-two covariantization makes the row tensorial, but it does **not** make it exact.

So:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\neq \nabla^{\mathfrak f}\Psi
}
\]

under the current variables. Exactness is not the next route. 

---

## 4. Projective / Maslov / spectral-flow route: diagnostic only

Agent 4 found that projective data are coherent but incomplete.

We can define:

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)]\in \mathbf P(\mathcal F_b),
\]

and crossings with

\[
[A_5^{\mathfrak f}(b)]
\]

are detected by:

\[
D_7=\omega_h(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

But projective data alone miss pure line/scale anomalies:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

Also, because the transport is affine rather than homogeneous, projective motion depends on the forcing integral, not just connection holonomy.

So projective/Maslov data should remain a **derived diagnostic**, not the main proof gate. 

---

## 5. Transported finite-core route: least-bad but still hard

Agent 5’s result is sober:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transport data do not automatically close finite-core non-concentration.}
}
\]

A transported finite-core vector could be:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots),
\]

or minimally:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots).
\]

But the old aligned branch can still formally survive:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

So this route needs a real theorem, not just a definition. The target must be a lower bound or incidence exclusion showing that the transported vector cannot align-cancel outside a controlled exceptional set. 

---

## Decision

Proceed to a **Transported Finite-Core Non-Concentration Wave**.

The next theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Transported Finite-Core Non-Concentration Theorem}
}
\]

in the form:

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
\]

The concrete attack is not to prove this abstractly at once. The first job is to test whether adding

\[

E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}

actually kills, weakens, or merely relocates the old aligned branch.

```latex
\subsection{Post-quotient audit: split and line-bundle repairs}
\label{subsec:post-quotient-split-line-bundle-audit}

The no-\(T\) quotient architecture keeps the determinant data
\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f})
=
u_{2r+1}v_5-u_5v_{2r+1}.
\]
This removes the representative-level \(T\)-coordinate, but it also discards
the full \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line.  Thus the pure line anomaly
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
has
\[
D_{2r+1}=0,
\]
while still giving
\[
\Phi_K(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f})
=
2\lambda_{2r+1}v_5,
\qquad
T_{2r+1}
=
\lambda_{2r+1}\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
Consequently the quotient scalar
\[
H_m^{\quot}(s)
=
\omega_h\!\left(
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right)
\]
is analytically coherent but incomplete for the original transform-state
detection problem.

A natural repair is the split readout
\[
\mathcal H_m^{\mathrm{split}}(s)
=
\left(
H_m^{\quot}(s),H_m^\parallel(s)
\right),
\]
where
\[
H_m^\parallel(s)
=
\frac{
\left\langle
\pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m),
A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\left\langle
A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\right\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]
For each coefficient
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
u_{2r+1}I+v_{2r+1}S,
\]
this gives the pair
\[
\left(
D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1}
\right),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_{2r+1}
=
\frac{
\langle A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]
On a good patch, if the whitening metric is fixed and nondegenerate, the pair
\[
(D_{2r+1},\lambda_{2r+1})
\]
recovers the full fixed-sector vector \(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\).  Thus the
split readout repairs the fatal incompleteness of the pure quotient readout.

However, this completeness reintroduces the Bottleneck-C obstruction through
the longitudinal coordinate.  For
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS),
\]
one has
\[
D(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wv_5-u u_5),
\]
and
\[
\lambda(E_{\eta\eta})
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\frac{
\langle wI+uS,A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]
Thus if the split readout is used as a pointwise vanishing gate, then on a
good patch it requires
\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0,
\]
and hence again requires
\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0
\]
unless \(wI+uS\) degenerates.  The split readout is therefore a complete
coordinate system for the fixed-sector vector, not a new closure mechanism.

\begin{remark}[Line-bundle transport attempt]
\label{rem:line-bundle-transport-attempt}
One can try to avoid pointwise vanishing by treating the longitudinal
coordinate as a section of
\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
With a fixed whitening metric, the natural local connection is
\[
\alpha_L
=
\frac{
\langle dA_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}{
\langle A_5^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}\rangle_{\wh}
}.
\]
If
\[
s=\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]
then
\[
\nabla^Ls=(d\lambda+\lambda\alpha_L)A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Locally this is coherent: under
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}\mapsto \mu A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
one has
\[
\alpha_L\mapsto\alpha_L+d\log\mu,
\]
and the covariant derivative transforms correctly.

The obstruction is global.  The construction requires the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)
line and the whitening metric to transform canonically under changes of patch,
source/core window, and whitening convention.  This is not currently proved.
Moreover, no canonical path, boundary condition, or holonomy theorem is
available for \((L,\nabla^L)\), and the longitudinal forcing is not exact in
the natural variables.  Thus line-bundle transport is a useful diagnostic
language but not presently a proof gate.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Current status of quotient, split, and line-bundle repairs]
\label{rem:current-status-quotient-split-line-repairs}
The quotient scalar is invariant but incomplete.  The split readout is complete
but restores the original fixed-sector obstruction.  The line-bundle
connection makes the longitudinal defect locally covariant, but lacks global
covariance, canonical paths, boundary data, exactness, or holonomy control.
Therefore none of these repairs currently replaces pointwise Bottleneck-C
closure.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 2 — Insert rank-two fixed-sector architecture subsection

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 1 and before the finite-core subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Rank-two fixed-sector bundle as the remaining viable language}
\label{subsec:rank-two-fixed-sector-remaining-language}

The preceding failures suggest that the defect should not be scalarized, nor
should one single out the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line as the primary geometric
object.  The best remaining local language is the full rank-two fixed-sector
bundle
\[
\mathcal F\to\mathcal B,
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]
This formulation keeps the whole fixed-sector vector
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\in\mathcal F_b
\]
and therefore avoids the incompleteness of the quotient scalar and the
noncanonical line-preservation problem of \(L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

The local candidate connection is the projected ambient derivative
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\bigl(d_X^{\mathcal J}A\bigr),
\]
where \(\mathcal J\) is the ambient corrected finite-\(s\) jet/kernel-state
bundle, \(d^{\mathcal J}\) is the ambient derivative, and
\[
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}:\mathcal J_b\to\mathfrak f_h(b)
\]
is the fixed-sector projection.  In a local frame
\[
E=(I,S),
\qquad
A=Ea,
\]
the connection has the form
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A
=
E(da+\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}a).
\]
If
\[
E=E^{\rm raw}W,
\]
then formally
\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W+W^{-1}dW.
\]
In particular, if the raw frame is flat in the chart, then
\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}=W^{-1}dW.
\]

On an overlap with
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\]
the connection matrices must satisfy
\[
\Gamma_j
=
G_{ij}^{-1}\Gamma_iG_{ij}
+
G_{ij}^{-1}dG_{ij}.
\]
Thus the rank-two connection is canonical if the fixed-sector frames glue by
canonical \(GL_2\)-transition maps and the fixed-sector projection is
functorial under the ambient transition maps.

\begin{proposition}[Conditional rank-two connection theorem]
\label{prop:conditional-rank-two-connection}
Assume that on a reduced good-patch base \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\):
\begin{enumerate}
\item the core/source convention is fixed and locally stable;
\item no zero moves into or out of \(q_{\core}\);
\item the fixed-sector frames satisfy transition laws
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2(\mathbf C),
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik};
\]
\item the ambient corrected jet bundle \(\mathcal J\) and projection
\(\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\) are functorial under these transitions;
\item the whitening branch and Gram normalization are fixed or functorial.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\]
defines a canonical connection on
\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}.
\]
\end{proposition}

The reduced-base hypotheses are essential.  On the unreduced base, changing the
source/core convention can produce affine corrections
\[
A_j^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_i^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij}.
\]
Such transformations do not define an ordinary vector-bundle connection.  Thus
the present rank-two connection is currently a fixed-convention, reduced-base
object unless an affine torsor transition theorem is proved.

\begin{remark}[Why rank two improves on the line bundle]
\label{rem:rank-two-improves-on-line-bundle}
The \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-line may rotate under legitimate changes of
trivialization, source/core convention, or whitening.  This blocked the
line-bundle route.  The full plane \(\mathfrak f_h=\mathbf C I\oplus\mathbf C S\)
can still transform by a \(GL_2\)-matrix.  Hence the rank-two bundle is the
right level at which to formulate covariance.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 3 — Insert affine forcing theorem subsection

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 2 and before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{The \(\eta\eta\) row as rank-two affine forcing}
\label{subsec:etaeta-row-rank-two-affine-forcing}

In the rank-two formulation, the active Bottleneck-C row is no longer a scalar
defect by itself.  It is a vector-valued section:
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in
\Gamma(\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}).
\]
Under a frame change
\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\]
the coordinate vector of \(wI+uS\) transforms by
\[
[w,u]_j^T
=
G_{ij}^{-1}[w,u]_i^T.
\]
The scalar coefficient
\[
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}
\]
is fixed-convention scalar data.  Therefore \(E_{\eta\eta}\) transforms as a
section of the rank-two fixed-sector bundle, provided the reduced atlas is
functorial.

This row should not be identified with ordinary curvature of
\(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\).  Curvature is antisymmetric in two tangent
directions:
\[
F_{\nabla^{\mathfrak f}}(X,Y)
=
[\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f},\nabla_Y^{\mathfrak f}]
-
\nabla_{[X,Y]}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The active row is symmetric in the source directions \(\eta_i,\eta_j\).  It is
better classified as a symmetric source-Hessian forcing term, or a
second-fundamental-form component, in the fixed-sector transport equation.

The natural local replacement for scalar Bottleneck-C flatness is therefore an
affine transport equation of the form
\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}
+
E_{\rm lower}.
\]
Here \(E_{\rm lower}\) denotes all lower, line, shadow, pure, connection, and
background/core terms.  The expected decomposition is
\[
E_{\rm lower}
=
E_{\rm GateA}
+
E_{\rm GateB}
+
E_{\rm line}
+
E_{K_3}
+
E_{\rm pure}
+
E_{\rm conn}
+
E_{\rm bg/core}
+
E_{K_1}^{\rm comp}.
\]
Under the current local ledger,
\[
E_{\rm GateA}=0,
\qquad
E_{\rm GateB}=0
\]
under the accepted Gate A/B hypotheses,
\[
E_{\rm conn}=0
\]
after passing to the covariant derivative,
\[
E_{K_3}=0
\]
after fixed-sector projection,
\[
E_{\rm pure}=0
\]
in the odd two-point germ, and
\[
E_{\rm line}\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The remaining table dependency is to verify that no additional uncontrolled
same-grade \(K_1\) source-Hessian companion survives outside the already
identified \(E_{\eta\eta}\) row.

\begin{remark}[What the affine equation changes]
\label{rem:what-affine-equation-changes}
The old scalar Bottleneck-C gate demanded local pointwise vanishing of the
\(S\)-visible component.  The rank-two equation instead allows the same row to
be an inhomogeneous forcing term in a vector-valued transport equation.  This
is a genuine conceptual improvement only if a later global theorem controls
the forced transport.  If one still demands
\[
E_{\eta\eta}=0
\]
pointwise, then the rank-two formulation collapses back to the old obstruction
\[
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0
\]
on a good patch.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 4 — Insert global affine transport no-go / dependency subsection

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 3 and before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Global affine transport dependency}
\label{subsec:global-affine-transport-dependency}

Assuming the local affine equation
\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A=E
\]
is available, parallel transport along a path \(\Gamma:a\to b\) gives
\[
A(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A(a)
+
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt.
\]
For the order-seven fixed-sector section this becomes
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A_7^{\mathfrak f}(a)
+
\int_a^b
U_{t\to b}
\left(
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\right)(t)\,dt.
\]
Thus the local Bottleneck-C obstruction becomes an affine displacement
problem.

At present no canonical global proof gate for this displacement is available.
The natural path and boundary candidates have the following status:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\kappa\)-paths are locally natural but have no known endpoint values for
\(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\).
\item midpoint paths \(m\mapsto b(m)\) are natural locally, but good-patch
boundaries are exceptional walls rather than known boundary conditions.
\item source/core deformation paths are excluded on the reduced base, since
source/core transfer is not functorial as an ordinary vector-bundle
transition.
\item Gram or whitening loops may measure gauge/atlas data rather than zeta
geometry unless a global atlas theorem is proved.
\item zero-counting contours are canonical for \(\xi\) or \(\zeta\), but no
map from those contours into the rank-two fixed-sector base is currently
constructed.
\end{itemize}

Nor is the forcing currently exact.  In the fixed-source midpoint calculus, the
active scalar density satisfies
\[
2880Q^{14}\nu_{\eta\eta}
=
qAA''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A^2,
\qquad
A=A_2.
\]
Integration by parts yields
\[
qAA''
+
20
\left(
\frac{q''}{6}
-
\frac{2q^3}{3}
\right)A^2
=
\left(qAA'-\frac12 q'A^2\right)'
-
q(A')^2
+
\left(
\frac{23}{6}q''
-
\frac{40}{3}q^3
\right)A^2.
\]
The last two terms are genuine bulk terms.  Therefore the forcing is not
presently a boundary term in the natural variables.

\begin{remark}[Current global dependency]
\label{rem:current-global-affine-transport-dependency}
The rank-two affine equation is currently descriptive rather than
contradictory.  To turn it into a proof gate one needs one of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item canonical boundary values for \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\);
\item a canonical path or loop with prescribed affine holonomy;
\item a path-independent affine displacement theorem;
\item a projective/scale index theorem derived from the rank-two transport;
\item a transported finite-core non-concentration theorem for the full
fixed-sector vector.
\end{enumerate}
None of these is presently proved.
\end{remark}
```

## Edit 5 — Insert projective / vector / energy diagnostics subsection

**Where:** Immediately after Edit 4 and before finite-core.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Derived diagnostics: projective, vector-valued, and energy data}
\label{subsec:derived-diagnostics-projective-vector-energy}

Several objects remain useful as diagnostics, but none currently replaces the
rank-two affine transport theorem.

First, projectivizing the fixed-sector vector gives
\[
\ell_{2r+1}(m)
=
[A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)]
\in
\mathbf P(\mathfrak f_h(m)).
\]
The quotient determinant is exactly projective incidence:
\[
D_{2r+1}
=
\omega_h(A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f},A_5^{\mathfrak f}),
\]
and
\[
D_{2r+1}=0
\iff
\ell_{2r+1}=\ell_5.
\]
Thus projective/Maslov/spectral-flow data recover the quotient determinant
geometry.  They remain incomplete by themselves because pure line anomalies
\[
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda A_5^{\mathfrak f}
\]
are projectively invisible but still visible to \(T\) and \(\Phi_K\).  A
projective index would therefore need to be paired with scale, energy, or the
full rank-two connection.

Second, the complete local fixed-sector object is the vector-valued odd germ
\[
\mathcal A_{\odd}^{\mathfrak f}(s;m)
=
\sum_{r\ge0}
A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}(m)s^{2r+1}
\in
\mathfrak f_h(m).
\]
It retains all fixed-sector information, preserves componentwise holomorphy
and Cauchy recovery, and avoids the incompleteness of quotient scalarization.
However, it is essentially the full fixed-sector version of the split readout.
It does not by itself prove the required finite-core lower bound
\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\vec f}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\vec f}
\Longrightarrow
\left\|
P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(\theta(m))
+
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}(\theta(m))
\right\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\vec f}(m,Q).
\]
The aligned branch
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
\]
therefore remains a genuine downstream dependency.

Third, one may define fixed-sector energies such as
\[
\mathcal E_7
=
\|A_7^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2
\]
or
\[
\mathcal E_{\odd}
=
\sum_r \omega_r
\|A_{2r+1}^{\mathfrak f}\|_{\wh}^2.
\]
For
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
\gamma(wI+uS),
\]
the first variation of \(\mathcal E_7\) contains
\[
2\operatorname{Re}\left[
\gamma\,
\langle A_7^{\mathfrak f},wI+uS\rangle_{\wh}
\right],
\]
which is sign-indefinite.  The second variation is positive but tautological:
\[
2|\gamma|^2\|wI+uS\|_{\wh}^2\ge0.
\]
No zero-energy, monotonicity, or endpoint theorem is presently available.
Thus energy detects the defect but does not yet provide a contradiction.

\begin{remark}[Role of Gate A and Gate B after the architecture audits]
\label{rem:role-of-gate-a-b-after-audits}
Gate A and Gate B should be retained as local algebraic lemmas:
\[
\text{Gate A: aggregate homogeneous cancellation,}
\]
\[
\text{Gate B: conditional local quotient/fixed-sector algebra through order }7.
\]
They simplify the local expansion and help classify lower terms.  They are not
proof-closing global gates.  The missing theorem is now a global statement
about rank-two affine transport, vector-valued finite-core non-concentration,
or a comparable non-scalar invariant.
\end{remark}
```

```latex
\begin{remark}[Audit convention for the current proof-state section]
\label{rem:audit-convention-current-proof-state}
The statements in this section distinguish three levels:
\begin{enumerate}

source/core and grading conventions;
```

# Edit 2 — Add actual one-pair source-jet no-locking formulas

**Where:** Immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{Source-convention rebuild and persistence of the \(\eta\eta\) row}
\label{subsec:source-convention-rebuild-etaeta-row}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Actual exterior-pair source jets and failure of pair-level locking}
\label{subsec:actual-exterior-pair-source-jets-no-locking}

The most direct possible rescue of the Bottleneck-C row would be a hidden
actual-source relation forcing the midpoint post-affine source jets
\[
\rho_2,\qquad \rho_4
\]
to satisfy the ratio required by the \(\eta\eta\) top-row coefficient.  This
does not occur at the one-pair level.

For an exterior functional-equation zero-pair write
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}.
\]
Put
\[
a:=1-\beta,\qquad b:=\beta,\qquad x:=2m-\gamma,\qquad u:=t-m.
\]
Then
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(m+u)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+(x+2u)^2}
+
\frac{b}{b^2+(x+2u)^2}.
\]
Affine subtraction removes only the constant and linear terms.  Thus the
post-affine coefficients \(\rho_2,\rho_4\) are the \(u^2,u^4\) coefficients of
the above expansion.

For one summand,
\[
[u^2]\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2}
=
\frac{4c(3x^2-c^2)}{(c^2+x^2)^3},
\]
and
\[
[u^4]\frac{c}{c^2+(x+2u)^2}
=
\frac{16c(c^4-10c^2x^2+5x^4)}{(c^2+x^2)^5}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\rho_2(\beta,x)
=
4a\frac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
4b\frac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\rho_4(\beta,x)
=
16a\frac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
16b\frac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}.
}
\]

\begin{proposition}[No one-pair jet-locking law]
\label{prop:no-one-pair-jet-locking-law}
For \(\rho_2(\beta,x)\ne0\), the ratio
\[
\frac{\rho_4(\beta,x)}{\rho_2(\beta,x)}
=
4
\frac{
a\dfrac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
b\dfrac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}
}{
a\dfrac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
b\dfrac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3}
}
\]
is a nonconstant rational function of the exterior-pair parameters.  In
particular, the actual one-pair source class does not force
\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed formulas are obtained by Taylor expanding the two summands at
\(u=0\).  The ratio \(\rho_4/\rho_2\) depends on the one-pair parameters
\((\beta,x)\), while the Bottleneck-C locking ratio depends on the local
baseline phase jets \(q_0,q_0''\).  There is no source-internal identity
equating these quantities.
\end{proof}

Two useful checks are:
\[
\beta=\frac12,\quad x=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\rho_2=-64,\qquad \rho_4=1024,\qquad
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}=-16,
\]
and, as \(|x|\to\infty\),
\[
\rho_2=\frac{12}{x^4}+O(x^{-6}),
\qquad
\rho_4=\frac{80}{x^6}+O(x^{-8}),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4}).
}
\]
Thus far exterior source atoms approximate the formal bad germ \(r(u)=u^2\)
to finite jet order.  Any cancellation of the aggregate Bottleneck-C
coefficient must therefore be a genuine global zero-tail identity, not a
pair-level source rigidity law.
```

# Edit 3 — Add renormalized-complement / ODE no-go

```latex
\begin{remark}[Source-tagging and renormalized-complement ODEs]
\label{rem:source-tagging-renormalized-complement-ode-no-go}
The quantities \(A_2^{\new}\) and \(A_4^{\new}\) in the rebuilt
Bottleneck-C coefficient are the second and fourth midpoint jets of the
tagged zero-source object
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\mathrm{aux},R}+T_{\mathrm{far},R},
\]
after affine subtraction.  They are not the corresponding jets of
\[
q-q_{\core},
\qquad
B_{\bg}+T_{\far,R}+E_{\est,R},
\qquad
q,
\]
or any other renormalized complement unless the entire finite-\(s\) row is
rebuilt.

Thus an ODE for a different complement does not affect the already-derived
row.  In the present source convention, the only relevant derivative-ratio
identity is
\[
\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}(m)}{(G^{\new})''(m)}
=
\frac{40(q_0^{\new})^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_0^{\new})''}{3q_0^{\new}}.
\]
No ODE, meromorphic identity, moving-cutoff identity, or standard
\(\xi'/\xi\) phase-calculus identity currently supplies this condition.

Moreover, near an exterior zero-source pole \(p\) in \(G^{\new}\),
\[
G^{\new}(t)\sim \frac{C}{t-p},
\qquad
(G^{\new})''(t)\sim \frac{2C}{(t-p)^3},
\qquad
(G^{\new})^{(4)}(t)\sim \frac{24C}{(t-p)^5},
\]
so
\[
\frac{(G^{\new})^{(4)}}{(G^{\new})''}
\sim
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}.
\]
But \(q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}\) does not contain that
exterior pole, so the right-hand side
\[
\frac{40(q_{\base}^{\new})^2}{3}
-
\frac{10(q_{\base}^{\new})''}{3q_{\base}^{\new}}
\]
has no matching pole there.  Hence the required equation is not a meromorphic
identity for the source-compatible complement.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 4 — Add reduced visibility-positive base and packet visibility

**Where:** Insert immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{Reduced core, packet visibility, and the visibility-positive base}
\label{subsec:reduced-core-packet-visibility-base}

The rank-two architecture is only meaningful after fixing the source/core
convention.  Arbitrary transfers of zero atoms between source and core are not
currently functorial.  Moving a single zero contribution \(q_\rho\) from source
to core changes the local corrected object, not merely its coordinates.  At
coefficient level one should expect
\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{\rho,2r+1},
\]
not a pure \(GL_2\)-transition.  Therefore source/core moves are excluded from
the atlas rather than transported.

We use the canonical reduced-core rule
\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]
Let
\[
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}
=
\mathcal E_{\rm geom}
\cup
\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary},
\]
where \(\mathcal E_{\rm core\ boundary}\) includes nearest-packet ties,
same-scale boundary, symmetry-closure ambiguity, endpoint-gap collapse, zero
collision or multiplicity, Gram/whitening singularity, and patch-boundary
failure.  Define
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}\), the selected core is locally constant as a
labelled symmetry-closed packet.

The RH-relevant local object is not a single zero but the symmetry packet
\[
\mathcal P(\rho)
=
\{\rho,\bar\rho,1-\rho,1-\bar\rho\},
\qquad
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne\frac12.
\]
Packet-level ordering is essential: functional-equation and conjugation
symmetries force internal equalities inside \(\mathcal P(\rho)\), and these
should not be counted as core-selection failures.  The dangerous tie walls are
ties between distinct packets.

For packet visibility, set
\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}.
\]
For the centered one-whitening-slot route, the incidence walls include
\[
\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\},
\]
and, when quotient isolation is used, also \(\{v_5=0\}\).  For the
non-centered \(q^{(7)}\)-transport route, include
\[
\{q^{(7)}=0\}\cup\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the off-line packet fixed-sector visibility
vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots)
\]
is nonzero modulo these explicit incidence exclusions.
```

# Edit 5 — Add order-7 packet visibility / one-whitening-slot theorem

**Where:** After the conditional rank-two connection theorem, or immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{The \(\eta\eta\) row as rank-two affine forcing}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Order-seven packet visibility on the reduced base}
\label{subsec:order-seven-packet-visibility-reduced-base}

The first admissible visibility coefficient is not \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\),
which defines the reference line, but \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\).  The direct raw
off-diagonal order-seven term is not itself the witness.  At a centered even
packet,
\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
-1&0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Since \(X_{-,0}=X_{+,0}=X_0\),
\[
X_0N_7^{\off}X_0=C_7(\det X_0)J,
\]
so
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]

The live centered channel is instead the one-whitening-slot term
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]
At centered parity,
\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]
Write
\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS.
\]
Then
\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
yB(SJX_0-X_0JS)
=
-2yB(pD+rI),
\]
and hence
\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})=-2yBr\,I.
}
\]

For the centered off-line packet,
\[
q''=2A_2,
\qquad
A_2=-4(a^{-3}+b^{-3})\ne0,
\]
and
\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}.
\]
Moreover
\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\qquad
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]
Thus the one-whitening-slot channel is nonzero outside the explicit incidence
walls
\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

There is also a non-centered visibility route.  The local construction uses
\[
t_\pm=m\pm\frac{s}{2},
\]
so \(m\) is a sampling midpoint, not necessarily the zero-packet center.  For
the paired packet
\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{a}{a^2+x^2}+\frac{b}{b^2+x^2},
\qquad x=2t-\gamma,
\]
one has, near \(x_m=2m-\gamma=0\),
\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3).
\]
Thus \(x_m=0\) is a simple zero of \(q^{(7)}(m)\), and every sufficiently small
nonzero perturbation of \(m\) activates the septic \(K_1\)-transport slice,
outside
\[
q^{(7)}=0,
\qquad
\Xi_{K_1}=0.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Packet visibility on \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\)]
\label{prop:packet-visibility-on-bred-plus}
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), the finite fixed-sector vector
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},A_9^{\mathfrak f},\ldots)
\]
is nonzero for the reduced off-line packet family.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For the centered route, the direct skew \(N_7^{\off}\)-term projects to zero,
but the one-whitening-slot \(K_1\)-channel has fixed-sector projection
\[
-2yBr\,I,
\]
which is nonzero outside \(\{y=0\}\cup\{q''=0\}\cup\{g=h\}\).

For the non-centered route, \(m\) is a free sampling midpoint.  The expansion
of \(q^{(7)}(m)\) shows that \(q^{(7)}=0\) is a proper analytic wall near the
packet center.  Away from this wall and from \(\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}\), the septic
\(K_1\)-transport slice gives \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Order-seven channel independence ledger]
\label{rem:order-seven-channel-independence-ledger}
The full order-seven corrected-whitening coefficient is
\[
A_{7,\core}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\sum_{a+g+b=7}
X_{-,a}N_gX_{+,b}.
\]
The direct skew \(N_7^{\off}\)-term is killed by \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\).  The
live one-whitening-slot term belongs to the \(K_1\)-transport sector.  \(K_3\)
shadow terms are projected away, pure same-point septic terms vanish in the
odd two-point germ, and \(K_5\)-terms lie in
\[
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Thus exact cancellation of the live \(-2yBr\,I\) channel can only come from a
same \(K_1\)-transport contribution or a direct diagonal \(N_7\)-term with the
same jet monomial.  No structural identity forcing such cancellation is
currently present; such cancellation is included in the visibility incidence
locus.
\end{remark}
```

after the displayed decomposition of \(E_{\rm lower}\), and before the existing explanatory paragraph.

```latex
The current local row table is:
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{row class} & \text{source} & \text{fixed-sector status}
& \text{present role}\\ \hline
E_{\rm GateA}
& \text{aggregate homogeneous scalar-grade rows}
& 0
& \text{closed by Gate A}\\
E_{\rm GateB}
& \text{ordinary order }\le 7\text{ local rows}
& 0
& \text{closed by Gate B hypotheses}\\
E_{\eta\eta}
& \text{symmetric second-source Hessian / mixed-block row}
& -\dfrac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
& \text{retained as affine forcing}\\
E_{\rm line}
& K_5\text{ normalization shadows}
& \in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}
& \text{transported line term}\\

& \text{pure same-point septic sector}
& 0
& \text{vanishes in odd two-point germ}\\
E_{\rm conn}
& \text{frame/projection/whitening gauge motion}
& 0
& \text{absorbed by }\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\\
E_{\rm bg/core}
& \text{fixed background/core baseline terms}
& \text{fixed analytic section}
& \text{included in affine forcing}
\end{array}
\]

Thus, under the current local ledger,
\[
E_{\rm GateA}=0,
\qquad
E_{\rm GateB}=0
\]
under the accepted Gate A/B hypotheses,
\[
E_{\rm conn}=0
\]
after passing to the covariant derivative,
\[
E_{K_3}=0,
\qquad
E_{\rm pure}=0,
\]
and
\[
E_{\rm line}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
The visibility-positive incidence exclusions used to define
\(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\) do not alter Gate A/B; they only restrict the
base to points where the packet-visibility channel is active.

\begin{theorem}[Conditional local rank-two affine forcing equation]
\label{thm:conditional-local-rank-two-affine-forcing}
On \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\), assume the rank-two connection theorem and
the row-table classifications above.  Then
\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower},
\]
where
\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]
is a tensorial section of \(\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\), and \(E_{\rm lower}\)
contains only Gate A/B-closed, connection-absorbed, line, shadow, pure,
background/core, and already-classified analytic forcing terms.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By definition,
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
[s^7]\Pi_{\mathfrak f}\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}(s;m).
\]
The projected connection gives
\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}d_\kappa^{\mathcal J}
\left([s^7]\widehat\Omega_\zeta^{\corr}\right),
\]
so frame, projection, and whitening-gauge variations are absorbed into
\(\nabla^{\mathfrak f}\).  The \(\eta_i\eta_j\) second-source Hessian row of
the promoted mixed block gives \(E_{\eta\eta}\).  All remaining terms are
classified by the displayed table.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The equation is local, not yet global]
\label{rem:local-affine-forcing-not-global}
Theorem~\ref{thm:conditional-local-rank-two-affine-forcing} does not prove a
global contradiction.  It changes the local interpretation of the
Bottleneck-C row: the row is no longer a scalar defect demanding pointwise
vanishing, but an inhomogeneous forcing term in a rank-two transport equation.
A global boundary, holonomy, exactness, index, or transported finite-core
non-concentration theorem is still required.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 7 — Add global affine transport no-go / dependency

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{Global affine transport dependency}
```

after the current main transport identity.

**Insert:**

```latex
For a loop \(\Gamma\) based at \(b\), the corresponding affine holonomy data are
\[
\operatorname{AffHol}_\Gamma
=
\left(
U_\Gamma,
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
\right),
\]
where
\[
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
=
\int_\Gamma
U_{t\to b}
\left(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}\right)(t)\,dt.
\]
A holonomy proof gate would need all of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a canonical loop \(\Gamma\subset\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\);
\item a global theorem constraining \(U_\Gamma\);
\item a global zeta-theoretic law forcing \(\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}=0\), or a
prescribed value;
\item an off-line-packet theorem forcing an incompatible value of
\(\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}\).
\end{enumerate}
None of these is presently available.

\begin{remark}[Affine holonomy is not presently a proof gate]
\label{rem:affine-holonomy-not-proof-gate}
Loops around core-boundary walls, packet-visibility incidence walls, Gram
singularities, or whitening branch loci are diagnostic but not currently
canonical RH objects.  A loop around a core-boundary wall may change labels or
source/core convention; a Gram loop may measure only gauge or atlas monodromy;
and zero-counting contours live in the complex zeta plane, not yet in the
rank-two fixed-sector base \(\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}\).  Thus affine holonomy
cannot presently replace the local affine forcing equation.  The most
plausible global successors are real path/boundary transport or a transported
finite-core non-concentration theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Global proof gate after local affine forcing]
\label{rem:global-proof-gate-after-local-affine-forcing}
The local affine forcing equation is not a contradiction.  It gives
\[
A(b)
=
U_{a\to b}A(a)
+
\int_a^b U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt,
\qquad
E=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]
To become proof-relevant, this identity needs one of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a canonical path \(\Gamma\) with known endpoint values for
\(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\);
\item a canonical loop with prescribed affine holonomy;
\item a path-independent affine displacement theorem;
\item a projective-plus-scale index theorem tied to the rank-two section;
\item a transported finite-core non-concentration theorem.
\end{enumerate}
At present, none is proved.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 8 — Add transported finite-core non-concentration note

**Where:** Immediately before:

```latex
\subsection{Finite-core sampled vector non-concentration}
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Visibility is not non-concentration]
\label{rem:visibility-not-nonconcentration}
The order-seven packet-visibility result proves that the relevant fixed-sector
vector is not identically zero on the reduced visibility-positive base.  It
does not prove the sampled finite-core lower bound.  The aligned branch
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\vec f}
\]
remains possible until a vector-valued non-concentration, cone-control,
interaction-rigidity, or transport-index theorem rules it out.  Thus
visibility closes the local detection problem but not the global sampling
problem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Transported finite-core data do not remove alignment]
\label{rem:transported-finite-core-data-do-not-remove-alignment}
One may try to strengthen the finite-core vector by adding covariant transport
data, for instance
\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots).
\]
Using the local affine equation, this is equivalent to adding
\[
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]
as additional coordinates.  This is coherent, but it does not by itself prove
sampled non-concentration.  The old aligned branch simply becomes
\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]
Adding derivative or forcing coordinates enlarges the finite vector but does
not impose a sign, cone, monotonicity, or endpoint constraint that forbids
alignment.  A transported finite-core theorem would therefore require a new
coercivity, boundary, incidence, or cone-control input.
\end{remark}
```
