## Assistant (2026-04-25 20:34:47)

_Thought for 5s_

## Executive summary

This push moved the project from “try to repair Bottleneck C” to a cleaner architectural state:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Scalar / quotient / split / line-bundle Bottleneck-C repairs are exhausted.}
}
\]

The surviving local architecture is now:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two fixed-sector affine transport on a reduced visibility-positive base.}
}
\]

The active row

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\]

should no longer be treated as a scalar defect to kill pointwise. It is better treated as a vector-valued affine forcing term in

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
\]

That is a real conceptual improvement. It does **not** prove RH. It gives us a coherent local transport framework. The remaining proof problem is global.

---

# 1. Main progress in this push

## 1.1 Bottleneck-C repair routes are now cleanly classified as no-gos

We tested and recorded the failures of:

\[
\Phi_K\text{-scalar }T\text{-flatness},
\]

\[
\Theta_\pm\text{ normal coordinates / formal counterterms},
\]

\[
\text{quotient-only determinant readout},
\]

\[
\text{split readout }(D,\lambda),
\]

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ line-bundle transport},
\]

\[
\text{endpoint symmetrization / alternative finite-}s\text{ carriers},
\]

\[
\text{source-convention rebuilds},
\]

\[
\text{exactness / residue / ODE rescue}.
\]

The key conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any transform-faithful pointwise Bottleneck-C closure still sees the }S\text{-visible row.}
}
\]

So pointwise closure reduces to an unproved identity:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]

The recent source and ODE audits show that this identity is not forced by one-pair zeta source geometry, formal local source geometry, endpoint symmetrization, source splitting, exactness, or meromorphic residue calculus. 

---

## 1.2 Actual one-pair source geometry was computed

We derived the actual exterior-pair source jets. For

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

with

\[
a=1-\beta,\qquad b=\beta,\qquad x=2m-\gamma,
\]

the post-affine source coefficients are

\[
\rho_2
=
4a\frac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
4b\frac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3},
\]

and

\[
\rho_4
=
16a\frac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
16b\frac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}.
\]

This showed that the needed locking law

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}
\]

is **not** intrinsic to a single actual zeta zero pair.

The far-tail asymptotic

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4})
\]

also shows that exterior-pair sources approximate the formal bad germ \(r(u)=u^2\). 

---

## 1.3 Source-convention rebuild was tested and failed to remove the obstruction

The most plausible rebuild was:

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

This is the cleanest non-core zero-source convention. It avoids treating a raw cutoff tail as the only source.

But the rederived coefficient has the same form:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
\]

So the rebuild does not close Bottleneck C. It only moves the required identity to the full non-core zero complement.

---

## 1.4 The reduced fixed-core base was clarified

We now know that the rank-two route must run on a reduced fixed-convention base:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

The canonical core rule is:

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]

This avoids arbitrary source/core transfers. That matters because source/core transfers are not known to be \(GL_2\)-functorial; they can be affine:

\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij,2r+1}.
\]

So they are excluded from the rank-two vector-bundle atlas unless a future affine-cocycle theorem is proved.

## 1.5 Packet visibility is now essentially solved locally

This is the biggest positive development.

Earlier, the raw centered \(N_7^{\off}\) term looked promising, but we found:

\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J
\]

is skew, so

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]

That raw channel is **not** the witness.

The live centered visibility channel is the one-whitening-slot term:

\[
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

At centered parity,

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

With

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\]

we get

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}+X_{-,0}YX_{+,1}
\right)
=
-2yBr\,I.
}
\]

The factors are explicit:

\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\qquad
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

For a centered off-line packet,

\[
q''=2A_2\ne0,
\]

and

\[
y_{\rm lead}=-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}\ne0.
\]

Thus the channel is nonzero outside explicit incidence:

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

The non-centered route is even cleaner. Since \(m\) is a free sampling midpoint, not the packet center, we can take

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma\ne0.
\]

Then

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3),
\]

so \(q^{(7)}\ne0\) for nearby non-centered midpoints. This activates the septic \(K_1\)-transport channel. 

The practical result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet visibility is closed on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\text{ modulo explicit analytic incidence.}
}
\]

\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},

=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).

In a local frame \(E=(I,S)\),

Find canonical \(a,b,\Gamma\) such that:

=

+

\]

has known endpoint constraints.

\]

Currently missing.

### Option B — Affine holonomy theorem

Find a canonical loop \(\Gamma\) such that:

\[
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}
=
\int_\Gamma U_{t\to b}E(t)\,dt
\]

is globally constrained, and off-line zeros force the opposite.

Needed:

\]

\]

\]

Currently missing.

=

\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
\]

This is probably the most plausible next route, but it is hard.

### Option D — Projective-plus-scale index theorem

Use projective motion plus scale:

\[

\]

plus norm/scale along the fixed-sector plane.

Needed:

\[

\]

\[

\]

\[
\text{global zeta symmetry forces zero index}.
\]

This is speculative.

## Theorem 5 — RH contradiction

Finally, one must prove:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\Longrightarrow
\text{nonzero affine transport / nonzero index / nonzero transported finite-core vector},
\]

while global zeta structure implies the opposite:

\[
\text{global zeta constraints}
\Longrightarrow
\text{zero affine displacement / forbidden index / impossible finite-core vector}.
\]

This is the actual RH step.

Right now, we do **not** have this theorem.

# Edit 1 — Add full-phase \(Q=b+G\) pointwise-flatness no-go

**Where:** Insert immediately after:

\subsection{Local Bottleneck-C ledger after repair attempts}
\label{subsec:local-bottleneck-c-ledger-after-repairs}

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Last-chance pointwise flatness in full phase variables}
\label{subsec:last-chance-pointwise-flatness-full-phase-variables}

The rebuilt source convention removes the unstable-cutoff objection by using
the full non-core zero complement
\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]
A final possible escape is that the exact decomposition of the full phase
derivative into rebuilt baseline and non-core complement might itself force
the Bottleneck-C flatness identity.  This subsection records that it does not.

Write
\[
Q(t):=q(t)
\]
for the full phase derivative, and decompose
\[
Q(t)=b(t)+G(t),
\]
where
\[
b(t):=q_{\base}^{\new}(t)
=
q_{\core}(t)+B_{\bg}(t)+E_{\est,R}(t),
\]
and
\[
G(t):=G^{\new}(t)=q_{\aux,R}(t)+T_{\far,R}(t).
\]
At the midpoint \(m\), put
\[
b_0:=b(m),
\qquad
b_2:=b''(m),
\]
and
\[
A_2:=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4:=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
Then
\[
A_2=\frac{Q''(m)-b''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{Q^{(4)}(m)-b^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]

The rebuilt Bottleneck-C flatness condition is
\[
\frac{b_0}{240}A_2A_4
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{b_2}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
A_2^2
=0.
\]
Substitution gives
\[
\frac{b_0}{11520}
\bigl(Q''-b''\bigr)
\bigl(Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}\bigr)
+
\frac{1}{576}
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
\bigl(Q''-b''\bigr)^2
=0,
\]
with all derivatives evaluated at \(m\).  Equivalently, if
\[
D_2:=Q''-b''=G'',
\qquad
D_4:=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}=G^{(4)},
\]
then the condition is
\[
D_2
\left[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
\right]
=0.
\]

\begin{proposition}[The rebuilt flatness equation is an extra fourth-order constraint]
\label{prop:rebuilt-flatness-extra-fourth-order-constraint}
The identity
\[
Q=b+G
\]
does not imply
\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
\]
On a good patch with \(G''(m)\ne0\), pointwise flatness is equivalent to the
additional derivative-ratio constraint
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
b^{(4)}(m)
=
Q^{(4)}(m)
-
\left(
\frac{40b(m)^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b(m)}
\right)
\bigl(Q''(m)-b''(m)\bigr).
\]
Thus the desired flatness is not a consequence of the tautological full-phase
decomposition.  It is an extra nonlinear fourth-order pointwise condition on
the selected baseline/source split.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed factorization shows that, if \(D_2=G''(m)\ne0\), the vanishing
condition is precisely
\[
b_0D_4
+
20
\left(
\frac{b''}{6}
-
\frac{2b_0^3}{3}
\right)
D_2
=0.
\]
Dividing by \(b_0D_2\) gives
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{G''(m)}
=
\frac{40b_0^2}{3}
-
\frac{10b''(m)}{3b_0}.
\]
The equivalent formula for \(b^{(4)}\) follows from
\[
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]
The decomposition \(Q=b+G\) supplies only
\[
G''=Q''-b'',
\qquad
G^{(4)}=Q^{(4)}-b^{(4)}.
\]
It supplies no relation fixing \(G^{(4)}/G''\) in terms of \(b,b''\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why defining the baseline by flatness is circular]
\label{rem:baseline-by-flatness-is-circular}
One could formally choose \(b\) by requiring the fourth-order equation in
Proposition~\ref{prop:rebuilt-flatness-extra-fourth-order-constraint}.  Such a
choice would kill the Bottleneck-C row by definition.  It is not a proof
unless an independent zeta-side principle selects exactly this baseline, for
example through the functional equation, a canonical scattering law, a
zero-counting conservation principle, or a functorial fixed-core construction.
No such principle is currently present.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Asymptotic scale is not an identity]
\label{rem:asymptotic-scale-not-identity}
If \(b\) is dominated by the smooth phase/background, one expects roughly
\[
b(t)\sim \frac12\log(t/2\pi).
\]
Then the required ratio has scale
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
\sim
\frac{40}{3}b^2
\asymp
\log^2 t.
\]
A non-core zero complement with pole distances of order \(1/\log t\) can have
the same dimensional scale.  This is not enough: the identity requires the
exact constant and sign
\[
\frac{40b^2}{3}-\frac{10b''}{3b}
\]
pointwise.  Local one-pair and finite-tail tests show that source geometry can
produce different fourth-to-second derivative ratios.  Thus a proof of
flatness would have to be a genuinely new global zero-complement rigidity
theorem.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 2 — Add meromorphic ODE principal-part no-go

**Where:** Insert immediately after:

and before the next subsection.

**Insert:**

```latex
\subsection{Meromorphic ODE principal-part no-go}
\label{subsec:meromorphic-ode-principal-part-no-go}

A related failed repair is to seek a meromorphic differential equation for the
source complement or for the full phase derivative.  The local flatness
condition would be implied by an equation of the form
\[
\frac{G^{(4)}}{G''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q},
\]
or by the same equation with \(G=q\).  This is incompatible with the principal
parts of the actual zero-pair pole fields.

Let
\[
H(t)=\frac{C}{t-p}+O(1)
\]
have a simple pole.  Then
\[
H''(t)=\frac{2C}{(t-p)^3}+O(1),
\qquad
H^{(4)}(t)=\frac{24C}{(t-p)^5}+O(1),
\]
so
\[
\frac{H^{(4)}}{H''}
=
\frac{12}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]

On the other hand, if the full phase derivative has
\[
q(t)=\frac{R}{t-p}+O(1),
\]
then
\[
q^2(t)=\frac{R^2}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right),
\qquad
\frac{q''}{q}
=
\frac{2}{(t-p)^2}+O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]
Hence
\[
\frac{40q^2}{3}-\frac{10q''}{3q}
=
\left(
\frac{40R^2}{3}
-
\frac{20}{3}
\right)
\frac1{(t-p)^2}
+
O\!\left(\frac1{t-p}\right).
\]
Matching the left-hand double-pole coefficient \(12\) would require
\[
R^2=\frac75.
\]

\begin{proposition}[Zero-pair residues rule out the meromorphic ODE repair]
\label{prop:zero-pair-residues-rule-out-meromorphic-ode}
The flatness-forcing ODE
\[
\frac{H^{(4)}}{H''}
=
\frac{40q^2}{3}
-
\frac{10q''}{3q}
\]
cannot hold as a meromorphic identity for the raw non-core zero source, for the
full phase derivative, or for any complement retaining the zero-pair poles.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For a zero-pair summand
\[
f_a(t)=\frac{a}{a^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]
the poles are
\[
p_a^\pm=\frac{\gamma\pm ia}{2},
\]
with residues
\[
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^+} f_a=-\frac{i}{4},
\qquad
\operatorname{Res}_{p_a^-} f_a=\frac{i}{4}.
\]
Thus the phase-pole residues are purely imaginary.  For a simple pole,
\[
R=\pm \frac{i}{4},
\]
so
\[
R^2=-\frac1{16},
\]
not \(7/5\).  If several same-sign pole contributions coincide, then
\[
R=\pm \frac{ni}{4},
\]
and still \(R^2<0\).  Therefore the right-hand double-pole coefficient cannot
match the coefficient \(12\) of \(H^{(4)}/H''\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Pole-cancelled complements are the wrong object]
\label{rem:pole-cancelled-complements-wrong-object}
A pole-cancelled complement can evade the principal-part contradiction at the
cancelled pole.  But Bottleneck-C uses the source moments
\[
A_2=\frac{G''(m)}2,
\qquad
A_4=\frac{G^{(4)}(m)}{24}.
\]
An ODE for a pole-cancelled complement is therefore an ODE for the wrong
object, unless the entire order-seven row is rederived with different moments.
\end{remark}
```

---

# Edit 3 — Add full symmetry-packet non-cancellation remark

**Where:** In:

```latex
\subsection{Actual exterior-pair source jets and failure of pair-level locking}
\label{subsec:actual-exterior-pair-source-jets-no-locking}
```

insert immediately after the paragraph ending:

```latex
Any cancellation of the aggregate Bottleneck-C
coefficient must therefore be a genuine global zero-tail identity, not a
pair-level source rigidity law.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Full symmetry-packet closure does not cancel the source moments]
\label{rem:full-symmetry-packet-does-not-cancel-source-moments}
The paired atom \(f_{\beta,\gamma}\) already includes the
functional-equation partner at the same ordinate:
\[
\beta+i\gamma,
\qquad
1-\beta+i\gamma.
\]
The full symmetry packet also contains the conjugate ordinate pair
\[
\beta-i\gamma,
\qquad
1-\beta-i\gamma,
\]
whose paired contribution is
\[
f_{\beta,-\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t+\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t+\gamma)^2}.
\]
If
\[
x_+(m)=2m-\gamma,
\qquad
x_-(m)=2m+\gamma,
\]
then the corresponding post-affine coefficients are
\[
\rho_2(\beta,x_+),\quad \rho_4(\beta,x_+),
\qquad
\rho_2(\beta,x_-),\quad \rho_4(\beta,x_-).
\]
The formulas above are even in \(x\).  Thus at a symmetric midpoint
\(m=0\), the \(\gamma\) and \(-\gamma\) packets add:
\[
\rho_2(\beta,-\gamma)=\rho_2(\beta,\gamma),
\qquad
\rho_4(\beta,-\gamma)=\rho_4(\beta,\gamma).
\]
At the midpoint centered on the \(+\gamma\) packet, \(x_+=0\) while
\(x_-=2\gamma\); again the conjugate packet supplies an additional contribution
rather than a sign-reversed copy.  Therefore functional-equation and conjugation
closure do not structurally force
\[
A_2=0,
\qquad
A_4=0,
\qquad
\nu_{\eta\eta}=0.
\]
Any cancellation after summing the full packet is a proper analytic incidence
condition, not a symmetry identity.
\end{remark}
```

For the centered route, the direct skew \(N_7^{\off}\)-term projects to zero,

\[

Below is a handover for a new agent joining the RH proof attempt from the **current paper draft** and the latest multi-agent push.

---

# RH Proof Attempt — Current Handover

## 0. Mission

We are trying to prove RH by deriving a contradiction from the existence of an off-critical zero. The current draft is **not a completed proof**. It is a live architecture with several local mechanisms clarified and several repair routes ruled out.

The current surviving route is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{rank-two fixed-sector affine transport on a reduced visibility-positive base.}
}
\]

The old scalar Bottleneck-C route has failed unless one proves a new pointwise global zero-source identity. The current task is not to keep repairing scalar Bottleneck C. The current task is to make the rank-two transport architecture proof-closing.

---

# 1. Current top-level status

The active obstruction was originally a scalar/fixed-sector Bottleneck-C row:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=
-\frac{\nu_{\eta\eta}}{24\pi q^3}(wI+uS)
\in \mathfrak f_h.
\]

The crucial shift is:

\[
\boxed{
E_{\eta\eta}\text{ is no longer treated as a scalar defect to kill pointwise.}
}
\]

It is now treated as a **rank-two vector-valued affine forcing term** in:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
}
\]

This is a local geometric replacement for the failed scalar Bottleneck-C closure.

The main local story is now in the paper: reduced base, packet visibility, one-whitening-slot \(K_1\) visibility channel, rank-two connection, affine forcing, \(E_{\rm lower}\) ledger, and global affine transport dependency. 

---

# 2. What is closed, conditional, or open

## 2.1 Closed / accepted local findings

### A. Scalar Bottleneck-C repair routes are exhausted

The following have been audited and should not be re-run unless a genuinely new idea appears:

\[
\Phi_K\text{-scalar }T\text{-flatness},
\]

\[
\Theta_\pm\text{ numerator-coordinate / counterterm repairs},
\]

\[
\text{quotient-only determinant readout},
\]

\[
\text{split readout }(D,\lambda),
\]

\[
L=\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}\text{ line-bundle transport},
\]

\[
\text{endpoint symmetrization},
\]

\[
\text{source-convention rebuilds},
\]

\[
\text{exactness / residue / meromorphic ODE repairs}.
\]

The key local conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Any transform-faithful pointwise Bottleneck-C closure still sees the }S\text{-visible row.}
}
\]

So scalar closure would require the unproved pointwise identity:

\[
\boxed{
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}=0.
}
\]

This identity is **not** forced by one-pair source geometry, formal toy geometry, source splitting, endpoint symmetrization, exactness, residue calculus, or meromorphic ODE structure. 

---

### B. One-pair actual source jets have been computed

For the exterior functional-equation pair:

\[
f_{\beta,\gamma}(t)
=
\frac{1-\beta}{(1-\beta)^2+(2t-\gamma)^2}
+
\frac{\beta}{\beta^2+(2t-\gamma)^2},
\]

with

\[
a=1-\beta,\qquad b=\beta,\qquad x=2m-\gamma,
\]

the post-affine source coefficients are:

\[
\rho_2
=
4a\frac{3x^2-a^2}{(a^2+x^2)^3}
+
4b\frac{3x^2-b^2}{(b^2+x^2)^3},
\]

\[
\rho_4
=
16a\frac{a^4-10a^2x^2+5x^4}{(a^2+x^2)^5}
+
16b\frac{b^4-10b^2x^2+5x^4}{(b^2+x^2)^5}.
\]

These do **not** satisfy the Bottleneck-C locking law:

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{10q_0^2}{9}
-
\frac{5q_0''}{18q_0}.
\]

Far-tail asymptotic:

\[
\frac{\rho_4}{\rho_2}
=
\frac{20}{3x^2}+O(x^{-4}).
\]

This supports the negative result: local actual zeta source geometry does not automatically kill the bad row.

---

### C. Source-convention rebuild does not solve Bottleneck C

The cleanest rebuilt convention is:

\[
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R},
\qquad
q_{\base}^{\new}=q_{\core}+B_{\bg}+E_{\est,R}.
\]

But the obstruction reappears as:

\[
\nu_{21,7}^{\new,\mathrm{agg}}
=
\frac{1}{Q^{14}}
\left[
\frac{q_0^{\new}}{240}A_2^{\new}A_4^{\new}
+
\frac{1}{144}
\left(
\frac{(q_0^{\new})''}{6}
-
\frac{2(q_0^{\new})^3}{3}
\right)
(A_2^{\new})^2
\right].
\]

So the rebuild only relocates the required identity to the full non-core zero complement. It does not prove it.

---

### D. Packet visibility is locally available at order 7

This is the biggest positive result from the latest push.

Initially, the raw centered off-diagonal \(N_7\) coefficient looked promising. But:

\[
N_7^{\off}=C_7J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
-1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\]

so after leading whitening,

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(X_0N_7^{\off}X_0)=0.
\]

Thus the raw \(N_7^{\off}\) term is **not** the witness.

The live centered channel is the one-whitening-slot term:

\[
T_7^{(1)}
=
X_{-,1}YX_{+,0}
+
X_{-,0}YX_{+,1},
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

At centered parity:

\[
X_{+,0}=X_{-,0}=X_0,
\qquad
X_{+,1}=-X_{-,1}.
\]

With

\[
X_0=pI+rD,
\qquad
X_{-,1}=BS,
\]

we get:

\[
\boxed{
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(T_7^{(1)})
=
-2yBr\,I.
}
\]

The factors are:

\[
B=
\frac{q''}
{4\pi\sqrt{gh}(\sqrt g+\sqrt h)},
\qquad
r=\frac12(g^{-1/2}-h^{-1/2}).
\]

For a centered off-line packet:

\[
q''=2A_2\ne0,
\]

and

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72}
\ne0.
\]

So the centered one-whitening-slot channel is nonzero outside:

\[
y=0,\qquad q''=0,\qquad g=h.
\]

The non-centered route is even cleaner. Since the draft treats \(m\) as a sample midpoint,

\[
t_\pm=m\pm \frac{s}{2},
\]

not necessarily the zero-packet center, one may take

\[
x_m=2m-\gamma\ne0.
\]

Then:

\[
q^{(7)}(m)
=
5160960(a^{-9}+b^{-9})x_m+O(x_m^3),
\]

so \(q^{(7)}(m)\ne0\) for nearby non-centered midpoints. This activates the septic \(K_1\)-transport channel.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Packet visibility is locally certified on }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\text{ modulo explicit incidence.}
}
\]

Do not confuse this with finite-core non-concentration. Visibility is non-identity, not a sampled lower bound.

---

## 2.2 Conditional local infrastructure

### A. Reduced base

The rank-two route runs on:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
=
\mathcal B\setminus \mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\core}.
\]

The canonical core is:

\[
\mathcal C_k(m)
=
\text{the unique symmetry-closed, same-scale \(k\)-packet nearest }m.
\]

The visibility-positive base is:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
=
\mathcal B_{\rm red}
\setminus
\mathcal E_{\rm invis}^{\core,7}.
\]

Typical visibility incidence includes:

\[
\{y=0\},
\qquad
\{q''=0\},
\qquad

\]

and for quotient isolation:

\[
\{v_5=0\}.
\]

For the non-centered route:

\[
\{q^{(7)}=0\},
\qquad
\{\Xi_{K_1}=0\}.
\]

Important: this is still conditional on a **reach/non-swallowing theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Every RH-relevant off-line packet must meet }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\text{ or lie in a controlled exceptional stratum.}
}
\]

That theorem is not fully proved.

---

### B. Rank-two bundle and connection

The rank-two fixed-sector bundle is:

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\qquad
\mathcal F_b=\mathfrak f_h(b)=\mathbf C I_b\oplus\mathbf C S_b.
\]

The candidate connection is:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
}
\]

In local frame \(E=(I,S)\):

\[
\nabla^{\mathfrak f}A
=
E(da+\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}a).
\]

If \(E=E^{\rm raw}W\), then:

\[
\Gamma^{\mathfrak f}
=
W^{-1}\Gamma^{\rm raw}W+W^{-1}dW.
\]

This is conditional on:

\[
\text{fixed core convention},
\]

\[
\text{stable reduced atlas},
\]

\[
GL_2\text{ fixed-sector transitions},
\]

\[
\text{functorial }\Pi_{\mathfrak f},
\]

\[
\text{fixed whitening branch}.
\]

Source/core transfers are **not** allowed inside the rank-two vector-bundle atlas because they may be affine:

\[
A_{2r+1,j}^{\mathfrak f}
=
G_{ij}^{-1}A_{2r+1,i}^{\mathfrak f}
+
B_{ij,2r+1}.
\]

A future affine-torsor formalism is possible, but not part of the current route.

---

The current local structural equation is:

\[
\boxed{
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=

}
\]

where:

\[
E_{\eta\eta}
=

The \(E_{\rm lower}\) ledger is:

E_{\rm GateA}=0,
\qquad

under the accepted local Gate A/B hypotheses,

\[
E_{\rm conn}=0
\]

after covariantization,

E_{K_3}=0,
\qquad

\]

and

\[
E_{\rm line}\in\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

\(E_{\rm bg/core}\) is fixed analytic baseline forcing.

Remaining caveat: possible same-grade \(K_1\)-companions / cross-channel incidence. No second uncontrolled \(K_1\) source-Hessian row has been found.

The rank-two local equation gives, along a path:

\[
A(b)
=

+

The missing theorem must control:

=

No canonical path, endpoint condition, affine holonomy law, exactness theorem, projective index theorem, or transported finite-core lower bound is currently proved.

This is the main open gate.

# 3. What not to do

Do **not** spend another push on these unless there is a genuinely new idea:

1. Do not try to force \(\nu_{\eta\eta}=0\) locally.
2. Do not revive scalar \(T\)-flatness.
3. Do not revive quotient-only \(D_{2r+1}\) as proof-complete.
4. Do not use the split readout as if it removes the obstruction; it restores the full fixed-sector vector and the obstruction with it.
5. Do not treat line-bundle transport as proof-gate; it lacks global covariance/path/holonomy control.
6. Do not use the raw centered \(N_7^{\off}\) term as a visibility witness; it is skew and projected away.
7. Do not claim packet visibility proves finite-core non-concentration.
8. Do not claim rank-two connection proves RH; it is only local infrastructure.

---

# 4. What to attack next

## Push A — Local formalization / cleanup

The current paper is close to a stable local architecture. The next local push should close the formal loose ends.

### Agent 1 — Reduced good-patch reach

Prove or refine:

\[
\text{every RH-relevant off-line packet meets }\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\]

or else lies in a controlled exceptional stratum.

This includes:

\[
d_k<d_{k+1},
\]

same-scale bounds,

endpoint separation,

symmetry closure,

Gram nondegeneracy,

visibility incidence avoidance.

This is the “exceptional non-swallowing” theorem.

### Agent 2 — Bundle / atlas theorem

Prove:

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}\to\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+}
\]

is a canonical analytic rank-two bundle.

Check:

\[
E_j=E_iG_{ij},
\qquad
G_{ij}\in GL_2,
\qquad
G_{ij}G_{jk}=G_{ik}.
\]

Clarify exactly which transitions are allowed.

### Agent 3 — Connection theorem

Prove:

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A)
\]

is a connection and transforms correctly under \(GL_2\) atlas changes.

### Agent 4 — \(E_{\rm lower}\) full row table

Print and verify the full order-7 row table.

Every term must be classified as:

\[
\text{Gate A/B closed},
\]

\[
\text{connection absorbed},
\]

\[
\text{line},
\]

\[
\text{shadow},
\]

\[
\text{pure same-point},
\]

\[
\text{background/core},
\]

\[
\text{or }K_1\text{ companion/incidence}.
\]

### Agent 5 — \(K_1\) companion / cross-channel incidence

Prove no same-grade \(K_1\) companion cancels \(E_{\eta\eta}\) or the visibility channel identically. If it can happen, define the exact incidence wall.

### Agent 6 — Local synthesis

Decide whether the local rank-two architecture is fully theorem-ready:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\quad
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+},
\quad
\nabla^{\mathfrak f},
\quad
\nabla_\kappa A_7=E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}.
}
\]

Deliver “local closed / local conditional / local failed.”

## Push B — Global proof-gate search

Only after Push A, attack the true RH gate.

### Route 1 — Path/boundary

Find canonical \(a,b,\Gamma\) with endpoint constraints:

\[
A(a),\quad A(b).
\]

Currently missing.

### Route 2 — Affine holonomy

Find canonical loop \(\Gamma\) and show global zeta structure forces:

\[
\Delta_\Gamma^{\rm aff}=0
\]

or a prescribed value, while off-line zeros force the opposite.

Currently missing.

### Route 3 — Transported finite-core non-concentration

Define:

\[
C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}
=
(A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla A_7^{\mathfrak f},
A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\nabla A_9^{\mathfrak f},
\ldots).
\]

Prove:

\[
\theta(m)\notin
\mathcal Z_k^{\rm tr}\cup\mathcal E_{\rm geom}^{\rm tr}
\Longrightarrow
\|C_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}(\theta(m))\|_\infty
\ge
\Lambda_{\rm tr}(m,Q).
\]

This is currently the most plausible global route, but the aligned branch remains:

\[
J_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}\approx -P_{\rm fd}^{\rm tr}.
\]

Need a real coercivity/cone/incidence theorem.

### Route 4 — Projective-plus-scale index

Use:

\[
[A_7^{\mathfrak f}(m)]\in \mathbf P(\mathfrak f_h)
\]

plus scale/norm along \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\).

Pure projective data are insufficient because pure \(A_5\)-line anomalies are projectively invisible.

# 5. What remains to prove RH

The full remaining proof stack is:

## Theorem 1 — Reduced good-patch reach

Every nondegenerate off-line packet produces a point in:

\[
\mathcal B_{\rm red}^{+},
\]

or lies in controlled incidence.

## Theorem 2 — Rank-two bundle and connection

\[
\mathcal F_{\rm red}^{+}
\]

is a canonical analytic rank-two bundle with connection:

\[
\nabla_X^{\mathfrak f}A
=
\Pi_{\mathfrak f}(d_X^{\mathcal J}A).
\]

## Theorem 3 — Local affine forcing

\[
\nabla_\kappa^{\mathfrak f}A_7^{\mathfrak f}
=
E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower}
\]

with complete \(E_{\rm lower}\) classification.

## Theorem 4 — Global affine transport control

A theorem controlling:

\[
\int_\Gamma
U_{t\to b}
(E_{\eta\eta}+E_{\rm lower})(t)\,dt.
\]

This is the main missing theorem.

## Theorem 5 — RH contradiction

Show:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\Longrightarrow
\text{nonzero / forbidden affine transport or finite-core object},
\]

while global zeta structure forces the opposite.

This final theorem does not currently exist.
